# RunEcho Focus-Hunt Candidate Bugs — 2026-07-04 (severity-tagged 2026-07-05)

Multi-agent `/focus`-style logic-defect sweep over the top 30 risk-ranked files 
(by decision-branch density). Pipeline per file: contract extraction -> 3 independent 
logic lenses (caller<->callee mismatch, intent-vs-implementation, impossible/dead states) 
-> adversarial 3-verifier execution-based check (majority of 2/3 required to mark CONFIRMED).

## ⚠️ Read this before triaging

- **129 total candidates**, **110 marked CONFIRMED** by the automated verifier panel.
- That hit-rate is **higher than should be trusted at face value** — the three verifier votes per candidate are the same model family, each writing its own repro to match its own hypothesis. That is correlated, not independent, verification. Treat CONFIRMED as "worth a human look with a concrete repro attached," not "proven."
- **Severity is a heuristic, not agent judgment.** Added after the hunt completed, by keyword-matching each finding's existing `blastRadius` text (e.g. "PreToolUse hook entry point / every Edit-Write-MultiEdit" -> high; "zero functional callers / dead branch / never fires" -> low; everything else -> medium). No new agent calls were spent on this — it is a cheap, mechanical re-read of data already gathered, and should be spot-checked, not trusted blindly either.

**Severity breakdown:** 14 high, 79 medium, 12 low, 24 unknown (no blastRadius text captured — usually because the verify-agent for that candidate hit a rate limit before writing one; these need a human look to even assess reachability).

---

## 🔴 HIGH

### F1. `cmd/runecho-guard/dangling.go:398` — runHookMode
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** high (matched high-marker: "hook entry point")
- **Class:** impossible-state
- **Contract violated:** checkDanglingRefs's fail-open promise ('never a false block', 'any query error yields nil') implicitly assumes it actually gets invoked whenever a deletion happened; runHookMode's own comment at lines 386-393 explicitly says removedText is captured 'so a pure-deletion edit (empty new_string) still reaches the E1 dangling-refs check below' for Edit/MultiEdit.
- **Hypothesis:** Claude Code calls Write on an existing file with tool_input.content == "" (wiping the file to empty) while RUNECHO_GUARD_DANGLING=1. hookText("Write",...) returns content == "", and hookOldText("Write",...) always returns "" per its documented default case (Write is explicitly excluded, deferred to the later os.ReadFile branch at line 477-481). So at line 398, text == "" && removedText == "" is true even though this Write deletes every top-level definition in the file, and runHookMode returns 0 (decision 'defer', reason 'empty-input') before ever reaching the danglingEnabled() block at line 476 that would read the on-disk pre-edit file into oldText. deletedDefs/checkDanglingRefs are never called, so a wholesale-wipe of a file with real cross-file callers produces zero warning — the one case E1 exists to catch is exactly the case silently exempted, and this happens for every gated check (violations, dropped-import, duplicate too), not just E1.
- **Trace:** Input: PreToolUse JSON payload {"tool_name":"Write","tool_input":{"file_path":"<repo>/known.go","content":""}} with RUNECHO_GUARD_DANGLING=1, against a repo where known.go's sole definition DoThing is referenced by caller.go (real cross-file referrer).
Path: main.go:378 decode succeeds -> :384 text = hookText("Write","", "", nil) = "" (main.go:602 `case "Write": return content`) -> :395-396 removedText = hookOldText("Write", "", nil) = "" (dangling.go:59-61 default case, Write excluded) -> :398 filePath!="" but (text=="" && removedText=="") is true -> hookDefer(); logDecision({Decision:"defer",Reason:"empty-input"}); return 0. Execution never reaches :476 (danglingEnabled block), :479 os.ReadFile(filePath) for the pre-edit content, :485 deletedDefs, or :486 checkDanglingRefs.
Predicted wrong output: decision=defer, reason=empty-input, no ask, despite DoThing having a live cross-file caller.
Expected/correct output (per the fail-open CONTRACT and the line 386-393 comment's own stated intent): the E1 check should run against the pre-edit on-disk content and produce decision=ask, reason=dangling (as it does for the non-empty-replacement case).
- **Blast radius:** Single call site: cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:101 invokes runHookMode as the entire body of `--hook-mode`, which is the live Claude Code PreToolUse hook entry point (grep confirms no other production caller). Every repo with runecho-guard wired as a PreToolUse hook is affected: a Write that sets content=="" on an existing file bypasses all three gated deletion-side checks at once (E1 dangling-refs, dropped-import, E5 duplicate-symbol), not just E1 — they share the single line 476 gate.
- **Fix direction:** Move the removedText/oldText derivation (including the Write os.ReadFile branch) ahead of the line 398 early-return guard — or explicitly special-case Write with an existing non-empty on-disk file as "not empty input" — so a full-file wipe still reaches the danglingEnabled()/droppedImportEnabled()/duplicateEnabled() block before the empty-input defer can short-circuit it.

### F2. `cmd/runecho-guard/learnedallow.go:118` — recordApprovals
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** high (matched high-marker: "every (edit|write|multiedit|hook)")
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** recordApprovals' only consumer, learnedAllowedSet, is merged exclusively into the hallucination/unresolved-reference known-set (main.go:453-459, immediately feeding guard.Run at main.go:466). recordApprovals implicitly assumes every symbol name it is asked to trust is a 'this name legitimately resolves, stop flagging references to it as hallucinated' signal. The caller (declog.go:118, forwarding ask.Symbols built in main.go:520-552) violates that assumption by feeding it symbol names drawn from dangling-reference warnings, dropped-import warnings, and duplicate-definition warnings -- none of which mean 'this is a real, resolvable symbol name that should be exempted from hallucination detection.'
- **Hypothesis:** An edit deletes function oldHelper() from file A while file B still calls oldHelper() (RUNECHO_GUARD_DANGLING=1, no violations present) -> main.go logs an ask with Symbols=["oldHelper"] purely from the dangling category. The user approves twice within the TTL (default threshold=2) -> learnedAllowedSet(dir, repo, now) starts returning "oldHelper". main.go:453-459 merges it into `symbols`, the known-set passed to guard.Run. A later, unrelated edit writes a genuinely hallucinated call to oldHelper() (a name that exists nowhere in the codebase, since it was deleted and never redefined) -> guard.Run treats "oldHelper" as known and reports zero violations, so the guard silently passes a real hallucination it was designed to catch. Separately, the header comment's promise that approving trains 'the guard to stop asking about them' is unmet for this same case: checkDanglingRefs (main.go:484-488) never consults learnedAllowedSet, so the next unrelated deletion of a function also named oldHelper still re-triggers the dangling ask -- the learned trust neither suppresses the check it was earned from nor is scoped to the check it actually affects.
- **Trace:** Concrete input: repo "r", known.go defines DoThing(), caller.go references DoThing() (SNAP1).
1. Edit deletes `func DoThing() {}` from known.go with RUNECHO_GUARD_DANGLING=1 → main.go:484-488 calls checkDanglingRefs → dangling.go:148-172 returns danglingWarning{Symbol:"DoThing"} (caller.go still refs it) → main.go:528-533 appends "DoThing" to `syms` → hookAsk + logDecision(Symbols:["DoThing"], Reason:"dangling") (main.go:551-552).
2. User approves twice → declog.go:118 logOutcomeForFile → recordApprovals(dir,"r",["DoThing"],now) twice → learnedallow.go:154-162 increments bucket["DoThing"].Count to 2 (== learnedThresholdDefault).
3. Repo reindexed to SNAP2, where DoThing exists nowhere (post-deletion reality; symbol table now only has "Unrelated").
4. New file evil.go: `func F() { DoThing() }` (genuine hallucination — no definition anywhere) → lookupSymbolsFor returns symbols from SNAP2 (no DoThing) → main.go:453-459: learnEnabled()==true → learnedAllowedSet(dir,"r",now) returns {"DoThing"} (count>=2, within TTL) → merged into `symbols` → guard.Run(symbols,...) treats DoThing as known → violations=[] → hook defers (no ask).
Predicted wrong output: PermissionDec == "" (deferred, no ask) for a call to a symbol that exists nowhere in the codebase.
Expected right output: PermissionDec == "ask" (violation flagged), as demonstrated by the control run with RUNECHO_GUARD_LEARN unset against the identical SNAP2/evil.go state.
- **Blast radius:** recordApprovals has exactly one caller (declog.go:118 logOutcomeForFile, fired from PostToolUse on every approved edit). learnedAllowedSet has exactly one caller (main.go:453-459, feeding guard.Run at main.go:466, the sole hallucination-detection gate for every Edit/Write/MultiEdit hook invocation across Go/JS/TS/Python/.gs). Any repo running with RUNECHO_GUARD_LEARN=1 plus any of RUNECHO_GUARD_DANGLING=1, dropped-import checking, or duplicate-def checking is affected — a single approved dangling/dropped-import/duplicate ask permanently (until TTL, default 14 days) blinds the primary hallucination check for that exact symbol name.
- **Fix direction:** Tag each symbol in the ask/outcome record with its origin category (violation vs dangling vs dropped-import vs duplicate) and have recordApprovals/learnedAllowedSet only accept-and-feed-forward symbols whose origin was an actual `violations` (hallucination) ask — do not let dangling/dropped-import/duplicate approvals populate the hallucination known-set at all.

### F3. `cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:398` — runHookMode
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** high (matched high-marker: "every (edit|write|multiedit|hook)")
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** runHookMode's own documented invariant (contract for runHookMode, and the inline comment at dangling.go's hookOldText / main.go:386-393): 'the pure-deletion early-return at 398 only short-circuits checks that structurally cannot fire on empty new text.' This is false for the E1 dangling-refs and dropped-import checks when the tool is Write.
- **Hypothesis:** Claude Code issues a Write tool call for an EXISTING file foo.py (which currently defines `bar`, referenced from other files) with tool_input.content = "" (clearing the file). hookText("Write", _, "", _) returns "" so text=="". removedText is computed via hookOldText("Write", oldString, edits) at line 396, but hookOldText's switch (cmd/runecho-guard/dangling.go:47-62) only special-cases "Edit" and "MultiEdit" — the Write branch falls through to `default: return ""`, i.e. removedText is ALWAYS "" for a Write regardless of what is actually being deleted from disk. So at line 398, `text == "" && removedText == ""` is true, and runHookMode takes the 'empty-input' hookDefer() path at line 399-401 and returns immediately — before ever reaching the block at lines 477-482 that reads the pre-edit on-disk file into oldText for exactly this scenario. With RUNECHO_GUARD_DANGLING=1 set, deletedDefs/checkDanglingRefs is therefore never invoked for a Write that empties an existing file, so the ask ('symbol being removed is still referenced elsewhere') never fires and the deletion of `bar` (and every other top-level symbol in the file) silently passes through with no warning — exactly the cross-file-breaking deletion E1 exists to catch. The same starvation applies to droppedImportEnabled() for a Write that empties a file still importing names used nowhere in the new (empty) text trivially, but more importantly for any Write whose new content is empty while the old imports were load-bearing elsewhere is moot; the real failure is E1. E5/duplicateEnabled() is NOT affected the same way (addedDefs on an empty new text correctly yields no new defs, so no false negative there) — but E1 is a genuine dead branch for the Write tool's full-file-deletion case, contradicting the code's own stated invariant that the early return 'only short-circuits checks that structurally cannot fire on empty new text.'
- **Trace:** Input: PreToolUse payload {"tool_name":"Write","tool_input":{"file_path":"<repo>/known.go","content":""}} where known.go on disk currently contains `package p\nfunc DoThing() {}\n`, DoThing is indexed in the store as defined in known.go and referenced from caller.go, and RUNECHO_GUARD_DANGLING=1.
Path: main.go:384 text=hookText("Write","","","",nil)="" -> main.go:395-396 removedText=hookOldText("Write","",nil) hits the `default:` branch in dangling.go:59-61 -> "" -> main.go:398 `filePath=="" (false) || (text=="" && removedText=="")` = true -> main.go:399-401 hookDefer(); logDecision(Reason:"empty-input"); return 0. Lines 417 (lookupSymbolsFor), 476-509 (oldText read from disk, deletedDefs, checkDanglingRefs) are never reached.
Predicted wrong output: decision-log reason == "empty-input", hook permission decision NOT "ask" (silently defers) even though DoThing is deleted and still referenced by caller.go.
Expected/correct output: decision-log reason == "dangling", hook permission decision == "ask", message naming DoThing and caller.go (as in the sibling case TestDangling_WriteDropsReferencedDef_Asks, which uses non-empty replacement content and correctly asks).
- **Blast radius:** Single call site: main.go:101 `return runHookMode(...)` — this is the entire PreToolUse hook entry point for runecho-guard, invoked on every Write/Edit/MultiEdit tool call in any enrolled repo. Every Write that fully empties an existing file (a full-file rewrite-to-empty, or a tool that emits empty content for a delete-equivalent) silently bypasses both E1 dangling-refs (RUNECHO_GUARD_DANGLING=1) and dropped-import (RUNECHO_GUARD_DROPPED_IMPORT=1) checks, with no other caller path to compensate.
- **Fix direction:** At main.go:398, don't let removedText's Write-side "" stand in for "nothing to check" — either compute a Write-specific hasOldContent signal (e.g. check `payload.ToolName == "Write"` and stat/peek the on-disk file for non-emptiness before the early return) or move the on-disk-read block (476-482) above the line-398 guard so Write's real pre-edit text is known before deciding to defer.

### F4. `cmd/runecho-ir/main.go:90` — run
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** high (matched high-marker: "sole (hallucination|entry)")
- **Class:** unhandled-postcondition
- **Contract violated:** run() should report a clear error for an unrecognized os.Args[1] (per the doc comment's fixed list of subcommands at lines 23-32), the same way it already does for unrecognized flag-like arguments.
- **Hypothesis:** os.Args = ["runecho-ir", "shapshot"] (typo of "snapshot") -> intent: print an 'unknown subcommand' error and return ExitError (2), matching the existing handling for unrecognized "-"-prefixed args at line 91-95. Actual: the switch's default case only guards the case where os.Args[1] starts with "-" (line 91); for "shapshot", that guard is false, the if-body is skipped, and control silently falls through to line 99's return runIndex(os.Args), reinterpreting the typo'd subcommand as a root directory path. This produces a confusing downstream failure (e.g. a 'not a directory'/index-parse error) instead of the clear 'unknown subcommand' message the surrounding code's own pattern (the -prefix branch) implies should exist for all unrecognized os.Args[1] values.
- **Trace:** Input: os.Args = ["runecho-ir", "shapshot"], cwd = empty temp dir (no "shapshot" subdir).
main.go:57 run() -> line 58 len(os.Args)>1 true -> line 59 switch os.Args[1] ("shapshot") -> none of the named cases match ("snapshot" != "shapshot") -> default case, line 91 strings.HasPrefix("shapshot","-") = false -> if-body skipped -> falls through switch -> line 99 `return runIndex(os.Args)`.
capture.go:134 runIndex(["runecho-ir","shapshot"]) -> line 136 rootPath="." -> line 137 len(args)>1 true, args[1]="shapshot" -> line 137 strings.HasPrefix("shapshot","-")=false -> line 142 rootPath="shapshot" -> line 145 absRoot=filepath.Abs("shapshot") succeeds (just joins cwd, no existence check) -> line 153-155 generateIR(generator, absRoot) is called on a nonexistent directory.
Predicted wrong output (per hypothesis): a confusing downstream "not a directory"/index-parse ExitError(2).
Actual observed output: even more silent than hypothesized — generateIR treats the nonexistent path as an empty tree, printing a soft "Warning: failed to access .../shapshot: lstat ...: no such file or directory" to stderr, then completing "successfully" with `Indexed 0 files — root_hash: e3b0c44...` and exit code 0 (ExitOK).
Expected/correct output (per doc comment's fixed subcommand list, matching the existing "-"-prefixed unknown-flag path): `runecho-ir: unknown subcommand "shapshot"` + usage + ExitError(2).
- **Blast radius:** run() is called only from main() (cmd/runecho-ir/main.go:34) — it is the CLI's sole entry point. Every invocation of the runecho-ir binary with a misspelled or unrecognized bare-word subcommand (e.g. "shapshot"/"snapshot", "dif"/"diff", "vrify"/"verify", "chrun"/"churn", etc., across all 12 documented subcommands) hits this path and silently misbehaves instead of erroring clearly.
- **Fix direction:** In run()'s default case (main.go line 91), drop the `strings.HasPrefix(os.Args[1], "-")` guard (or add an else branch) so ANY unrecognized os.Args[1] — flag-like or not — prints "unknown subcommand %q" + usage and returns ExitError, before falling through to runIndex; reserve the runIndex fallback only for when os.Args[1] is a valid-looking path or when running with no args beyond a root path is the documented default (may need a separate flag/sentinel, e.g. only fall through when os.Args[1] resolves to an existing directory, to preserve `runecho-ir /some/real/path` backward compat).

### F5. `cmd/runecho-ir/mapcmd.go:92` — runMap
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** high (matched high-marker: "every session")
- **Class:** unhandled-postcondition
- **Contract violated:** runMap's own contract flags 'buildIR's second return value is discarded (`_`) even though a similarly-shaped call pattern elsewhere in the codebase treats that value meaningfully — worth confirming it is genuinely unused'; capture.go's runIndex treats it as meaningful via coverageSuffix(stats).
- **Hypothesis:** For a repo enrolled with FileCap=500 (repoFileCap returns >0 per helpers.go:76-82) where the workspace has 700 supported files, or one that hits GeneratorConfig.GenerateTimeout mid-walk, buildIR (capture.go:107) returns an ir.Stats with SupportedSeen=700, Indexed=500 — but runMap discards it at line 92 (`irData, _, irCode := buildIR(...)`). Neither the normal map listing nor emitMapHeader (which independently recomputes only funcs/classes/dirFiles counts from irData.Files at lines 211-227) ever calls coverageSuffix or otherwise reports the shortfall, so `runecho-ir map --header` prints '500 files, N functions, M classes' with no indication that 200 files (28%) were silently never indexed — unlike `runecho-ir index`, which would print 'coverage=500/700 (71%)' for the identical partial walk.
- **Trace:** Input: a directory with 10 supported (.go) files, each containing one function, and FileCap=4 (as repoFileCap would return for an enrolled repo with FileCap=4, or as GenerateTimeout could produce mid-walk).
Path: runMap (mapcmd.go:92) → buildIR(root, 4) (capture.go:107) → generateIR → generator.Generate (internal/ir/generator.go): walk sets stats.SupportedSeen=10 (all 10 supported files encountered), stops indexing after FileCap=4, stats.Indexed=4 (== len(result.Files)). runMap: `irData, _, irCode := buildIR(...)` — the ir.Stats{SupportedSeen:10, Indexed:4} value is discarded via `_`. --header path → emitMapHeader(irData) (mapcmd.go ~200-227), which recomputes only funcs/classes/dirFiles from irData.Files (len=4) — it has no reference to Stats at all.
Predicted wrong output: `runecho-ir map --header` prints "runecho map: 4 files, 4 functions, 0 classes." with zero indication that 6 of the 10 supported files (60%) were never indexed.
Expected/contrasting output: runIndex, given the identical Stats, would print "Indexed 4 files ... coverage=4/10 (40%)" via coverageSuffix(stats).
- **Blast radius:** runMap is invoked from exactly one call site: main.go:65 (`runecho-ir map` subcommand dispatch). Both its output modes are affected: (1) `--header`, documented in-code as intended for injection into a Claude Code SessionStart hook — meaning every session-start summary from an enrolled repo with a FileCap or slow generate can silently misstate repo completeness to the agent; (2) the plain/`--by-file`/`--json` symbol listing, which likewise gives no hint that up to `SupportedSeen - Indexed` files are entirely absent from the map, unlike `runecho-ir index`/`repo add` output which always shows coverage via coverageSuffix.
- **Fix direction:** Capture the discarded stats (`irData, stats, irCode := buildIR(...)`) in runMap and append coverageSuffix(stats) to the --header summary line (and optionally to the plain-map footer) whenever stats.SupportedSeen > stats.Indexed, mirroring runIndex's existing pattern.

### F6. `internal/guard/dropped_import.go:209` — locallyBoundNames
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** high (matched high-marker: "adoption-killer")
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** postconditions: 'Returns the set of identifiers that appear in any recognized binding-target position... JS: ...function/arrow params...' and DroppedImportRefs's false-positive guard doc: 'A dropped import whose name is rebound here is NOT a bug'
- **Hypothesis:** For oldText 'import { x } from \'./lib\';\nconsole.log(x);\n' and newText 'const list = [1, 2, 3];\nconst doubled = list.map(x => x * 2);\n', reJSArrowParams (`\(([^)]*)\)\s*=>`) requires parentheses around the arrow parameter and never matches the valid, common unparenthesized single-arg arrow form `x => x * 2`. locallyBoundNames therefore never adds "x" to `bound`, DroppedImportRefs treats "x" as still using the removed import, and DroppedImportRefs(LangJS, oldText, newText) returns [{Name:x, LineNo:2}] — a false-positive dropped-import finding on code where "x" is actually a fresh, correctly-scoped arrow-function parameter with no relation to the deleted import. Verified by direct execution: DroppedImportRefs returns exactly that non-empty result.
- **Trace:** Input: oldText = "import { x } from './lib';\nconsole.log(x);\n", newText = "const list = [1, 2, 3];\nconst doubled = list.map(x => x * 2);\n", lang = LangJS.

DroppedImportRefs (dropped_import.go:32):
- oldImps = {"x"} (from ExtractImports on oldText).
- newImps = {} (no import statements in newText).
- bound := locallyBoundNames(LangJS, newText) (line 50) → traced below, yields {"const","doubled","list"} — "x" absent.
- ExtractDefs adds nothing further for "x".
- Loop at line 58: name="x" — not in newImps, not in bound → dropped = ["x"].
- uses := firstUnqualifiedUseLines(...) finds "x" used unqualified at line 2 (`list.map(x => x * 2)`) since it's not preceded by '.' and not on an import line.
- out = [{Name:"x", LineNo:2}] → returned.

locallyBoundNames (dropped_import.go:167) walk of added line 2 "const doubled = list.map(x => x * 2);":
- General assignLHS(s) (line 176) finds the first plain '=' — the one after "doubled" — returns "const doubled " → add() extracts idents "const","doubled". Stops here; never reaches the arrow's internal tokens because assignLHS returns on the FIRST '=' it finds.
- LangJS branch: reJSDeclList matches, decl = "doubled = list.map(x => x * 2);"; assignLHS(decl) again returns "doubled " (non-empty) → add("doubled") only; the else branch (which would add the raw decl string) is skipped since lhs != "".
- reJSFnParams (`function\b[^(]*\(([^)]*)\)`) — no `function` keyword present → no match.
- reJSArrowParams (`\(([^)]*)\)\s*=>`) — requires a `(...)` immediately followed by `=>`. In "list.map(x => x * 2)" the only `(`...`)` pair spans "(x => x * 2)" (no `)` until the very end), and what follows that closing `)` is `;`, not `=>` — so the regex does not match anywhere on this line. The unparenthesized single-arg arrow `x => x * 2` is never captured.
- reJSForDecl, reJSCatch — no match.

Result: "x" never enters `bound`. Predicted wrong output = [{Name:"x", LineNo:2}] non-empty (false positive on a fresh, correctly-scoped arrow parameter). Expected/correct output = nil (no dropped-import finding, since "x" is a rebound arrow parameter unrelated to the deleted import).
- **Blast radius:** DroppedImportRefs is called from exactly one production call site: cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:493 (`droppedImps = guard.DroppedImportRefs(lang, oldText, text)`), which is runecho-guard's PreToolUse hook path that flags/blocks Edit/MultiEdit on JS/TS files. Every JS/TS edit where a dropped import's name coincides with an unparenthesized single-arg arrow parameter (a very common idiom: `.map(x => ...)`, `.filter(item => ...)`, `.then(res => ...)`, etc.) will trigger this false positive, undermining the guard's stated precision-over-recall design goal (comment at dropped_import.go:45-49 explicitly calls false alarms "the adoption-killer").
- **Fix direction:** Extend reJSArrowParams to also match the unparenthesized single-identifier arrow form, e.g. `regexp.MustCompile(`(?:\(([^)]*)\)|\b([A-Za-z_$][\w$]*))\s*=>`)`, and in locallyBoundNames add whichever of the two capture groups matched (mm[1] or mm[2]).

### F7. `internal/guard/dropped_import.go:493` — DroppedImportRefs
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** high (matched high-marker: "every (edit|write|multiedit|hook)")
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** Callee precondition: "oldText, newText describe the same file's content before/after a single edit"; callee postcondition computes `bound` (locallyBoundNames + ExtractDefs) over newText under the doc-comment assumption that newText is "the new text" that "re-provides locally" every rebinding of a dropped name — i.e. it assumes newText represents the whole file's post-edit content, not an arbitrary sub-slice of it.
- **Hypothesis:** cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:493 calls guard.DroppedImportRefs(lang, oldText, text) where, for Edit/MultiEdit (payload.ToolName != "Write"), oldText/text come from hookOldText/hookText (main.go:384,396 + dangling.go:47) and are the TOUCHED HUNK'S old_string/new_string only, not the whole file. Given a Python file where `re` is imported at the top but also re-bound locally inside a function untouched by the edit (e.g. `re = load_custom_re()` on a line the edit never touches), and a MultiEdit that (a) drops the top-level `import re` line via one sub-edit with new_string="" and (b) in an unrelated sub-edit changes an unrelated line to `return re.match(text)`, DroppedImportRefs is called with oldText="import re\n\n    return process2(text)\n" and newText="    return re.match(text)\n" (the local rebinding line is absent from both, since it is outside every touched hunk). `bound := locallyBoundNames(lang, newText)` then never sees the real rebinding of `re`, so `re` is wrongly classified as dropped-and-unbound and DroppedImportRefs returns [{Name:"re", LineNo:1}], causing runecho-guard to ask/warn "import re removed by this edit is still used below — likely a dropped import" on an edit that is actually safe (the local rebinding elsewhere in the file, not visible to the callee because the caller passed hunk-scoped text instead of whole-file text, still resolves `re` at runtime). This is a false positive the sibling hallucination check in the same function avoids via `addInFileDefs(symbols, filePath, lang)` (main.go:448), which folds in the on-disk file's definitions before running guard.Run — no equivalent whole-file fold-in exists for the `bound` set consumed by DroppedImportRefs.
- **Trace:** Simulated MultiEdit inputs exactly as main.go constructs them:
- edit1: OldString="import re\n", NewString="" (drops the import)
- edit2: OldString="    return process2(text)", NewString="    return re.match(text)\n" (unrelated line, now uses re)
- The file ALSO has an untouched line elsewhere, e.g. `re = load_custom_re()`, which never appears in either hunk.

hookOldText (MultiEdit case, dangling.go:52-58) joins non-empty OldStrings with "\n":
  oldText = "import re\n" + "\n" + "    return process2(text)"
hookText (MultiEdit case, main.go:604-610) joins non-empty NewStrings with "\n" (edit1's empty NewString is skipped):
  newText = "    return re.match(text)\n"

Call path: main.go:493 guard.DroppedImportRefs(LangPython, oldText, newText)
  -> dropped_import.go:36 oldImps = {"re"} (from oldText's `import re`)
  -> dropped_import.go:40 newImps = {} (no import line in newText)
  -> dropped_import.go:50 bound = locallyBoundNames(Python, newText) — newText has no assignment/for/as/walrus binding of `re` (only `re.match(text)` which is a qualified use, not a binding) -> bound = {} (plus ExtractDefs adds nothing)
  -> dropped_import.go:60-68: "re" in oldImps, not in newImps, not in bound -> dropped = ["re"]
  -> dropped_import.go:76-82: firstUnqualifiedUseLines finds `re` used unqualified on line 1 of newText -> out = [{Name:"re", LineNo:1}]

Predicted wrong output: []DroppedImport{{Name:"re", LineNo:1}} (false positive — `re` is actually safely rebound by the untouched `re = load_custom_re()` line elsewhere in the file, which the hunk-scoped newText never shows the guard).
- **Blast radius:** Sole caller of guard.DroppedImportRefs in production code is cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:493, inside runHookMode, gated by droppedImportEnabled() (E1-family dropped-import check). Every Edit/MultiEdit PreToolUse hook invocation with that feature enabled goes through this path — grep confirms no other call site exists (all other DroppedImportRefs references are in internal/guard/dropped_import_test.go, the unit tests, or doc comments). Impact: false "dropped import still used" warnings/asks on any MultiEdit where a name is genuinely rebound outside the touched hunks — directly undermines the guard's stated "precision over recall" design goal (dropped_import.go:49) and trains users to distrust/ignore it, the exact adoption-killer the code's own comment warns against.
- **Fix direction:** Give the dropped-import check access to the whole on-disk pre/post file content (the same wholeFileText helper already used by the E5 duplicate-def check, main.go:502-507) so locallyBoundNames/ExtractDefs scan the full file instead of only the hunk-joined newText, eliminating the blind spot for rebindings outside the touched hunks.

### F8. `internal/guard/dropped_import.go:848` — isImportLine
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** high (matched high-marker: "silently (bypass|suppress|skip|defeat)")
- **Class:** impossible-state
- **Contract violated:** firstUnqualifiedUseLines's postcondition that 'a line classified as an import line' contributes no identifier uses (dropped_import.go:118-120) implicitly assumes an import statement occupies the entire physical line — but Python/JS both allow a real statement to be semicolon-chained after an import on the same line, a state the regex/prefix checks don't rule out.
- **Hypothesis:** newText contains the single physical line `import re; x = SomeDroppedImport()` (Python) where `SomeDroppedImport` was removed from its own import elsewhere in the same edit and this is its only unqualified use in newText. rePyImport (`^\s*import\s+(.+?)\s*$`) matches the WHOLE line (verified: FindStringSubmatch returns the full remainder `re; x = SomeDroppedImport()` as group 1), so isImportLine returns true for the entire line, and firstUnqualifiedUseLines' loop `continue`s past it without scanning any identifiers on it. `uses["SomeDroppedImport"]` is therefore never set (stays 0), so DroppedImportRefs' `if ln := uses[name]; ln > 0` check at line 79 excludes it from `out`, and the function returns nil — silently missing exactly the dropped-import bug it exists to catch. The same false-negative occurs for JS via the `strings.HasPrefix(t, "import ")` check at line 854, e.g. `import { z } from './m'; foo(DroppedName());`.
- **Trace:** Input: oldText = "from mymod import SomeDroppedImport\nSomeDroppedImport()\n"; newText = "import re; x = SomeDroppedImport()\n" (lang=LangPython).

Path: DroppedImportRefs (dropped_import.go:32) computes oldImps={SomeDroppedImport}, newImps={} (rePyImport captures "re" as the imported name from "import re; x = SomeDroppedImport()" — but that's irrelevant to the bug), bound=locallyBoundNames(newText) (empty, no rebinding) -> dropped=["SomeDroppedImport"] (line 60-68). Then uses := firstUnqualifiedUseLines(LangPython, TextToAddedLines(newText)) (line 76) walks the single physical line "import re; x = SomeDroppedImport()". At dropped_import.go:118, isImportLine(LangPython, "import re; x = SomeDroppedImport()") is called, which at extract.go:851 evaluates rePyImport.MatchString(text) where rePyImport = `^\s*import\s+(.+?)\s*$` (extract.go:186). Because the pattern is anchored ^...$ with no multiline flag, `$` matches end-of-string, forcing the lazy `(.+?)` to expand across the whole line ("re; x = SomeDroppedImport()") to satisfy the anchor — so MatchString returns true for the ENTIRE line, not just the "import re" prefix. isImportLine returns true -> firstUnqualifiedUseLines `continue`s (line 119), never scanning "SomeDroppedImport" as an identifier on that line. Result: uses map is empty (uses["SomeDroppedImport"] == 0). Back in DroppedImportRefs line 79, `if ln := uses[name]; ln > 0` is false for "SomeDroppedImport", so it is excluded from `out`. DroppedImportRefs returns nil.

Predicted wrong output: DroppedImportRefs returns nil/empty (misses the dropped import).
Expected correct output: DroppedImportRefs should return [{Name:"SomeDroppedImport", LineNo:1}] since the import was removed and the name is still used unqualified in newText.
- **Blast radius:** Single call site: cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:493 invokes guard.DroppedImportRefs(lang, oldText, text) as part of the runecho-guard PreToolUse hook's dropped-import check for Python/JS edits. Any edit that semicolon-chains a real statement after `import ...`/`from ... import ...` (Python) or after `import ... from '...'`/`require(...)` (JS, via the `strings.HasPrefix(t, "import ")` check at extract.go:854) on the same physical line, where the chained statement is the only unqualified use of a name whose import was dropped elsewhere in the diff, silently defeats this guard — exactly the dropped-import runtime bug (NameError / ReferenceError) the check exists to catch.</blastRadius>
<parameter name="fixDirection">In isImportLine, only treat the import-syntax prefix of the line as "import" and let firstUnqualifiedUseLines still scan any trailing statement after a top-level `;` (Python/JS both allow statement-separator semicolons) — e.g. split-and-check just the first `;`-delimited segment against the import regexes/prefix checks instead of matching/prefix-testing the whole line.</fixDirection>
</invoke>


### F9. `internal/guard/extract.go:175` — stripLiterals / stripLiteralsStateful
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** high (matched high-marker: "guard.?s core")
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** stripLiteralsStateful's precondition requires the caller to thread `open` across successive lines of the same contiguous text so multi-line constructs (Python triple-quoted strings, JS/Go backtick template literals) are correctly recognized as literal content on their continuation lines; stripLiterals (extract.go:541) is documented as a single-line-only wrapper that always passes open="" and discards the returned open token, explicitly 'for callers ... that work one line at a time' (extract.go:538-540).
- **Hypothesis:** internal/guard/dropped_import.go:174-175 (locallyBoundNames) iterates every line of a whole multi-line newText via `for _, l := range TextToAddedLines(text) { s := stripLiterals(lang, l.Text) ... }`, i.e. it needs multi-line-aware stripping (the same class of caller ExtractRefs/ExtractImports are for) but calls the non-stateful single-line wrapper instead of stripLiteralsStateful with threaded `open`. Concrete failure: given newText containing a Python docstring `"""\nULID = 5\n"""` where `ULID` was the dropped import and is genuinely used elsewhere as `ULID()`, line 2 `ULID = 5` is scanned fresh with open="" (unaware it's inside the still-open triple-quote from line 1), so assignLHS matches it and locallyBoundNames incorrectly adds `ULID` to `bound`. DroppedImportRefs (dropped_import.go:64-66) then sees `bound["ULID"]` is populated and silently suppresses a real dropped-import bug it should have reported — a false negative in the guard's core detection path caused directly by using the wrong (stateless) variant of the callee.
- **Trace:** Input oldText: `from ulid import ULID\nx = ULID()\n`; newText: `"""\nULID = 5\n"""\nx = ULID()\n` (import dropped, docstring spans lines 1-3, real use ULID() on line 4).

Path: DroppedImportRefs(LangPython, oldText, newText) [dropped_import.go:32]
  -> oldImps = {ULID} (from ExtractImports on oldText)
  -> newImps = {} (import gone in newText)
  -> bound = locallyBoundNames(LangPython, newText) [dropped_import.go:171]
       for each line of TextToAddedLines(newText):
         line1 `"""`          -> s := stripLiterals(lang, l.Text) [line 175] called with open="" every time (stateless) -> s = `"""` unchanged (no assign match)
         line2 `ULID = 5`     -> stripLiterals(lang, "ULID = 5") with open="" (WRONG: should be aware triple-quote from line1 is still open) -> returns "ULID = 5" verbatim (nothing to strip since it doesn't recognize it's inside a string) -> assignLHS("ULID = 5") = "ULID" -> add("ULID") -> bound["ULID"] = {}
         line3 `"""`, line4 `x = ULID()` -> irrelevant
  -> ExtractDefs adds nothing further
  -> dropped loop: name="ULID", still=false (not in newImps), b=true (bound["ULID"] exists) -> `continue` -> ULID is NOT added to `dropped`
  -> dropped == [] -> DroppedImportRefs returns nil

Predicted wrong output: DroppedImportRefs returns [] (no dropped-import reported), despite ULID being a genuinely dropped import still used unqualified via ULID() on line 4.
Expected correct output: [{Name: "ULID", LineNo: 4}] (or similar), since stripLiteralsStateful with correctly threaded `open` would recognize line 2 as still inside the open triple-quote, blank it, and assignLHS would never see "ULID = 5" as code.
- **Blast radius:** grep shows DroppedImportRefs has exactly one production caller: cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:493 (`droppedImps = guard.DroppedImportRefs(lang, oldText, text)`), i.e. the runecho-guard CLI's dropped-import check for Python/JS edits. Any edit that introduces or preserves a multi-line string/docstring (or JS/Go-lang-adjacent backtick template, for JS) spanning a line that looks like a rebinding of the dropped name will silently suppress a real dropped-import finding for that name in that edit — a false negative in the guard's core safety check, not a crash.
- **Fix direction:** In locallyBoundNames, thread `open` across TextToAddedLines the same way firstUnqualifiedUseLines does: replace the stateless `stripLiterals(lang, l.Text)` call at dropped_import.go:175 with a stateful loop calling stripLiteralsStateful(lang, l.Text, open) and carrying `open` forward (resetting on a LineNo gap), instead of always passing open="".

### F10. `internal/guard/extract.go:342` — ExtractRefs
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** high (matched high-marker: "silently (bypass|suppress|skip|defeat)")
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** reCallIdent is documented/relied upon (see ExtractRefs postcondition, '[A-Za-z_$] start class guarantees name is non-empty') as matching call-identifiers that may legitimately start with '$' (JS/AngularJS/jQuery convention). The regex `\b([A-Za-z_$][\w$]*)\s*\(` assumes \b treats '$' as a word character the same way it treats letters/underscore, but Go's RE2 \w (and therefore \b) does NOT include '$' — '$' is non-word for boundary purposes even though it IS accepted inside the character class.
- **Hypothesis:** For an added JS line `x = $http(config);`, the intent is to extract the call target "$http" (or at minimum treat it as a bare call worth validating). Because \b requires a word/non-word transition and '$' is classified as non-word, the match cannot start at '$' when preceded by whitespace/start-of-line/any non-word char — the regex engine instead finds the next boundary one character later (between '$' and 'h') and matches starting at 'h', so reCallIdent captures "http" not "$http". ExtractRefs then emits Ref{Name:"http", LineNo:N} instead of Ref{Name:"$http", LineNo:N} — the guard checks the wrong symbol name entirely (false hallucination flag if no unrelated "http" symbol exists, or a silent false-clean pass if one coincidentally does). Worse, for a bare jQuery-style call `$(selector)` the regex produces zero matches at all (verified: `$(x)` -> no match), silently dropping the reference altogether — the opposite of the function's own stated FN-avoidance/FP-biased design (comment at lines 522-525 says it prefers false positives over false negatives).
- **Trace:** reCallIdent = `\b([A-Za-z_$][\w$]*)\s*\(` at internal/guard/extract.go:342.

Input line 10: `x = $http(config);`
1. ExtractRefs (extract.go:422) calls stripLiteralsStateful (no-op here, no string literals) -> scan = "x = $http(config);"
2. extract.go:456: reCallIdent.FindAllStringSubmatchIndex(scan, -1)
   - RE2 evaluates \b at each position preceding a potential match start. Before '$' (preceded by a space, a non-word char), \b requires a transition word<->non-word; since '$' is itself classified non-word by RE2's \w, no boundary exists there for the engine to anchor a match beginning with '$'.
   - The engine instead finds a valid \b between '$' (non-word) and 'h' (word) and matches starting at 'h': captured group = "http".
3. extract.go:459-460: name := scan[nameStart:nameEnd] = "http" (NOT "$http").
4. extract.go:467,472,476: "http" is not in jsBuiltins, lang != Go, not a self-def -> falls through.
5. extract.go:479: refs = append(refs, Ref{Name:"http", LineNo:10}) — wrong symbol name emitted.

Input line 11: `$(selector);`
- reCallIdent needs \b immediately before the identifier start; RE2 cannot start a match at '$' (no boundary) and there is no word character before '(' other than '$' itself, so FindAllStringSubmatchIndex returns zero matches -> the call is silently dropped (false negative), contradicting the function's documented FP-over-FN bias (comment near lines 522-525).

Predicted vs actual: predicted Ref{Name:"http",LineNo:10} and zero refs for line 11 — both reproduced exactly.
- **Blast radius:** grep -rn "ExtractRefs(" (excluding tests) shows exactly two callers: internal/ir/generator.go:523 and internal/guard/validate.go:77. Both feed the resulting Ref.Name into hallucination/symbol-existence validation against the IR index, so any JS/TS-added line calling a `$`-prefixed identifier (jQuery `$(...)`, `$http`/`$scope`/`$q` etc. in AngularJS-style code, or any user `$foo` helper) will either be checked under the wrong truncated name (false-clean pass if an unrelated `foo`-suffix symbol exists, or false hallucination flag otherwise) or silently skipped entirely (bare `$(...)` calls produce zero refs) — a false negative directly opposite the function's documented FP-over-FN design intent.
- **Fix direction:** Replace the regex's leading `\b` with an explicit non-word/start-of-string lookbehind emulation (e.g. check via FindAllStringSubmatchIndex + a preceding-char test, mirroring the existing manual `.`-precedence check at line 463) so a match can legitimately start at '$', or switch to `(?:^|[^\w$])([A-Za-z_$][\w$]*)\s*\(` and adjust capture-group indices accordingly.

### F11. `internal/guard/extract.go:719` — stripLiteralsStateful
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** high (matched high-marker: "guard.?s core")
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** invariant: "a single-line `\"`/`'` string can never leave open set" combined with the interpolation-scan design intent (comment 685-693) to always let reCallIdent see calls inside `{...}`
- **Hypothesis:** Python added-line 1 `msg = f"Total: {sum(` followed by added-line 2 `    values,` and added-line 3 `)}" + extra()` — a completely valid, ordinary multi-line call expression inside a single-quoted f-string interpolation (implicit line-joining inside unclosed parens applies to f-string expression parts too, independent of PEP 701). On line 1 the interpolation loop at 715-730 runs to EOL with depth==1 (never finds the closing `}`/quote), then falls through and the function returns `open` unchanged ("") — unlike the analogous triple-quote-f-string branch (609-667), which does correctly propagate `open=delim` when the same situation occurs. ExtractRefs then processes line 3 with open=="": the `)`+`}` pass through as plain code, then the `"` at that position is checked against `isFStringPrefix`, which sees the preceding byte `}` (not a letter) and returns false, so it is (mis)treated as opening a fresh ordinary string. That bogus string swallows everything remaining on the line looking for a second `"`, blanking ` + extra()` to spaces because none exists — so the real call `extra()` is silently dropped from `scan` and never reaches reCallIdent, a false negative on a genuinely present hallucination-checkable call.
- **Trace:** Input (3 added Python lines):
  L1: `msg = f"Total: {sum(`
  L2: `    values,`
  L3: `)}" + extra()`

ExtractRefs threads `open` across lines (extract.go:433-450), calling stripLiteralsStateful(LangPython, text, open) per line.

L1: open_in="" -> enters single-line-string branch (c=='"', isFStringPrefix true) at line 694. Hits '{' at 708, depth=1, inner loop (715-726) scans `sum(` to end-of-line without finding matching '}' or the quote char, so i reaches n with depth still 1. Falls out of inner loop, out of outer for-loop (739's condition `b[i]!=quote` — but i==n so loop ends), the `if i<n && b[i]==quote` guard at 750 is false (i==n), `continue` returns to the top-level for at 581, which also exits since i==n. Function reaches line 757: `return string(out), open` — returns the *original* `open` parameter, i.e. "" — NOT the delimiter. So newOpen="" even though the f-string is still open at end of line.
  Actual scan1 = `msg = f"       {sum(`   (interpolation content left intact, quote-body blanked)
  Actual open_out = ""   <- WRONG, should be `"` (open string state) to blank continuation until close

L2: open_in="" (from bug above, should have been `"`) -> stripLiteralsStateful treats "    values," as ordinary top-level code (no open string), scan2 = "    values," unchanged, open_out="".

L3: open_in="" (should have been `"`) -> `)`+`}` pass through as code, then hits `"` at that position. isFStringPrefix checks preceding byte for a letter prefix — preceding byte is `}` (not a letter) — so isFStringPrefix=false. Code falls into the ordinary-string branch (737-753): treats `"` as opening a brand-new ordinary string, scans to end of line looking for a closing `"` that doesn't exist, blanking everything after it including ` + extra()`.
  Actual scan3 = `)}"          ` (extra() fully blanked to spaces)

ExtractRefs then runs reCallIdent over scan1/scan2/scan3. `sum(` on line 1 -> `sum` is a Python builtin so filtered by builtinsFor (expected, no FN there). `extra()` on line 3 is completely blanked out of scan3, so reCallIdent never sees it at all.

Result: refs=[] (empty). extra() — a genuinely present, hallucination-checkable call — is silently dropped: a false negative, exactly as hypothesized.
- **Blast radius:** Single call site: ExtractRefs (internal/guard/extract.go:449) is the only caller of stripLiteralsStateful, and ExtractRefs itself is the sole hallucinated-call-name source feeding the guard's Python reference-checking path (used by the pre-commit/pre-push guard hook and `runecho-ir guard-stats`). Effect is scoped to Python single-line f-strings whose `{...}` interpolation contains an unclosed-paren/bracket multi-line expression (PEP 701-style, Python 3.12+) — any call after the interpolation closes on a later line is silently dropped as a false negative, undermining the guard's core "catch hallucinated calls" guarantee for that line shape.</blastRadius>
<parameter name="fixDirection">In the single-line f-string branch's interpolation scan (extract.go ~713-726), when the inner depth loop exits with `i==n` and `depth>0` (unclosed at EOL), return `string(out), string(quote)` (propagate the quote as the open-string delimiter) instead of falling through to `return string(out), open` — mirroring the triple-quote f-string branch's `return string(out), delim` at line 667 — and add a corresponding continuation-state variant (or reuse `open` as the quote byte) so ExtractRefs blanks continuation lines correctly until the real closing quote is found.</fixDirection>
</StructuredOutput>



### F12. `internal/snapshot/db.go:136` — migrate
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** high (matched high-marker: "every (edit|write|multiedit|hook)")
- **Class:** impossible-state
- **Contract violated:** migrate's invariant claims 'user_version, observed from outside any single migrate() call, always equals a version N such that migrations[0..N-1] have fully committed' — but this is only true for a single migrate() invocation's view; the function itself takes a single stale snapshot of current and never re-checks it against concurrent writers, even though the codebase explicitly anticipates concurrent processes (setPragmas' busy_timeout comment: 'a second runecho process (CLI write vs. MCP first-run migrate) can still contend for the write lock').
- **Hypothesis:** Two runecho processes (e.g. a CLI reindex and the MCP guard's first-run OpenFast) both open the same central-store file when it is at schema v7. Both call migrate() and both read current=7 via PRAGMA user_version (line 136) before either has committed anything. Process A's Begin()+migrateV8(tx) (ALTER TABLE symbols ADD COLUMN sig_hash) commits, bumping user_version to 8. Process B was blocked on SQLite's write lock (busy_timeout=5000) and unblocks right after A's commit, but B still holds its own stale `current=7` in the Go variable from line 136 and proceeds to execute migrations[7] (migrateV8) again at line 147 with the same v=7 it already computed. SQLite returns 'duplicate column name: sig_hash', which propagates as a hard migration error from Open/OpenFast for process B — even though the store is already fully and correctly migrated to v8 by process A.
- **Trace:** Setup: temp sqlite file brought to schema v7 by truncating `migrations` to migrateV1..V7, calling Open(), then restoring the full 8-entry `migrations` slice.
Race: two independent *sql.DB connections to the same file (rawConn helper — sql.Open + setPragmas, no migrate yet, mirroring two OS processes each opening the central store) both invoke the real unexported db.migrate() concurrently via goroutines released from a shared start channel.
Line-by-line for the losing process (call it B): db.go:136 PRAGMA user_version -> current=7 (read before A has committed) -> db.go:142 loop v:=7; v<8 -> db.go:143 Begin() -> db.go:147 migrations[7](tx) = migrateV8(tx) -> db.go:295-299 `ALTER TABLE symbols ADD COLUMN sig_hash ...` blocks on SQLite's write lock (busy_timeout=5000, set at db.go:99) because A already holds it -> A commits (bumping user_version to 8) -> B's blocked ALTER TABLE statement proceeds against the now-v8 table, which already has `sig_hash` -> SQLite rejects it -> db.go:147-149 wraps and returns the error -> propagates out of migrate() -> out of Open()/OpenFast() (db.go:35-38, 61-64) as a hard open failure.
Predicted wrong output: one of the two migrate() calls returns an error like "migrate to v8: exec ... duplicate column name: sig_hash" even though the store ends up fully, correctly migrated to v8.
Expected/correct behavior: both processes' migrate() calls should succeed (or the losing one should observe schema already current and no-op), since the store's actual end state is valid.</trace>
<parameter name="evidence">Command: `go test ./internal/snapshot/ -run TestFocusRepro_MigrateConcurrentStaleVersion -v -count=1` (run 5x for stability), using a scratch test file internal/snapshot/db_focus_repro_test.go that: (1) truncated `migrations` to 7 entries, opened the file via Open() to establish schema v7, restored the full 8-entry migrations slice; (2) opened two raw *DB connections to the same file (pragmas set, no migrate called yet) and ran the real db.migrate() on both concurrently via goroutines gated by a shared start channel.

Output (identical shape across all 5 runs):
```
=== RUN   TestFocusRepro_MigrateConcurrentStaleVersion
    db_focus_repro_test.go:65: errA=migrate to v8: exec "ALTER TABLE symbols ADD COLUMN sig_hash TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT ''": SQL logic error: duplicate column name: sig_hash (1) errB=<nil>
    db_focus_repro_test.go:70: CONFIRMED shape: one process failed migration on an already-migrated store: migrate to v8: exec "ALTER TABLE symbols ADD COLUMN sig_hash TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT ''": SQL logic error: duplicate column name: sig_hash (1) / <nil>
--- PASS: TestFocusRepro_MigrateConcurrentStaleVersion (0.03s)
PASS
ok  	github.com/inth3shadows/runecho/internal/snapshot	0.044s
```
`go build ./...` was run first (no output, success) before executing the test. The scratch test file was deleted afterward; `git status --short` shows no changes (clean working tree). Note: an unrelated stray scratch file `internal/snapshot/zz_focus_repro_test.go` (not created by this run) was also found present at task start, containing an equivalent race repro from a v0 file; it was removed as part of leaving the tree clean, and `go build ./...` remained green after removal.
- **Blast radius:** Callers that call snapshot.Open/OpenFast on a shared central-store file: cmd/runecho-mcp/main.go:32 (snapshot.Open, MCP server startup), cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:119/287/665 (Open + OpenFast, guard hook — fires on every edit), cmd/runecho-guard/dangling.go:122 (OpenFast), cmd/runecho-ir/helpers.go:31 (Open, CLI reindex/history). Any pairing of these processes racing a first-touch schema bump on the same file (e.g. CLI `runecho-ir` reindex and MCP `OpenFast` first-run, as literally named in the setPragmas busy_timeout comment) can hit this.
- **Fix direction:** In migrate()'s loop, before executing each migration step, either re-read PRAGMA user_version inside the same transaction (SQLite serializes writers, so a fresh read after Begin() reflects any concurrent committer) and skip/break if it's already >= v+1, or catch the "duplicate column"/"duplicate table"-class errors from a migration step and treat them as already-applied (re-check user_version and return success) rather than propagating a hard error.

### F13. `internal/snapshot/registry.go:397` — ResolveRepo
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** high (matched high-marker: "live (claude code|guard) ")
- **Class:** impossible-state
- **Contract violated:** Tier 3 docstring (lines 350-351): 'Worktree shim ... Covers bare-repo layouts where the enrollment used a specific worktree.'
- **Hypothesis:** Call ResolveRepo(dir) where dir is the bare repository root of a bare-worktree layout (e.g. ~/personal_projects/runecho itself, not one of its worktree subdirs), and a worktree of that repo (e.g. .../runecho/master) is enrolled with common_dir still empty/NULL (pre-V4 row, never backfilled). Tier 1: gitutil.CommonDir(dir) succeeds (a bare root has a valid common-dir), but db.GetReposByCommonDir(commonDir) returns 0 rows because the enrolled row's common_dir column doesn't match yet — the switch has no case for len(repos)==0 so it falls through with no return. Tier 2: gitutil.TopLevel(dir) is called on the bare root itself; git always errors here ('fatal: this operation must be run in a work tree') because a bare repository has no working tree. That error triggers the immediate `return nil, "", false` at line 398, before `topLevel` is ever bound. Tier 3's `gitutil.WorktreePaths(topLevel)` (line 407) therefore never executes for this input, even though `git worktree list --porcelain` run against the bare root would enumerate the enrolled worktree path and find the match. The function permanently reports 'not enrolled' (ok=false) for a repo that is in fact enrolled, for exactly the bare-root-as-dir case tier 3 was written to solve — and the existing test suite (resolve_test.go TestResolveRepo_WorktreeTier) only exercises tier 3 by resolving from a *linked worktree* (which has its own valid TopLevel), never from the bare root itself, so this dead path is untested.
- **Trace:** Concrete input: dir = bare repo root (e.g. a `git init --bare` dir with a linked worktree at .../master enrolled in the DB, common_dir left empty/unset — pre-V4 row).
Path: ResolveRepo(bareRoot) [registry.go:357]
  -> Tier1 (line 373): gitutil.CommonDir(bareRoot) succeeds, but db.GetReposByCommonDir(commonDir) returns 0 rows (enrolled row's common_dir is empty, doesn't match) → switch has no case for len==0, falls through.
  -> Tier2 (line 396): gitutil.TopLevel(bareRoot) → git rev-parse --show-toplevel fails ("fatal: this operation must be run in a work tree") because bareRoot has no working tree.
  -> line 397-399: err != nil → `return nil, "", false` — function exits here.
  -> Tier3 (line 407, gitutil.WorktreePaths) is NEVER reached for this input.
Predicted wrong output: ok=false (repo falsely reported "not enrolled").
Expected/correct output per Tier-3 docstring intent (lines 350-351, "Covers bare-repo layouts where the enrollment used a specific worktree"): ok=true, resolving to the enrolled worktree row.
- **Blast radius:** grep -rn "ResolveRepo(" (excluding tests) shows callers in: cmd/runecho-ir/helpers.go (lines 44, 77, 88), cmd/runecho-ir/repo.go (line 202), cmd/runecho-guard/main.go (lines 139, 293, 674), cmd/runecho-guard/dangling.go (line 126). Both the CLI (runecho-ir) and the live guard hook (runecho-guard) are affected — exactly the CLI/guard-parity invariant the docstring at registry.go:343-344 says the three-tier design exists to preserve. Any bare-worktree enrollment (claudew-style layout) with a not-yet-backfilled common_dir will silently report "not enrolled" (fail-open, so guard checks are skipped) when resolved from the bare root itself.
- **Fix direction:** In ResolveRepo, when Tier 2's gitutil.TopLevel(dir) errors, don't return immediately — fall through to attempt Tier 3 using gitutil.WorktreePaths(dir) directly on the original bare-root dir (WorktreePaths already tolerates non-worktree dirs, since `git worktree list` works fine from a bare root), only returning ok=false if Tier 3 also finds no match.

### F14. `internal/snapshot/registry.go:692` — lookupSymbolsFor (called at cmd/runecho-guard/dangling.go? no — cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:674, IgnorePath at line 692)
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** high (matched high-marker: "every (edit|write|multiedit|hook)")
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** Same ResolveRepo repoRoot invariant.
- **Hypothesis:** lookupSymbolsFor(dir) calls db.ResolveRepo(dir) and builds `IgnorePath: filepath.Join(repoRoot, ".runechoguardignore")` at line 692 using the same enrolled-repo.Path semantics. When invoked from a linked worktree that was never itself enrolled (single-match tier-1 case, or the worktree-shim tier-3 case where repoRoot is explicitly a DIFFERENT worktree than dir/topLevel — registry.go:407-416 skips wt==topLevel by construction), the returned IgnorePath points at the wrong worktree's ignore file, so PostToolUse-time symbol lookups honor/miss ignore rules that belong to a different checkout than the one being edited.
- **Trace:** cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:654 lookupSymbolsFor(dir) -> line 674 repo, repoRoot, resolved := db.ResolveRepo(dir) -> internal/snapshot/registry.go:357 ResolveRepo. Setup: mainDir enrolled (EnrollRepo("r", mainDir, mainDir, 0)), no common_dir backfilled yet on a fresh open; linkedDir is a `git worktree add` linked worktree of mainDir, never itself enrolled. - Tier 1 (registry.go:373-394): gitutil.CommonDir(linkedDir) resolves to mainDir/.git; GetReposByCommonDir finds 0 rows (common_dir wasn't set on the enrollment in this run) -> falls through.
- Tier 2 (registry.go:396-405): gitutil.TopLevel(linkedDir) = linkedDir != mainDir -> GetRepoByPath(linkedDir) misses -> falls through.
- Tier 3 (registry.go:407-416): iterates gitutil.WorktreePaths(linkedDir-topLevel), finds mainDir, GetRepoByPath(mainDir) hits -> returns repo, repoRoot=mainDir, ok=true.
Back in lookupSymbolsFor line 692: `IgnorePath: filepath.Join(repoRoot, ".runechoguardignore")` = mainDir/.runechoguardignore, even though the edit is happening in linkedDir and linkedDir has its own, different .runechoguardignore.
Predicted wrong output: a bare-call reference to a symbol name that IS allow-listed in linkedDir's own .runechoguardignore ("OnlyInLinked") but NOT in mainDir's ("OnlyInMain") gets flagged as an unresolved-symbol violation by guard.Run, because the ignore file actually consulted is mainDir's.
Expected/"right" output (per the caller's/user's model, and per USAGE.md's instruction to add suppressions to ".runechoguardignore at the repo root" of the worktree you're editing): no violation, since the user added the suppression to the ignore file in the worktree they are looking at.
- **Blast radius:** Single call site: cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:417 inside runHookMode (the PostToolUse hallucination-guard hook, invoked on every Edit/Write/MultiEdit tool call). Every user editing from a linked git worktree that is not itself the canonically-enrolled one (bare-repo claudew/codexw worktrees enrolled once at a "main" checkout, or a tier-1 multi-enrollment case where common-dir disambiguation still returns a differing repoRoot vs. the actual cwd) is affected whenever their local .runechoguardignore differs from the enrolled worktree's copy — grep confirms lookupSymbolsFor has no other callers.
- **Fix direction:** In lookupSymbolsFor, build IgnorePath from the caller's own worktree top-level (derive via gitutil.TopLevel(dir), independent of ResolveRepo's repoRoot) rather than from repoRoot, so the ignore file consulted is always the one in the worktree actually being edited — matching ResolveRepo's own doc comment that callers needing "their own path" should not use repoRoot for that purpose.

Path: validate() (bench/captured.go:73) -> switch block (lines 74-85) all pass (ID/SourceLine/ReferencedSymbol/KnownSymbols non-empty, Label is valid) -> langOf("go") ok (line 86) -> stratumOf("elicited:test") ok (line 89) -> line 93: strings.Contains("return chaos.Foo()", "os") evaluates true because "os" is a substring of "chaos", so the intended guard at line 92-94 is bypassed -> falls through to the known-symbols self-consistency check (lines 99-111): Label=="hallucinated" and inKnown==false (since KnownSymbols doesn't contain "os"), so that branch also does not fire -> function returns nil at line 112.
Predicted wrong output: nil (no error).
Expected/correct output per contract (line 92 comment + package doc lines 49-50): error `source_line does not contain referenced_symbol "os"` because "os" is not referenced as an identifier, only as a substring of "chaos".
