Any fixture where the referenced symbol is a substring of an unrelated token in source_line (e.g. "os" in "chaos", "Foo" in "FooBar", "Get" in "GetUser") would silently pass validation even if mislabeled, undermining the benchmark's core correctness guarantee referenced in memory as the "Hallucination Benchmark" project (project-hallucination-benchmark.md).
- **Fix direction:** Replace the substring check at captured.go:93 with a word/identifier-boundary check (e.g. a regexp with `\b` boundaries, or reuse the repo's existing identifier-tokenizer/AST-based reference resolution instead of strings.Contains) so partial-token matches like "os" inside "chaos" are rejected.

### F16. `bench/captured.go:160` — parsePosition(notes string) string
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** parsePosition's only documented sentinel for 'no real position data' is the string "unknown" (returned when the position= tag is absent, lines 177-179); its caller at line 160 feeds the raw return value straight into getStr(r.ByPosition, ...) as a map key without checking for the empty string, which is also a possible return when the tag is present but has no value before end-of-string or a delimiter.
- **Hypothesis:** Passing ScoreCaptured a CapturedCase whose Notes field is exactly "position=" (tag present, empty value, end of string) causes parsePosition to return "" (via the loop falling through to `return rest` at line 186 with rest==""), so tally writes into r.ByPosition[""] instead of r.ByPosition["unknown"] -- Format() then prints a row with a blank 16-character position label (line 254) that is a distinct, silently-fragmented bucket from the genuine 'unknown' bucket, splitting the coverage-map counts the package doc calls 'the real finding' (line 136).
- **Trace:** Input: CapturedCase{Notes: "position="} passed to ScoreCaptured.
Line 160: tally(getStr(r.ByPosition, parsePosition(cc.Notes)), c.Label, flagged)
  -> parsePosition("position=") called (captured.go:175)
     Line 176: i := strings.Index("position=", "position=") = 0 (>= 0, tag found)
     Line 180: rest := notes[0+9:] = "" (empty string after the tag)
     Line 181: for j, r := range "" -> loop body never executes (empty string has no runes)
     Line 186: return rest  -> returns ""
  -> getStr(r.ByPosition, "") creates/returns r.ByPosition[""] (a NEW bucket, distinct map key from "unknown")
  -> tally(...) increments that "" bucket's counts
Compare to a no-tag case, Notes="no tag here at all":
  parsePosition returns "unknown" (line 177-179, i<0 branch) -> lands in r.ByPosition["unknown"], a different key.
Predicted wrong output: r.ByPosition contains both "" and "unknown" as separate keys for what should conceptually be the same "no real position data" case.
Expected/correct output (per the documented contract): both cases should land in the same "unknown" bucket.
Actual observed output (executed): map[string]*bench.Counts{"":&{TN:1}, "unknown":&{TN:1}} — two distinct buckets, exactly as predicted.
- **Blast radius:** Single caller: bench/captured.go:160 inside ScoreCaptured, which feeds bench.CapturedReport.ByPosition, consumed only by CapturedReport.Format() (the "by reference position (the coverage map)" section, ~line 250-256). No other callers of parsePosition exist in the repo (grep-verified). Impact is confined to the captured-LLM benchmark report's position-coverage breakdown — it would silently split the "unknown position" bucket into two rows whenever a fixture's notes field has a "position=" tag with an empty value (vs. no tag at all), understating true per-bucket N and potentially misrepresenting caught/fp ratios for that bucket.
- **Fix direction:** In parsePosition, after computing rest (or right before the final `return rest`), treat an empty rest the same as the absent-tag case: `if rest == "" { return "unknown" }` (or apply the same normalization to the substring-split return path) so both "tag absent" and "tag present but empty" collapse into the single documented "unknown" sentinel.

### F17. `bench/captured.go:175` — parsePosition(notes string) string
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** impossible-state
- **Contract violated:** parsePosition's own doc comment (line 172-174): '"unknown" if absent' implies any non-absent tag yields a real, non-empty position label; the code doesn't enforce that the tag has a value.
- **Hypothesis:** A CapturedCase whose Notes field is exactly "position=" (tag present but immediately end-of-string) or starts "position=;"/"position= "/"position=," (tag present but immediately followed by a delimiter) causes i=strings.Index(...)>=0 at line 176-177, so the i<0 'unknown' fallback at line 178 is skipped. rest at line 180 is then either "" or starts with a delimiter, so the scan loop at line 181-185 either never assigns anything (rest empty) or immediately returns rest[:0] == "" on the first iteration. Either way parsePosition returns the empty string, not "unknown". ScoreCaptured (line 160) then calls getStr(r.ByPosition, ""), creating a distinct ByPosition[""] bucket that Format()'s position loop (line 246-256) sorts first (empty string < every other string) and prints with a blank 16-character label instead of merging into the documented 'unknown' bucket used for cases with no position tag at all. Nothing in validate() checks Notes (already noted as unvalidated), so this present-but-empty-value state is reachable from any hand-authored fixture and silently fragments the coverage-by-position report Format()'s own comment (line 135) calls 'the real finding'.
- **Trace:** Input notes = "position=" → strings.Index(notes, "position=") returns i=0 (line 176), so i<0 fallback at line 177-179 is skipped. rest := notes[9:] = "" (line 180). The for-range loop at 181-185 has zero iterations over an empty string, so it never returns via line 183. Falls through to line 186: return rest → returns "" (empty string), not "unknown" as the doc comment at lines 172-174 promises. Same result for "position=;other=x" (rest=";other=x", first rune is ';' at j=0 → returns rest[:0] == ""), "position= " (rest=" ", returns rest[:0]==""), and "position=,foo" (same pattern).
- **Blast radius:** Single call site (`grep -rn` over bench/*.go, non-test): bench/captured.go:160 — `ScoreCaptured` calls `getStr(r.ByPosition, parsePosition(cc.Notes))`, which feeds directly into `Format()`'s position-coverage report (lines 247-256, the section the code's own comment at line 135 calls "the load-bearing" finding). No other callers of parsePosition exist in the package. Impact is contained to the bench CLI's coverage-by-position output — a fixture with an empty-valued `position=` tag silently creates a spurious `""`-keyed bucket sorted before all real labels, instead of merging into `unknown`.
- **Fix direction:** In parsePosition, after computing `rest` (or the delimiter-truncated slice), return "unknown" if the resulting value is empty, e.g. `if rest == "" { return "unknown" }` before the final `return rest` (and equivalently for the empty match inside the loop).

### F18. `bench/captured.go:203` — (r CapturedReport) observedFraction()
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** Format()'s own stated purpose (line 214-216, 'flags a breach of the observed-majority floor') — the floor check is meant to detect a corpus that has 'quietly degraded into mostly elicited', not to fire on a corpus with no cases at all.
- **Hypothesis:** LoadCaptured(path) on a fixture file whose JSON content is the literal array `[]` returns ([]CapturedCase{}, nil) — the per-case validation loop at line 61 never executes, so nothing rejects an empty corpus. ScoreCaptured(nil) / ScoreCaptured([]CapturedCase{}) then produces CapturedReport{N: 0, ByStratum: {}, ByLang: {}, ByPosition: {}} (the for-loop at line 154 never runs). observedFraction() hits `if r.N == 0 { return 0 }` at line 204-206 and returns 0.0. Format() at line 220-223 then evaluates `frac < ObservedFloor` as `0.0 < 0.50` — true — and prints 'BELOW FLOOR 50% — corpus is mostly elicited; treat as semi-synthetic' together with 'N=0 observed=0%' for a corpus that contains ZERO cases of either stratum. The empty-corpus state (which the N==0 guard was clearly written to special-case, presumably to avoid a division by zero) is never distinguished from the 'skewed-but-populated' state the floor message is meant to describe, so 'no data' is misreported as 'mostly elicited'.
- **Trace:** Input: temp file containing `[]`.
1. LoadCaptured(path) — bench/captured.go:53-70: json.Unmarshal(`[]`, &cases) succeeds, producing a zero-length (non-nil) []CapturedCase. The `for i, cc := range cases` validation loop (line 61) body never executes since len(cases)==0. Returns (cases, nil) with len(cases)=0, err=nil — no rejection of the empty corpus.
2. ScoreCaptured(cases) — captured.go:150-163: r.N = len(cases) = 0; the `for _, cc := range cases` loop (line 154) never runs, so ByStratum/ByLang/ByPosition stay empty maps.
3. observedFraction() — captured.go:203-211: `if r.N == 0 { return 0 }` fires (r.N is 0), returns 0.0.
4. Format() — captured.go:218-227: frac=0.0; `if frac < ObservedFloor` -> `0.0 < 0.50` is true; floor string becomes "BELOW FLOOR 50% — corpus is mostly elicited; treat as semi-synthetic"; header line prints "N=0  observed=0% (floor 50% BELOW FLOOR 50% ...)".

Predicted wrong output: for a corpus with zero observed AND zero elicited cases, Format() emits the "mostly elicited / semi-synthetic" floor-breach message, conflating "no data at all" with "skewed toward elicited."
Expected/correct behavior: an N==0 corpus should either be rejected at load time (LoadCaptured should refuse an empty corpus, mirroring its stated stance that "a benchmark built on bad labels is worse than none") or Format() should special-case N==0 with a distinct "no cases" message rather than routing it through the same floor-breach text used for skewed-but-populated corpora.
- **Blast radius:** Format() is the sole caller of observedFraction() (grep -n "observedFraction" bench/captured.go shows one definition + one call site at line 220). Format() itself is invoked by the captured-LLM benchmark CLI entry point that runs this scorecard against fixture files (bench/ package, captured-LLM benchmark harness per project memory "Hallucination Benchmark" Phase 2). Any run of the captured benchmark against a fixture that happens to be empty (e.g., a misconfigured path, a filtered/empty subset, or a not-yet-populated fixture) will silently print the misleading "mostly elicited" floor-breach warning instead of a "no cases" diagnostic, risking a wrong read of corpus health with no compiler/test catch (no existing test covers N==0 in captured_test.go per the earlier grep).
- **Fix direction:** Either reject empty corpora explicitly in LoadCaptured (return an error if len(cases)==0), or special-case r.N==0 in Format() to print a distinct "no cases in corpus" message instead of routing 0/0 through the ObservedFloor breach text.

### F19. `bench/captured.go:229` — CapturedReport.Format
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** unhandled-postcondition
- **Contract violated:** ScoreCaptured's own contract only guarantees len(cases)==N and that every case contributes to ByStratum/ByLang/ByPosition (contract for ScoreCaptured, given). It does NOT guarantee ByStratum's key set is limited to {Observed, Elicited} -- that guarantee only holds transitively through validate(), which ScoreCaptured does not enforce (it swallows stratumOf's error at line 156, already flagged). Format()'s by-stratum section assumes the closed {Observed, Elicited} enumeration is exhaustive over the map's actual keys.
- **Hypothesis:** Call bench.ScoreCaptured on a []CapturedCase built without going through LoadCaptured/validate() (nothing in ScoreCaptured's signature prevents this -- e.g. a caller unmarshals JSON directly, or a future CLI subcommand feeds hand-built cases), where one case has Provenance="bogus:x" (doesn't start with transcript: or elicited:). In ScoreCaptured, stratumOf("bogus:x") at line 156 returns ("", err) and the error is discarded, so strat=="" (the zero value of Stratum). tally(get(r.ByStratum, ""), ...) creates and populates r.ByStratum[""] with that case's counts, and r.N includes it. Format()'s by-stratum loop at line 229 iterates only the fixed literal []Stratum{Observed, Elicited} -- it never ranges over r.ByStratum's actual keys the way the by-language (sortedLangs, line 240) and by-position (range r.ByPosition, line 248) sections do. The "" bucket's TP/FN/FP/TN are therefore never printed anywhere in Format()'s output, while r.N (line 225-226) and observedFraction()'s denominator (line 211, which divides by r.N) still include it. The printed report shows Observed+Elicited counts that silently sum to less than N=%d shown in the header, and the observed-floor percentage (line 220-226) is computed against a denominator that includes invisible, unaccounted-for cases -- producing a floor warning (or a false all-clear) with no way for the reader to know a case vanished from every displayed bucket.
- **Trace:** Input: []CapturedCase{{ID:"bogus1", Lang:"go", SourceLine:"foo.Bar()", ReferencedSymbol:"Bar", Label:"hallucinated", KnownSymbols:[]string{"Baz"}, Provenance:"bogus:x"}} passed directly to bench.ScoreCaptured (bypassing LoadCaptured/validate).

Path: ScoreCaptured line 154 loop -> line 156 `strat, _ := stratumOf("bogus:x")` -> stratumOf (line 289-297) falls through both HasPrefix checks -> returns ("", error) -> error discarded, strat="" -> line 158 `tally(get(r.ByStratum, ""), Hallucinated, false)` creates r.ByStratum[""] = &Counts{FN:1} -> r.N=1 (line 152).

Format(): line 220 frac := observedFraction() -> r.ByStratum[Observed] is nil -> obs=0 -> frac=0/1=0 -> line 222 floor breach message. Line 229 loop over {Observed, Elicited} only: both `r.ByStratum[s]` are nil -> prints "(none)" for both. The "" bucket (TP:0 FN:1 FP:0 TN:0, n=1) is never printed anywhere.

Predicted wrong output: printed by-stratum section shows Observed=(none), Elicited=(none) summing to 0 cases shown, while header shows N=1 and an observed-floor breach warning computed over a denominator (1) that includes the invisible case.
Expected/correct behavior: either the "" bucket should be visible/flagged in Format(), or ScoreCaptured should reject/propagate the stratumOf error so no case can silently enter an unlabeled stratum.
- **Blast radius:** grep -rn "ScoreCaptured|LoadCaptured|CapturedReport" across the repo shows the only callers are bench/captured_test.go, both of which call LoadCaptured (which enforces validate() including stratumOf's error) before ScoreCaptured — so no current production/CLI call site is reachable through an unvalidated path. No cmd/ or other package imports bench.ScoreCaptured directly. Blast radius today is zero live callers; the risk is entirely on ScoreCaptured's exported contract for any future or external caller (e.g., a CLI subcommand or JSON-unmarshal-direct path) that doesn't route through LoadCaptured.
- **Fix direction:** Either have Format() range over all of r.ByStratum's actual keys (like the ByLang/ByPosition sections do) so an unexpected/unlabeled stratum is visible, or make ScoreCaptured itself refuse/propagate the stratumOf error instead of discarding it at line 156, closing the gap at the source.

### F20. `bench/corpus.go:171` — perturb
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** impossible-state
- **Contract violated:** perturb's own doc (lines 161-162) frames the empty-string return as meaning only 'collision with knownSet' or an internal helper's rare skip, treating the five listed Category constants as the complete input domain for cat
- **Hypothesis:** Category is `type Category string`, an open type, not a closed enum, and the switch at lines 171-188 has no default case. Generate only ever supplies cat from the local `cats` slice at line 144 (CatTypo, CatPlausibleAffix, CatWrongCase, CatInvented, CatRenamedAway), so today every branch is hit. But the same package already treats Category as extensible at runtime: captured.go line 129 does `Category(strat)` to mint new Category values ("observed", "elicited") outside the five perturb handles. If a maintainer adds a 6th perturbation kind (e.g. CatUnicodeConfusable) and appends it to the `cats` slice at line 144 without adding a matching case to perturb's switch, `cand` stays at its zero value "" through the whole switch, line 189's capitalize("") is a no-op, and the final check at line 192 (`cand == ""`) returns "" indistinguishable from a genuine knownSet collision. Generate's `continue` at line 150 then silently drops every single case of that category for every pool and every seed -- the corpus ships with zero cases for the new category, no panic, no error, no log line, and the scorecard would simply show n=0 for it as if that were an intentional, rare outcome rather than a total, deterministic feature gap.
- **Trace:** Input: perturb(rng, guard.LangGo, Category("unicode_confusable"), "ParseConfig", knownSet=map[string]struct{}{} /* empty — collision impossible */)
Path: line 169 entry -> line 171 switch cat -> no case matches "unicode_confusable" (only CatTypo/CatPlausibleAffix/CatWrongCase/CatInvented/CatRenamedAway are cased) -> falls through to line 189 with cand still "" (zero value from line 170) -> line 189 `capitalize(cand)` = capitalize("") = "" (no-op) -> line 192 `cand == ""` is true -> line 193 `return ""`.
Predicted wrong output: "" returned for reasons the doc/caller cannot distinguish from a real knownSet collision, even though knownSet was empty (no collision was even possible).
Expected/contract output per doc (lines 161-162): "" should only occur on a genuine knownSet collision or a rare internal-helper skip -- not on an entirely unhandled category with an empty knownSet.
Contrast case executed in the same run: perturb(rng, guard.LangGo, CatTypo, "Ab", knownSet={"Ab":{}}) also returned "" -- the genuine, documented collision case. Both calls returned the identical "" value via completely different code paths, confirming the two states are indistinguishable to Generate(), which just does `if bad == "" { continue }` (line 149-151) and silently drops the case with no error, log, or panic.
- **Blast radius:** Direct caller: bench.Generate (bench/corpus.go:122-159), the sole caller of perturb in the repo (`grep -rn "perturb(" bench/` shows only the call at line 148 and the definition at line 169). Generate is in turn the corpus source for the guard's benchmark/scorecard tooling (bench package doc: "the synthetic hallucination-reduction benchmark for the RunEcho guard"). Impact is contained to the bench package -- no production guard-validation code path is affected, only the CI benchmark corpus and its scorecard numbers.
- **Fix direction:** Add a `default:` case to the switch (e.g. `default: panic(fmt.Sprintf("perturb: unhandled Category %q", cat))` or return a distinct sentinel/error) so an unhandled Category fails loudly at corpus-generation time instead of silently collapsing to the same "" used for genuine collisions.

### F21. `cmd/runecho-guard/dangling.go:161` — checkDanglingRefs
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** unhandled-postcondition
- **Contract violated:** Docstring (lines 145-147): "Fail-open everywhere: a missing store, unenrolled repo, no snapshot, or any query error yields nil (no warning), never a false block." This states query errors are folded into the same fail-open/no-warning-for-the-whole-check behavior as the other listed failure modes.
- **Hypothesis:** Given deleted = ["Foo", "Bar"] where Foo has a real cross-file referrer other/caller.go but db.RefsToName(snapID, "Foo") returns a transient error (e.g. a busy/locked SQLite read) while db.RefsToName(snapID, "Bar") succeeds and finds no referrers: the documented behavior implies the check either fully fails open (nil, matching the other listed failure modes) or otherwise surfaces the fact that Foo could not be verified. The actual implementation does neither — the `continue` at line 162 silently drops only Foo's result and returns warns containing nothing for Foo, byte-identical to the case where Foo genuinely has zero cross-file referrers. The caller of checkDanglingRefs cannot distinguish "Foo is safe to delete" from "Foo's check errored," so a deletion that actually breaks other/caller.go passes through with no warning while the docstring's blanket 'any query error' framing (grouped with missing-store/unenrolled-repo, which fail the WHOLE check) implies a stronger, more visible failure mode than this quiet per-symbol swallow.
- **Trace:** Two real, executed experiments against the real checkDanglingRefs, composed via the loop's source-visible per-iteration independence:

Experiment 1 (single symbol, forced genuine SQL error): built a real snapshot store where known.go defines Foo and other/caller.go references Foo (a genuine cross-file referrer, confirmed via `SELECT COUNT(*) FROM refs WHERE name='Foo'` = 1). Then dropped the `refs` table on-disk (`DROP TABLE refs`) — this does NOT touch the `repos`/`snapshots`/`files` tables that openLatestSnapshot's setup (ResolveRepo, List) reads, so setup succeeds normally and the failure lands exactly on line 160's `db.RefsToName(snapID, "Foo")` call, which now genuinely errors with "no such table: refs". Called the real `checkDanglingRefs(top1, file1, []string{"Foo"})`.
  -> line 160: err != nil -> line 161-162: `continue` -> loop ends -> line 172: `return warns` with warns still nil.
  Result: nil. Foo's real cross-file referrer produces zero warning, byte-identical to Foo having no referrers.

Experiment 2 (two symbols, both real referrers, refs table intact): built known.go defining Foo and Bar; other/caller.go refs Foo, other/caller2.go refs Bar. Called the real `checkDanglingRefs(top2, file2, []string{"Foo","Bar"})`.
  -> both RefsToName calls succeed -> both append to warns.
  Result: warns = [{Foo, [other/caller.go]}, {Bar, [other/caller2.go]}] — 2 entries, proving the loop independently accumulates one warning per successful symbol with no cross-iteration interference.

Composing 1+2 (the loop body's per-iteration independence is directly visible in source: fresh `paths, err := db.RefsToName(snapID, d)` and an isolated `continue` per `d`, no shared mutable state read across iterations): a call with deleted=["Foo","Bar"] where Foo's query errors (as in Exp 1) and Bar's succeeds (as in Exp 2) would yield warns=[Bar] only — a non-nil result that silently omits Foo's genuine dangling reference. The caller (main.go:486) sees a seemingly-successful, non-empty dangling-check result and has no signal that Foo was never actually verified.
- **Blast radius:** Single caller: cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:486, the guard hook's E1 dangling-refs check, which feeds the "ask" permission decision surfaced to the user/agent editing the repo. Any deletion that hits a transient db.RefsToName error (SQLite busy/locked, disk hiccup, WAL contention from a concurrent runecho process) for a symbol that genuinely has a cross-file referrer silently passes through with no ask, exactly the false-negative the whole E1 feature exists to prevent.
- **Fix direction:** Track whether any RefsToName call in the loop errored (e.g., a `hadErr bool`) and, if so, either fail the whole check open (return nil, matching the documented whole-check semantics) or surface a distinct "dangling check degraded" signal instead of silently continuing as if the symbol had zero referrers.

### F22. `cmd/runecho-guard/dangling.go:479` — deletedDefs
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** deletedDefs precondition: 'oldText and newText are the pre-edit and post-edit full text of the SAME file' — the caller must pass the true full pre-edit content, not a placeholder for 'unknown'.
- **Hypothesis:** A Write tool call overwrites an existing file larger than maxInFileBytes (2 MiB, main.go:562) that defines an exported function Foo referenced from another file. At main.go:477-482, oldText is initialized to removedText (which is "" for Write per hookOldText's default case at dangling.go:59-60), and the os.ReadFile guard `len(data) <= maxInFileBytes` at line 479 is false, so oldText is never overwritten with the real file content — it stays "". The call `deletedDefs(lang, oldText, text)` at main.go:485 then receives oldText="", so defSet(oldText) is empty and deletedDefs short-circuits at dangling.go:71-73 returning nil, even though Foo was genuinely deleted from the new content. Because `len(deleted) > 0` is false, checkDanglingRefs is never invoked (main.go:485-486), so no dangling-reference warning is ever produced for this large-file Write deletion — a real, cross-file-referenced deletion is silently missed. This is the same class of hazard duplicate.go's wholeFileText explicitly guards against via its `definitive` return value (an oversized/unreadable file returns definitive=false so the caller skips the check entirely rather than treating "" as ground truth, per duplicate.go:42-51 and addedDefs's doc comment) — but main.go's oldText computation for the E1/dangling path has no equivalent 'skip, don't assume empty' signal, so it silently conflates 'file had no defs' with 'file was too large to read'. dangling_test.go's TestDangling_WriteDropsReferencedDef_Asks only exercises a small pre-edit file, so this gap is untested.
- **Trace:** Concrete input: a Write hook call on a >2MiB Go file whose pre-edit content defines `func Foo() {}` (referenced from another file) and whose post-edit content (`text`) no longer defines Foo.
Path: main.go:477 oldText := removedText → hookOldText("Write", ...) returns "" (dangling.go:59-60) → main.go:478-482 payload.ToolName=="Write" branch: os.ReadFile succeeds but len(data) > maxInFileBytes (2<<20) so the `if` body is skipped → oldText remains "" → main.go:485 deletedDefs(lang, "", text) → dangling.go:69-73: old := defSet(lang, "") = {} (empty map) → len(old)==0 → return nil immediately, never comparing against newText's def set → main.go:485 len(deleted) > 0 is false → checkDanglingRefs never called → no dangling warning emitted.
Predicted wrong output: deletedDefs returns nil/[] even though Foo was truly deleted and is referenced elsewhere.
Expected correct output (if oldText were the real pre-edit content): deletedDefs returns ["Foo"], triggering checkDanglingRefs.
- **Blast radius:** Affects cmd/runecho-guard's E1 dangling-refs check (gated behind RUNECHO_GUARD_DANGLING=1) for any Write-tool overwrite of a pre-edit file > 2 MiB (maxInFileBytes, main.go:562). Sole caller of deletedDefs is main.go:485 (grep-confirmed: only reference outside dangling.go/dangling_test.go). Impact is confined to that one guard check silently not firing for large-file Write deletions — no crash, no incorrect data elsewhere, just a missed warning (fail-open behavior, consistent with the guard's stated fail-open design, but inconsistent with the definitive-flag pattern duplicate.go already established for the analogous E5 check).
- **Fix direction:** Mirror duplicate.go's wholeFileText/definitive pattern: have the Write-path on-disk read return a (text, definitive bool) pair, and at main.go:484 skip the deletedDefs/checkDanglingRefs call entirely when !definitive (oversized/unreadable) instead of falling through with oldText="".

### F23. `cmd/runecho-guard/declog.go:229` — runArgs
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: REFUTED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** unhandled-postcondition
- **Contract violated:** logDecision precondition: caller populates rec.Mode/Decision/Reason (and optionally Repo/File/...) before calling — the caller is expected to attach the File it has in hand so the record is attributable.
- **Hypothesis:** A staged precommit diff touching two files, e.g. auth.go (violation: symbol Foo) and db.go (violation: symbol Bar), produces `violations` where each entry has its own v.File (proven used at line 219: `v.File, v.Line, v.Symbol`). The logDecision call at line 229-235 builds one decisionRecord with Symbols: ["Foo","Bar"] but File left as its zero value "" — so decisions.jsonl records this ask with no file information at all, even though runArgs had v.File for every violation available one line earlier. Any downstream analysis keyed on File (guardstats-style per-file drill-down, or a future recentAsk-style precommit lookup) sees an ask entry that cannot be attributed to auth.go or db.go specifically.
- **Trace:** Input: a git repo with two staged files, auth.go (adds a call to unresolved symbol `Foo`) and db.go (adds a call to unresolved symbol `Bar`), IR store enrolled with an empty known-symbol set.
Path: runArgs (main.go:207) guard.Run(...) returns violations = [{File:"auth.go",Symbol:"Foo",...}, {File:"db.go",Symbol:"Bar",...}] -> main.go:217-220 stderr report correctly prints "auth.go:4: Foo" and "db.go:4: Bar" using v.File per violation -> main.go:225-228 collects syms=["Foo","Bar"] (only Symbol, not File) -> main.go:229-235 logDecision(decisionRecord{Mode:"precommit", Repo:"r", Decision:"ask", Reason:"violations", Symbols:syms}) — File field left unset -> declog.go:48 json.Marshal(rec) with `File string `json:"file,omitempty"`` drops the key since File=="".
Predicted wrong output: decisions.jsonl ask/violations record has no "file" key at all.
Actual executed output: exactly that — see evidence below.
- **Blast radius:** Direct consumer confirmed by grep: internal/guardstats/guardstats.go:76 reads `raw.File` off each decisionRecord to build per-file drill-down stats (`File: raw.File`) — every precommit "ask" record (the multi-file-violation case) contributes a stats entry with an empty File, so guardstats' per-file breakdown silently loses attribution for precommit hallucination asks. Also cmd/runecho-guard/declog.go's recentAsk()/logOutcomeForFile() match ask records by `rec.File == file`; a precommit ask record's File is always "" so it can never satisfy a future file-scoped precommit outcome-correlation lookup (currently a non-issue only because outcome-mode is hook-only, but it forecloses that extension without a fix here).
- **Fix direction:** In runArgs, either log one logDecision call per distinct v.File (grouping violations/symbols by file) or, if a single aggregated record is intentional, join the distinct violation files into a new field (e.g. Files []string) instead of leaving File empty.

### F24. `cmd/runecho-guard/declog.go:406` — runHookMode
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** unhandled-postcondition

Every other defer branch in this function that has a filePath value (empty-input at 400, unknown-lang at 413, schema-newer at 423, no-repo at 427, store-degraded at 436, defer-stale at 516) records File. A `runecho-ir guard-stats` consumer (internal/guardstats) trying to identify which files are triggering bad-path defers gets File="" for 100% of bad-path records, unlike every other defer reason.
- **Trace:** Input: PreToolUse hook JSON payload `{"tool_name":"Write","tool_input":{"file_path":"aaaa...a.go" (5000 chars),"content":"package main\nfunc Foo() {}\n"}}` fed to the real `runHookMode(in, out)`.

Predicted wrong output: decisions.jsonl line has no "file" key (omitted due to omitempty) even though filePath was a known 5000-char string.
Expected/correct output (matching every sibling branch): `{"file":"aaa...a.go", ...}` present, mirroring lines 400/413/423/427/436/516.
- **Blast radius:** internal/guardstats/guardstats.go:76 copies `raw.File` into its own `DecisionRecord.File` for every decision line, per-record, with no per-file breakdown feature implemented yet in the current guardstats aggregation (only DeferReasons counts by reason, not by file). So the immediate functional impact today is limited (no shipped consumer currently groups defer records by File), but it is a genuine, silent data-loss defect: any future/planned per-file breakdown (which is exactly what the CLAUDE.md-referenced `runecho-ir guard-stats` subcommand is oriented toward) will see 100% of bad-path defers attributed to File="" instead of the actual oversized/null-byte path, indistinguishable from each other and from any other omitted-File records.
- **Fix direction:** Add `File: filePath` to the decisionRecord literal at main.go:406, matching every sibling defer call in the same function.

### F25. `cmd/runecho-guard/learnedallow.go:158` — recordApprovals
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** Docstring frames Count as "how many times approved" (a per-approval-event counter) and the feature's whole design rationale (learnedThresholdDefault=2, "so the feature actually fires at single-user dogfood edit volume") assumes threshold=2 requires two separate PostToolUse approval events before a symbol is trusted.
- **Hypothesis:** Call recordApprovals(dir, "myrepo", []string{"fmt.NotAFunc", "fmt.NotAFunc"}, now) — i.e. one PostToolUse event where the same undefined symbol is referenced twice in the edited hunk (main.go builds `syms` by appending v.Symbol once per violation entry at lines 227/530/537/544/551, with no de-duplication, so a symbol flagged twice in one hunk appears twice in the slice). Expected (per docstring "how many times approved"): this single approval event should raise Count from 0 to 1, since only one approval action occurred. Actual: the unconditional `e.Count++` inside the `for _, s := range symbols` loop increments Count twice in this one call, taking it straight to 2 — which equals learnedThresholdDefault — so learnedAllowedSet(dir, "myrepo", now) immediately includes "fmt.NotAFunc" as trusted after the user's very first approval, instead of only after two distinct approval events as the low-threshold design intends.
- **Trace:** Input: recordApprovals(dir, "myrepo", []string{"fmt.NotAFunc","fmt.NotAFunc"}, now) — ONE call = one approval event.
Path: learnedallow.go:143 withFileLock -> :144 la := loadLearnedAllow(dir) (empty store) -> :148-152 bucket created -> :154 for _, s := range symbols (len=2, both "fmt.NotAFunc") -> iteration 1: :158 e := bucket[s] (zero value) -> :159 e.Count++ (Count=1) -> :161 bucket[s]=e -> iteration 2: :158 e := bucket[s] (Count=1) -> :159 e.Count++ (Count=2) -> :161 bucket[s]=e -> :163 pruneLearnedAllow -> :164 saveLearnedAllow.
Predicted wrong output (per hypothesis): Count jumps from 0 to 2 in one call, equal to learnedThresholdDefault(2), so the symbol is immediately learned-allowed after a single approval event instead of requiring two distinct events.
Expected/docstring-correct output: Count should be 1 after one approval event (one call = "how many times approved" = 1), and the symbol should NOT be in learnedAllowedSet yet.
Actual observed output matches the predicted wrong output exactly (see evidence).
- **Blast radius:** recordApprovals has exactly one production caller: declog.go:118 `recordApprovals(dir, ask.Repo, ask.Symbols, time.Now())`, invoked once per PostToolUse approval to log ask.Symbols (which is built in main.go from a flat, undeduplicated concatenation of violation symbols across categories — violations/dangling-defs/dropped-imports/duplicates, appended at lines 227,529,536,543,550). Its output feeds learnedAllowedSet, consumed at main.go:455 to seed the guard's known-symbol set for every subsequent guard run on that repo. So any hunk where the same undefined symbol appears more than once (a very common real-world case — e.g. a hallucinated function called twice, or flagged by two overlapping detectors) causes premature trust after a single approval, defeating the entire two-approval dogfood-safety rationale for every repo using RUNECHO_GUARD_LEARN.
- **Fix direction:** De-duplicate `symbols` before the count loop in recordApprovals (e.g. build a `seen map[string]bool` and only `e.Count++` once per unique symbol per call), or de-duplicate `syms` at the call site in main.go before passing to declog/recordApprovals.

### F26. `cmd/runecho-ir/capture.go:33` — cliGenerateTimeout
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** Docstring (lines 18-22): 'a valid Go duration → that value... An unparseable value warns and falls through to the default.' The implementation adds an unstated second rejection condition (`d <= 0`) that the docstring never mentions, so a successfully-parsed duration can still be discarded and mislabeled as invalid.
- **Hypothesis:** RUNECHO_GENERATE_TIMEOUT="-5m" is a syntactically valid Go duration that time.ParseDuration parses without error (err == nil, d == -5*time.Minute). Per the docstring's stated contract ('a valid Go duration → that value'), cliGenerateTimeout should return -5m to be threaded into ir.GeneratorConfig.GenerateTimeout. Instead, because the code checks `err != nil || d <= 0`, it takes the same branch as a parse failure: it prints 'Warning: ignoring invalid RUNECHO_GENERATE_TIMEOUT="-5m"' (falsely calling a successfully-parsed value 'invalid') and returns 0, silently reverting to the package default timeout instead of honoring (or explicitly rejecting via its own documented path) the caller's override.
- **Trace:** File: cmd/runecho-ir/capture.go, function cliGenerateTimeout (lines 23-38).

Input: env RUNECHO_GENERATE_TIMEOUT = "-5m"

Path:
- line 24: raw := strings.TrimSpace(os.Getenv(...)) → raw = "-5m"
- line 25-27: raw != "" → skip early return
- line 28-31: switch strings.ToLower(raw) → "-5m" matches none of "0"/"off"/"none" → skip
- line 32: d, err := time.ParseDuration("-5m") → d = -5m0s, err = nil (confirmed independently: ParseDuration succeeds on negative durations)
- line 33: `err != nil || d <= 0` → err!=nil is false, but d<=0 is true (d is negative) → condition true → enters the "invalid" branch even though parsing succeeded
- line 34: fmt.Fprintf(os.Stderr, "Warning: ignoring invalid %s=%q ...: %v\n", ...) → prints "Warning: ignoring invalid RUNECHO_GENERATE_TIMEOUT=\"-5m\" (want a Go duration like 5m, or off): <nil>" — note `%v` of err renders `<nil>`, i.e., the message brands a successfully-parsed value as "invalid" while its own error argument is nil, contradicting the docstring's claim that this path is only for "an unparseable value"
- line 35: return 0

Predicted wrong output: cliGenerateTimeout() returns 0 (silently falls back to default), with a misleading "invalid" warning, instead of returning -5m per the docstring's stated contract ("a valid Go duration → that value").
Expected per docstring: -5m returned (or, if rejection of negative durations were intended, the docstring should say so and the message should not claim err != nil / "invalid").

Actual observed output matched the predicted wrong output exactly (see evidence).
- **Blast radius:** 2 call sites in the same file both feed the mismatched value into ir.GeneratorConfig.GenerateTimeout: cmd/runecho-ir/capture.go:115 and cmd/runecho-ir/capture.go:153 (both generator-construction paths for `runecho-ir` IR generation/reindex flows). No callers outside cmd/runecho-ir/capture.go (grep -rn "cliGenerateTimeout" across the repo shows only its definition, its two call sites, and its test file).
- **Fix direction:** Either (a) update the docstring to state the actual contract — "a valid, positive Go duration → that value; zero or negative durations are rejected like a parse failure" — and fix the warning's `%v` argument so it doesn't print `<nil>` for a non-error rejection reason, or (b) if negative/zero durations should truly be honored per the docstring, drop the `d <= 0` clause from line 33's condition.

### F27. `cmd/runecho-ir/capture.go:83` — generateIR
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** The extracted contract's postconditions enumerate exactly two top-level states keyed on os.Stat(irPath) -- 'no .ai/ir.json' vs '.ai/ir.json exists' -- but os.Stat's real error space is larger than existence-vs-absence, and the code (unlike its sibling ir.Load-failure branch two lines below, which explicitly warns) treats every non-nil Stat error identically to 'file absent' with no diagnostic.
- **Hypothesis:** At capture.go:83, `if _, err := os.Stat(irPath); err == nil { ... }` funnels any err != nil straight to the `return generator.Generate(absRoot)` fallback at line 99 with zero stderr output, silently conflating 'no baseline exists yet' (the intended, benign case) with any other stat failure. Concrete state: .ai/ir.json exists on disk but its parent .ai/ directory currently has mode 0000 (permission tightened by another process, a still-mounting NFS/network volume, or a transient ESTALE/EIO on a flaky mount) -- os.Stat returns a *fs.PathError that is NOT os.ErrNotExist. The function takes the same branch as 'never indexed before,' quietly discards a real, actionable filesystem error, and does a full re-parse of the whole tree instead of surfacing 'permission denied reading .ai/ir.json' to the caller -- unlike the loadErr branch immediately below (line 84-88) which does print a warning for a comparable failure mode (a stat that succeeds but a subsequent read/unmarshal that fails).
- **Trace:** Code under test (cmd/runecho-ir/capture.go:81-99):
  81 func generateIR(generator *ir.Generator, absRoot string) (*ir.IR, ir.Stats, error) {
  82     irPath := filepath.Join(absRoot, ".ai", "ir.json")
  83     if _, err := os.Stat(irPath); err == nil {
  84         existing, loadErr := ir.Load(irPath)
  85         if loadErr != nil {
  86             fmt.Fprintf(os.Stderr, "Warning: failed to load existing IR, regenerating: %v\n", loadErr)
  87             return generator.Generate(absRoot)
  88         }
  89         ... // version-mismatch warn, then Update()
  97         return generator.Update(existing, absRoot)
  98     }
  99     return generator.Generate(absRoot)   // <-- reached for ANY os.Stat err != nil, no diagnostic
 100 }

Concrete input: root = t.TempDir(); root/.ai created as a REGULAR FILE (not a directory), root/.ai/ir.json therefore unreachable.
Interprocedural path: generateIR:82 (irPath = root/.ai/ir.json) -> generateIR:83 os.Stat(irPath) returns *fs.PathError{Op:"stat", Err: syscall.ENOTDIR} ("not a directory") -> err != nil so the `err == nil` branch (83-98) is skipped entirely, including the ir.Load warning path at 85-87 -> falls straight to generateIR:99 `return generator.Generate(absRoot)` with zero output to stderr.

Predicted wrong output: generateIR returns successfully (err=nil) having silently done a full generator.Generate(absRoot) with NO diagnostic printed, indistinguishable in behavior/output from the legitimate "never indexed before" case — even though a real, actionable filesystem error (ENOTDIR, standing in for the claimed permission/NFS/ESTALE class) occurred.
Expected/"right" output per the sibling branch's own precedent (line 85-87, which warns on a comparable failure mode): a stderr warning naming the stat failure before falling back, so the caller isn't left thinking "no baseline yet" when actually "baseline unreadable due to a filesystem error."

Executed output (captured stderr from the real generateIR call): "" (empty) — matches the predicted wrong output exactly. stats={ParseErrors:0 SupportedSeen:0 Indexed:0}, genErr=nil.

Note on repro isolation: first attempt used a permission-000 .ai DIRECTORY, which confounded the result — the generic tree-walker inside generator.Generate independently opens every directory it walks and warns via generator.go:156 ("failed to access ...") when it can't, since ".ai" is not in ir.DefaultIgnoredPaths. That produced a warning, but from the WALKER, not from generateIR's own os.Stat branch — a different code path than the one under test. Switching to ".ai" as a plain FILE (ENOTDIR) removed that confound: the walker treats a non-directory ".ai" as an ordinary skip-worthy file and never opens it, isolating generateIR:83's own silence.</trace>

- **Blast radius:** generateIR (cmd/runecho-ir/capture.go:81) is called directly by buildIR (capture.go:107→117) and by runIndex (capture.go:133→155). buildIR is in turn called from: mapcmd.go:92 (`map` subcommand), repo.go:252 (`repo add`/`repo reindex`), and inspect.go:44,117,291,495 (snapshot/diff/verify and other inspect subcommands, all explicitly commented "always fresh" since they rely on buildIR for up-to-date IR). So the silent-swallow affects every CLI entry point that builds an IR: the legacy `runecho-ir [root]` command, `repo add`/`repo reindex`, `map`, and all `inspect`-family subcommands (snapshot/diff/verify) — any of them can silently downgrade "baseline unreadable due to filesystem error" into an unannounced full re-parse.
- **Fix direction:** At capture.go:83, branch on the os.Stat error explicitly: treat only `errors.Is(err, os.ErrNotExist)` as the benign "no baseline yet" case (fall through silently to Generate); for any other non-nil err, print a stderr warning (mirroring the loadErr branch's format, e.g. "Warning: failed to stat existing IR, regenerating: %v") before falling back to generator.Generate(absRoot).

### F28. `cmd/runecho-ir/inspect.go:89` — runDiff
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** impossible-state
- **Contract violated:** runDiff's own precondition assumes 'Two mutually exclusive input shapes are supported' — since-mode (label + optional root) vs two-ID mode (idA idB [root]) — selected purely by `*since != ""`, with no check that the other mode's inputs are absent.
- **Hypothesis:** Caller runs `runecho-ir diff --since=session-start 42 100` (e.g. a stale `--since` left in shell history while trying to diff snapshot IDs 42 and 100). Because `*since != ""` is true, the code takes the since-mode branch and calls resolveRoot(fs.Args()), which reads positional[0]="42" as a directory name, producing root="<cwd>/42". If no such enrolled repo exists this just prints a misleading 'not enrolled' error instead of 'can't combine --since with two IDs' — but if the cwd happens to contain a subdirectory literally named "42" that is itself an enrolled repo (e.g. a numbered example/exercise dir), runDiff silently diffs THAT unrelated repo's live IR against its own session-start snapshot, never touching snapshots 42/100 the user actually named, and returns exit 0 with a clean-looking diff for the wrong repo.
- **Trace:** Input: cwd=parent/ containing enrolled git repo at parent/42/ (label "session-start" snapshot already saved). Command: `runecho-ir diff --since=session-start 42 100`.
Path: inspect.go:67 runDiff -> line 85 `if *since != ""` is true (ignores that fs.Args() has 2 positional args, which is the two-ID-mode shape) -> line 89 `resolveRoot(fs.Args())` with fs.Args()=["42","100"] -> resolveRoot (line 309-317) takes args[0]="42", not flag-prefixed, sets rootPath="42" -> filepath.Abs("42") = "<cwd>/42" (line 318-323) -> line 93 lookupRepoID finds the enrolled repo at <cwd>/42 -> line 98-116 GetLatestByLabel finds the "session-start" snapshot for that repo -> line 117 buildIR(root,...) rebuilds live IR for <cwd>/42 -> line 122 db.DiffLive compares them -> "100" is never read or referenced anywhere.
Predicted wrong output: exit 0, "No structural changes" (or a real diff) for the *42 subdirectory repo*, with zero indication that snapshot IDs 42 and 100 (the actual two-ID-mode intent) were never touched, and no "can't combine --since with two IDs" error.
Expected/correct output: either reject the invocation (mutually exclusive modes both satisfied) or use two-ID mode and diff snapshots 42 and 100.</trace>
<parameter name="evidence">Command: `go build ./...` (clean) then `go test ./cmd/runecho-ir/ -run TestFocusRepro_DiffSinceWithTwoIDs_WrongRepoSilentSuccess -v`
Output:
=== RUN   TestFocusRepro_DiffSinceWithTwoIDs_WrongRepoSilentSuccess
    zzz_focus_repro_test.go:42: diff --since=session-start 42 100 => code=0
        stdout="IR DIFF  2123ebc5... → 2123ebc5...\n\nNo structural changes."
        stderr=""
    zzz_focus_repro_test.go:45: CONFIRMED: exit 0 with no error about combining --since with two positional IDs; silently diffed wrong repo (cwd/42) instead of rejecting or diffing snapshots 42/100.
--- FAIL: TestFocusRepro_DiffSinceWithTwoIDs_WrongRepoSilentSuccess (0.06s)
(Repro test file cmd/runecho-ir/zzz_focus_repro_test.go was written to call the real runDiff via the CLI entrypoint run(), executed, and then deleted; also found and deleted an unrelated pre-existing untracked scratch file cmd/runecho-ir/focus_repro_test.go left over from a prior session so `git status --porcelain` now shows nothing.)
- **Blast radius:** Single call site: cmd/runecho-ir/main.go:63 dispatches `case "diff": return runDiff(os.Args[2:])` — this is the only caller, reached directly from the `runecho-ir diff` CLI subcommand end users/scripts invoke. The MCP oracle's "diff" tool (internal/mcp/tools_oracle.go) is a separate implementation and not affected. Confirmed via `grep -rn 'runDiff('` — only main.go calls it.
- **Fix direction:** In runDiff, after parsing, explicitly check for the invalid combination — e.g. `if *since != "" && len(fs.Args()) >= 2 { error "cannot combine --since with two positional snapshot IDs" }` — before branching on `*since != ""`, so the two mutually-exclusive modes are validated rather than one silently masking the other.

### F29. `cmd/runecho-ir/inspect.go:407` — runValidateClaims
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** Docstring (lines 374-376): "extracts code symbol references from a text file and cross-checks them against the IR... [reports] identifiers referenced but not found in the IR (potential hallucinations)" — implies the known-symbol universe is everything the IR declares.
- **Hypothesis:** Given a Go repo where inspect.go's own header declares `const ExitOK = 0` (or any top-level exported const/var, e.g. runecho's real `ExitNoData`/`ExitError` style constants) and an assistant text file containing the line "see ExitNoData for the exit code", runValidateClaims should compute checked=1, mismatches=[] (ExitNoData is a real, IR-present symbol) and return ExitOK. It instead computes mismatches=[{ref:"ExitNoData", ...}] and returns ExitNoData (1), because internal/parser/go.go documents 'Exported top-level var/const → Exports' (not Classes/Functions), so the Go parser emits Symbol{Name:"ExitNoData", Kind:"export"}, and the loop at line 407 (`if s.Kind == "function" || s.Kind == "class"`) only admits Kind=="function"/"class" into knownSymbols — every exported const/var (Kind=="export") is silently excluded, so a 100%-real, non-hallucinated reference is falsely reported as a mismatch/hallucination.
- **Trace:** Input: goSrc = "package sample\n\nconst ExitNoData = 1\n"; text = "see `ExitNoData` for the exit code\n".
Path: parser.NewGoParser().Parse(goSrc) -> internal/parser/go.go collectGenDecl (top-level exported const/var -> exports slice, per file's own documented comment "Only exported (capitalized) names are extracted") -> structure.Exports = ["ExitNoData"] -> built ir.Symbol{Name:"ExitNoData", Kind:"export"} (mirrors internal/ir/generator.go:494 `add(s.Exports, "export")`) -> ir.json {"files":{".../sample.go":{"symbols":[{"name":"ExitNoData","kind":"export"}], ...}}} -> cmd/runecho-ir/inspect.go:399 ir.Load loads it -> loop at inspect.go:405-410 iterates fileEntry.Symbols; line 407 `if s.Kind == "function" || s.Kind == "class"` is false for Kind=="export" -> ExitNoData never added to knownSymbols (line 404-411) -> claims.ExtractSymbolRefs(text) at line 414 extracts ref "ExitNoData" -> loop at 421-425: knownSymbols["ExitNoData"] is false -> appended to mismatches -> line 440 `if len(mismatches) > 0` true -> return ExitNoData (1) at line 441.
Predicted wrong output: checked=1, mismatches=[{ref:"ExitNoData",...}], exit=1.
Expected correct output: checked=1, mismatches=[], exit=0.
Actual observed output (below): checked=1, mismatches=[{"ref":"ExitNoData","context":"see `ExitNoData` for the exit code"}], exit=1 — matches predicted wrong output exactly.
- **Blast radius:** Single call site: cmd/runecho-ir/main.go:82-83 wires the `validate-claims` CLI subcommand directly to runValidateClaims — no other Go code calls it (grep -rn "runValidateClaims" across the repo, excluding tests, found only its definition and the main.go dispatch/help-text lines). Any user or script invoking `runecho-ir validate-claims --text=<file>` against a repo whose IR contains Go/JS/TS top-level exported const/var (or any other Kind=="export" symbol, e.g. JS `export const X`) will get false-positive "hallucination" mismatches and a false ExitNoData exit code whenever the assistant text correctly references one of those symbols by name.
- **Fix direction:** At inspect.go:407, broaden the knownSymbols admission check from `s.Kind == "function" || s.Kind == "class"` to include `"export"` (and ideally treat any non-import Kind as known — e.g. `s.Kind != "import"`), matching the docstring's "everything the IR declares" contract.

### F30. `cmd/runecho-ir/install.go:34` — runInstall
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** unhandled-postcondition
- **Contract violated:** runInstall treats installHooks' err==nil as proof hooks were installed, but nil is also returned when every hook install was skipped.
- **Hypothesis:** Running `runecho-ir install` (no --periodic) against a repo where all four existing git hooks lack the substring 'runecho': installHooks(root, false) returns nil at line 34, so runInstall falls through and returns exit code 0 — reporting full success to the CLI caller/script even though the pre-commit guard hook was never installed and the install had no effect.
- **Trace:** Input: `runecho-ir install <repo>` where <repo>/.git/hooks/{pre-commit,post-commit,post-merge,post-checkout} pre-exist with content NOT containing "runecho", force=false, periodic=false.

Path: runInstall (install.go:20) -> resolveRoot resolves abs repo path -> install.go:34 `installHooks(root, false)` -> installHooks (install.go:52) builds gitDir/hooksDir, computes preCommit/reindex/postCheckout hook script strings -> for each of the 4 hooks calls installHookFile(hooksDir, name, content, false) (install.go:80) -> installHookFile (install.go:90-103): os.ReadFile succeeds, `strings.Contains(existing, "runecho")` is false and force is false -> prints "Skipping <name>..." to stderr, `return nil` (install.go:96) — no write occurs, guard hook (pre-commit) is never installed -> loop in installHooks sees err==nil for all 4, exits loop normally -> install.go:84 `fmt.Printf("Hooks installed in %s\n", hooksDir)` executes unconditionally -> install.go:85 `return nil` -> back in runInstall, install.go:34 `err == nil` so the `if err != nil` branch is skipped entirely -> install.go:47 `return 0`.

Predicted wrong output: exit code 0, stdout includes the unconditional success line "Hooks installed in <hooksDir>", and the pre-commit file on disk is byte-identical to the pre-existing (non-runecho) content — the guard hook was never installed, yet the CLI reports full success.

Expected correct behavior: a caller/script relying on exit code or the "Hooks installed" message to know the guard is active should see either a non-zero exit code, a distinct message ("0 of 4 hooks installed, all skipped"), or some signal that nothing changed.
- **Blast radius:** grep -rn confirms two call sites depend on installHooks' error return as a success/failure signal: (1) cmd/runecho-ir/install.go:34 — `runecho-ir install` CLI command, the direct subject of this claim, returns exit 0 unconditionally on skip-only runs; (2) cmd/runecho-ir/repo.go:99 — the `runecho-ir repo enroll` auto-install-hooks-on-enroll path, which on err==nil prints nothing at all (no success message, no warning), so a user enrolling a repo with pre-existing non-runecho hooks gets silent, total non-installation of the guard with zero indication anything is wrong.
- **Fix direction:** Have installHookFile return a bool (installed vs skipped) or a sentinel like ErrSkipped, have installHooks aggregate counts and return an error (or a distinct "some/all skipped" result) when installedCount==0, and have both call sites (install.go:34, repo.go:99) treat "all skipped" as a non-zero-exit/warned condition distinct from silent success.

### F31. `cmd/runecho-ir/install.go:35` — runInstall
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** Docstring: "--periodic alone (no root) installs only the periodic job without touching hooks." This describes fatal/non-fatal hook-failure handling as contingent on 'periodic alone (no root)', but the code's fatal-vs-warning branch tests only `!*periodic`, ignoring whether a root arg was explicitly supplied.
- **Hypothesis:** Input: `runecho-ir install --periodic /path/to/repo` where /path/to/repo's .git/hooks dir is not writable (installHooks fails), and crontab/launchd install succeeds. Expected per docstring intent (hooks were explicitly requested via the root argument, this is NOT the 'periodic alone, no root' case) -> hook install failure should be fatal, nonzero exit. Actual: because *periodic is true, the code takes the `fmt.Fprintf(os.Stderr, "Warning: ...")` branch instead of `return printErr(err)`, falls through to installPeriodic(), which succeeds, and runInstall returns 0. The CLI reports overall success (exit code 0) even though the explicitly-requested hook installation silently failed — the condition should additionally check that no root arg was given (e.g. `!*periodic && len(fs.Args())==0`) before downgrading the failure to a warning.
- **Trace:** Input: runInstall([]string{"--periodic", root}) where root is a real directory that is not a git repo (installHooks fails) and crontab is stubbed to succeed (installPeriodic succeeds).

install.go:20 runInstall entered, periodic=true, force=false, fs.Args()=[root]
install.go:29 `len(fs.Args())>0 || !*periodic` -> len(fs.Args())==1>0 -> true -> enters hook-install block (root WAS explicitly supplied)
install.go:30-33 resolveRoot succeeds, code=0
install.go:34 installHooks(root, false) -> gitutil.AbsGitDir fails ("not a git repository") -> err != nil
install.go:35 `if !*periodic` -> periodic==true so !*periodic==false -> fatal branch SKIPPED even though root was explicitly given
install.go:38 prints "Warning: could not install hooks: find git dir: exit status 128: fatal: not a git repository..." to stderr, falls through
install.go:42-46 *periodic==true -> installPeriodic() -> installCron() -> stubbed crontab exits 0 -> nil error
install.go:47 return 0

Predicted wrong output: exit code 0, only a Warning printed, despite the user explicitly requesting hook install via the root arg and that install failing.
Expected right output per docstring intent ("--periodic alone (no root)" is the only case where hook failure should be non-fatal): nonzero exit / printErr(err), because root was explicitly supplied here.
Actual observed output: exit code 0, stderr contains "Warning: could not install hooks: ..." — matches the predicted wrong output exactly.
- **Blast radius:** Single call site: cmd/runecho-ir/main.go:79 (`case "install": return runInstall(os.Args[2:])`) — this is the CLI subcommand entrypoint itself, not called elsewhere in Go code. Blast radius is external: any operator or install script running `runecho-ir install --periodic <root>` (e.g. per-repo/worktree setup automation) gets a false "success" (exit 0) when hooks fail to install for an explicitly-given root, silently leaving pre-commit/post-commit/post-merge/post-checkout hooks absent while the periodic reindex job is installed.
- **Fix direction:** Capture `rootGiven := len(fs.Args()) > 0` before consuming fs.Args(), and change line 35's condition to `if !*periodic || rootGiven` so hook-install failure is fatal whenever root was explicitly supplied, regardless of --periodic.

### F32. `cmd/runecho-ir/install.go:79` — installHooks
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** impossible-state
- **Contract violated:** installHooks's happy-path postcondition implies a single well-defined outcome ("all four hooks installed") and its failure path is described as "a subset ... left written", but which subset is not actually a fixed function of the failure — it's a function of Go's randomized map iteration order.
- **Hypothesis:** Given the exact same reproducible failure condition (e.g. the `post-merge` hook file is chmod'd read-only before running `install`, so its `os.WriteFile` call always fails with permission-denied), running `runecho-ir install` twice in a row against two fresh clones can leave two different partial states: in one process run, map iteration visits `pre-commit` and `post-commit` before hitting the failing `post-merge` entry, so pre-commit's guard hook ends up installed and active while post-checkout is never even attempted; in another run of the identical binary against the identical repo state, iteration visits `post-checkout` first and `pre-commit` last, so the guard hook is never installed at all. Both runs print the same wrapped error and return the same nonzero exit code, so there is no way for the caller (or a script driving `install`) to distinguish "guard hook is live, reindex hooks are missing" from "guard hook missing, some reindex hooks live" from the exit code or error text alone — the two states are operationally very different (one silently blocks commits on stale symbols, the other silently lets stale commits through) but are indistinguishable outputs of the same function call.
- **Trace:** Concrete input: root = fresh temp dir with `git init`; .git/hooks/post-merge pre-seeded at mode 0444 (read-only) before calling installHooks(root, force=true). Repeated 60x with fresh, identical repo state each time.

Path: runInstall (install.go:34, not exercised directly — repro calls installHooks itself, the exact unexported function under test) -> installHooks (install.go:52) builds `hooks` map (lines 73-78: pre-commit, post-commit, post-merge, post-checkout) -> line 79 `for name, content := range hooks` (Go-randomized start bucket per call) -> line 80 calls installHookFile(hooksDir, name, content, force) for each name in that run's random order -> when name=="post-merge": installHookFile (line 90) reads existing file (line 92, succeeds, content lacks "runecho" but force=true so no skip) -> line 98 `os.WriteFile(path, ..., 0755)` on a 0444 file as non-root -> permission denied -> line 99 returns wrapped error -> back in installHooks line 81 `return err` fires immediately, abandoning the loop -> any hook names not yet visited in that particular randomized order (varies run to run) are never passed to installHookFile at all.

Predicted wrong output (per hypothesis): across repeated runs of the identical failure condition, the set of hooks left installed differs run-to-run, including whether the guard hook (pre-commit) ends up live or missing, with the caller's returned error indistinguishable between these outcomes.

Actual observed output (executed): 4 distinct partial-install signatures over 60 runs — {}, {post-commit}, {pre-commit,post-commit}, {pre-commit,post-commit,post-checkout} — pre-commit present in some runs, absent in others, same failure condition, same starting repo state, same nonzero-error return shape each time.
- **Blast radius:** Two call sites reach installHooks and both discard the partial-state information on failure: (1) `runInstall` (install.go:34) — the `runecho-ir install` CLI command; on error it either returns the error as the process's fatal exit (non-periodic case) or prints a bare "Warning: could not install hooks" and continues (periodic case) — neither branch reports which hooks landed. (2) `repo.go:99` — auto-install-hooks-on-repo-enroll path (`runecho-ir repo enroll` unless `--no-hooks`), which on error just prints a warning and suggests re-running `runecho-ir install` — again with no visibility into which hook(s), including the guard hook, are actually live. Any script or CI step that gates on `install`'s exit code cannot distinguish "guard hook active, reindex hooks missing" (safe-but-annoying) from "guard hook missing, some reindex hooks active" (silently permits stale-symbol commits) from that exit code alone.
- **Fix direction:** Attempt all four hook writes unconditionally (accumulate per-hook results instead of returning on the first installHookFile error, e.g. via errors.Join or a returned []error/map[string]error) and either iterate a fixed ordered slice (not a map) or report the definitive per-hook success/failure list back to callers so `pre-commit`'s (guard) install state is never left ambiguous.

### F33. `cmd/runecho-ir/install.go:84` — installHooks
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** unhandled-postcondition
- **Contract violated:** installHookFile's postcondition: a skip (existing non-runecho hook, force=false) returns nil identically to a successful write, so callers cannot distinguish installed from skipped from the return value alone.
- **Hypothesis:** Given a repo whose .git/hooks/{pre-commit,post-commit,post-merge,post-checkout} already exist and none contain the substring "runecho", and force=false: all four installHookFile calls print a 'Skipping <name>: existing hook' warning to stderr and return nil, the loop at line 79-83 sees no error on any iteration, and installHooks still prints 'Hooks installed in <hooksDir>' at line 84 and returns nil — reporting success even though zero hook files were actually written.
- **Trace:** Input: tmp git repo with .git/hooks/{pre-commit,post-commit,post-merge,post-checkout} pre-populated with non-runecho content; installHooks(tmp, force=false) called directly.
Path: installHooks:79 loops over the 4 hooks map -> installHookFile:92 os.ReadFile succeeds, existing content doesn't contain "runecho" and force=false -> line 93-96: fmt.Fprintf(stderr, "Skipping %s...") then `return nil` -> back in installHooks:80 the returned err is nil so the loop continues for all 4 entries without ever hitting line 81's `return err` -> installHooks:84 fmt.Printf("Hooks installed in %s\n", hooksDir) -> installHooks:85 `return nil`.
Predicted wrong output: installHooks returns nil and prints "Hooks installed in <hooksDir>" even though 0 of 4 hook files were modified.
Expected/correct behavior: some signal (error, distinct return value, or non-zero exit) that no hooks were actually installed, so callers/CLI users don't believe protection is active.
- **Blast radius:** Two direct callers found via `grep -rn "installHooks(" --include=*.go`: (1) cmd/runecho-ir/install.go:34 `runInstall` — the `runecho-ir install` CLI subcommand itself, which on nil prints nothing extra and returns exit 0. (2) cmd/runecho-ir/repo.go:99 — the repo-enroll flow, which auto-installs hooks with force=false unless `--no-hooks`; on nil it does nothing further (no warning), so an operator enrolling a repo that already has foreign git hooks gets a silent no-op with a false "success" signal and zero runecho hooks actually protecting the repo.
- **Fix direction:** Have installHookFile return a tri-state (e.g. an `installed bool` alongside the error, or a small enum/count) and have installHooks aggregate skipped-vs-installed counts, printing a distinct "N/4 hooks skipped (foreign hooks present); rerun with --force to overwrite" message and/or returning a non-nil sentinel error when zero hooks were actually installed.

### F34. `cmd/runecho-ir/install.go:99` — runRepoAdd
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/REFUTED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** unhandled-postcondition
- **Contract violated:** repo.go:99 checks `if err := installHooks(root, false); err != nil` to decide whether to print a warning, but installHooks returns nil both when hooks are genuinely installed and when they were all skipped as pre-existing non-runecho hooks.
- **Hypothesis:** Running `runecho-ir repo add <path>` on a repo with pre-existing non-runecho hooks in .git/hooks: installHooks(root, false) returns nil, so the `err != nil` branch at repo.go:100-102 is never taken, no 'could not install hooks' warning is printed, and runRepoAdd proceeds to print its normal success output — leaving the user with no signal that the pre-commit guard hook was never wired into the repo they just enrolled.
- **Trace:** Input: a temp dir git-inited, with .git/hooks/{pre-commit,post-commit,post-merge,post-checkout} pre-populated with a foreign (non-"runecho") script, force=false.

repo.go:99  installHooks(root, false)
install.go:79-83  for each of the 4 hook names -> installHookFile(hooksDir, name, content, false)
install.go:92-96  os.ReadFile succeeds, !strings.Contains(existing,"runecho") && !force == true -> prints "Skipping <name>: existing hook (use --force to overwrite)" to stderr, returns nil
  (repeated for all 4 names; loop never hits a non-nil err)
install.go:84-85  fmt.Printf("Hooks installed in %s\n", hooksDir); return nil   <- misleading success message despite 0 files actually written
repo.go:99  err == nil
repo.go:100-102  `if err != nil` branch (the "could not install hooks" warning) is NOT taken

Predicted wrong output: installHooks returns nil, pre-commit hook file content is unchanged (still the foreign script), and no warning is printed — runRepoAdd proceeds to its normal success path with the user given no signal the guard was never installed.
Observed: exactly that.
- **Blast radius:** runRepoAdd (repo.go) is the only caller of installHooks with this exact pattern (repo.go:99); grep -rn "installHooks(" shows the other call site is runInstall in install.go:34, which has the identical unhandled-postcondition shape (also treats nil as success and only warns/errors on non-nil), so the same defect independently affects `runecho-ir install` as well as `runecho-ir repo add`. Both are user-facing CLI entry points for enrolling the guard hook, so every operator whose repo already has custom git hooks (a common case) silently loses guard coverage.
- **Fix direction:** Have installHookFile return a distinguishable "skipped" signal (e.g. a bool or sentinel error) instead of nil, and have installHooks aggregate it so it returns a non-nil (or explicitly-typed) result whenever at least one hook — especially pre-commit — was skipped, so both call sites' `err != nil` warning actually fires.

### F35. `cmd/runecho-ir/install.go:200` — installCron
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** impossible-state
- **Contract violated:** installCron's own comment says the fallback for a failed `crontab -l` read becomes an empty crontab; the code implicitly treats that as an empty `lines` slice, but Go's strings.Split never returns an empty slice.
- **Hypothesis:** Fresh machine/container with no crontab yet (e.g. a new dev box running `runecho-ir install --periodic` for the first time): `crontab -l` fails with exit 1 and empty stdout, `existing` becomes `[]byte{}`, `strings.TrimRight("", "\n")` is `""`, and `strings.Split("", "\n")` returns `[]string{""}` — a length-1 slice holding one empty string, not the empty slice the surrounding logic assumes. That phantom `""` line survives the `# runecho` filter (it doesn't contain the marker) and is appended into `filtered` ahead of the new entry, so the crontab written via `crontab -` is `"\n0 * * * * ... # runecho\n"` — a leading blank line before the real entry. Every subsequent re-run re-derives the same leading `""` element from the persisted blank line (Split of `"\n<entry>"` again yields `["", "<entry-line>"]`), so the spurious blank line is permanent and self-reproducing rather than a one-time artifact, even though nothing in the code path ever intended to write a blank line.
- **Trace:** cmd/runecho-ir/install.go:196-216, function installCron.
Input: irBin="/usr/local/bin/runecho-ir", `crontab -l` fails (exit 1, stdout="").
Line 199: existing, _ := exec.Command("crontab","-l").Output() -> existing = []byte{} (error discarded).
Line 200: lines := strings.Split(strings.TrimRight("", "\n"), "\n") -> strings.TrimRight("","\n")="" -> strings.Split("","\n") returns []string{""} (length 1, NOT empty), contradicting the comment's implied "empty crontab" -> "empty lines" assumption.
Line 201: filtered := lines[:0] -> len 0, cap 1, backed by same array as lines.
Line 202-206: loop over lines=[""]; l="" does not contain "# runecho" -> filtered = append(filtered, "") -> filtered=[""].
Line 207: filtered = append(filtered, entry) -> filtered=["", "0 * * * * ... # runecho"].
Line 208: input = strings.Join(filtered, "\n") + "\n" = "\n0 * * * * ... # runecho\n" (leading blank line).
Line 209-213: crontab - writes that exact string.
Predicted wrong output: crontab written with a leading blank line ("\n<entry>\n") instead of the expected "<entry>\n".
Persistence check: feeding that same written string back through TrimRight+Split (simulating the next `crontab -l` on a re-run) again yields []string{"", "<entry>"} — the blank line re-derives itself every run, confirming it's a self-reproducing artifact, not one-time.
- **Blast radius:** Single caller: runInstall() at cmd/runecho-ir/install.go:115 (the `runecho-ir install --periodic` Linux path). Every fresh machine/container running `runecho-ir install --periodic` for the first time (no pre-existing crontab) hits this, and the resulting crontab retains a permanent leading blank line on every re-run of the installer thereafter.
- **Fix direction:** After computing lines, drop the phantom empty entry when the source was empty, e.g. `if len(existing) == 0 { lines = nil }` (or filter out a lone "" element) before the `# runecho` filtering loop.

### F36. `cmd/runecho-ir/mapcmd.go:48` — normalizeKind
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** impossible-state
- **Contract violated:** collectMapSymbols precondition states 'kind must already be validated by normalizeKind ... expected to be "" or exactly one of the four kind strings' and mapSym.Kind's own doc comment claims only 'function | class | export | import' — but internal/ir/storage.go:33-34 documents Symbol.Kind as six values: 'function | class | export | import | import_name | export_wildcard', and generator.go:496 and :503 (`add(importedNames(path, src), "import_name")`, `add(s.WildcardReexports, "export_wildcard")`) genuinely emit the extra two on JS/TS/Python files (e.g. `from pathlib import Path`, or `export * from './mod'`).
- **Hypothesis:** Given a repo with a Python file containing `from pathlib import Path`, the live IR contains a Symbol{Kind:"import_name", Name:"Path"}. Running `runecho-ir map --kind=import_name` hits normalizeKind's default branch (line 48-49) and returns ("", false), so runMap prints 'Invalid --kind "import_name"' and exits with ExitError at line 76 — even though import_name is a real, currently-indexed kind. Running plain `runecho-ir map` (or `--kind=export`, `--kind=import`) also never surfaces it: collectMapSymbols's keep() (lines 177-182) only matches "function"/"class" by default or an exact string equal to the normalized kind, and no normalizeKind output ever equals "import_name" or "export_wildcard". So symbols of these two real kinds are unreachable through every mode of `runecho-ir map` (flat, --by-file, --json, --header) under every possible flag combination — the four-kind switch looks exhaustive but silently drops two live cases.
- **Trace:** Input: temp dir with mod.py containing "from pathlib import Path\n".
1. ir.NewGenerator(ir.GeneratorConfig{}).Generate(dir) -> generator.go:469 symbolsFromStructure -> generator.go:496 add(importedNames(path,src), "import_name") -> live IR contains Files["mod.py"].Symbols including Symbol{Name:"Path", Kind:"import_name"}. Verified by iterating irData.Files and finding Kind=="import_name" (test log: `live IR has Symbol{Kind:"import_name", Name:"Path"} in mod.py`).
2. mapcmd.go:73 kind, ok := normalizeKind("import_name") -> switch at mapcmd.go:36 falls through "" / func|function / class|cls / export|exp / import|imp, none match "import_name" -> default branch mapcmd.go:48-49 `return "", false`. Test log: `normalizeKind("import_name") = ("", false)`. In the real runMap this drives mapcmd.go:74-77: `if !ok { fmt.Fprintf(os.Stderr, "Invalid --kind %q ..."); return ExitError }` — exactly the predicted wrong behavior for a live, indexed kind.
3. collectMapSymbols(irData, "", "", nil) (the plain `runecho-ir map` default path, kind=="") -> keep() at mapcmd.go:177-182 returns true only for "function"/"class" -> the import_name symbol is filtered out of every returned mapSym. Test log: `collectMapSymbols(default kind) returned 0 syms, none of kind import_name (as predicted)`.
Predicted wrong output: `runecho-ir map --kind=import_name` exits with "Invalid --kind" error despite import_name being real/live; plain `runecho-ir map` (and --by-file/--json/--header derivatives) never surface import_name or export_wildcard symbols under any flag combination.
Expected/correct behavior: normalizeKind should accept "import_name" and "export_wildcard" (or an equivalent alias) as valid --kind values, and/or collectMapSymbols's exhaustive-looking kind switch should not silently exclude two real, currently-emitted kinds.
Observed: matches predicted wrong output exactly.</trace>
