<parameter name="evidence">Command: `go build ./...` (repo root) -> no output, exit 0 (build clean before/after, no source files modified).
Command: `go test ./cmd/runecho-ir/ -run TestFocusRepro_ImportNameUnreachable -v`
Output:
=== RUN   TestFocusRepro_ImportNameUnreachable
    focusrepro_test.go:35: live IR has Symbol{Kind:"import_name", Name:"Path"} in mod.py
    focusrepro_test.go:46: normalizeKind("import_name") = ("", false)
    focusrepro_test.go:59: collectMapSymbols(default kind) returned 0 syms, none of kind import_name (as predicted)
--- PASS: TestFocusRepro_ImportNameUnreachable (0.02s)
PASS
ok  	github.com/inth3shadows/runecho/cmd/runecho-ir	0.036s

Repro used the real repo functions (ir.NewGenerator/Generate, normalizeKind, collectMapSymbols) — no reimplementation. Scratch file cmd/runecho-ir/focusrepro_test.go was deleted after the run; `git status --short` / `git diff --stat` for this task's own artifacts show no changes (an unrelated `zzfocus_repro_test.go` remains in the working tree from a separate, concurrently-running verification session in this shared checkout — not created or touched by this task).
- **Blast radius:** Both normalizeKind and collectMapSymbols have exactly one caller each, runMap (cmd/runecho-ir/mapcmd.go:73 and :115) — confirmed via `grep -rn "normalizeKind|collectMapSymbols"` across cmd/ and internal/ (non-test hits only in mapcmd.go itself). So the defect is fully contained to the `runecho-ir map` CLI subcommand: every invocation mode (flat, --by-file, --json) silently omits import_name/export_wildcard symbols by default, and any explicit `--kind=import_name` or `--kind=export_wildcard` hard-errors with "Invalid --kind" even though those kinds are live and indexed. No other subcommand or internal caller is affected.
- **Fix direction:** Add "import_name" and "export_wildcard" (with sensible flag aliases, e.g. "import_name"/"importname" and "export_wildcard"/"wildcard") as accepted cases in normalizeKind's switch, and update collectMapSymbols's default-kind keep() / doc comment plus kindAbbrev if they should also appear in the unfiltered default view — or explicitly document that these two are --kind-only (not part of the function+class default) if that's the intended scope.

### F37. `cmd/runecho-ir/mapcmd.go:62` — runMap
- **Verdict:** ❓ UNVERIFIED (votes: CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** changedSymbols precondition states sessionID is used to pick GetLatestByLabelSession vs GetLatestByLabel — implicitly assuming callers only supply --session together with a meaningful --since.
- **Hypothesis:** Running `runecho-ir map --session=abc123` with no `--since` parses successfully and produces byte-identical output to `runecho-ir map` with no flags at all: `*sessionID` is populated but changedSymbols (the only reader of sessionID, line 108) is only invoked inside `if *since != ""` (line 107-113). The CLI gives no error and no warning that the session filter was silently discarded — a user scoping a review to one agent session gets the full unscoped map with no indication anything was ignored.
- **Trace:** Input A: `runecho-ir map <dir>` (no flags).
Input B: `runecho-ir map --session=abc123 <dir>`.
Path for both: runMap() -> fs parses flags (sessionID="" or "abc123", since="") -> line 73 normalizeKind -> line 79 resolveRoot -> line 84 mustOpenDB -> line 92 buildIR -> line 100 `if *header` false -> line 107 `if *since != ""` is FALSE for both inputs (since == "" in both cases) -> changedSymbols (and thus sessionID) is never called/read -> line 115 collectMapSymbols(irData, kind, dirPrefix, changed=nil) -> identical rendering path for A and B.
Predicted wrong output: stdout, stderr, and exit code identical between A and B, with no error/warning that --session was ignored.
Expected/correct behavior (per the claim being tested as a defect): either reject --session without --since, or emit a warning that the session filter has no effect without --since.
- **Blast radius:** Sole caller of changedSymbols is runMap in cmd/runecho-ir/mapcmd.go (grep -rn "changedSymbols(" confirms one call site). Sole consumer-facing surface is the `runecho-ir map` CLI subcommand; no other command or internal package passes --session through this path. Impact is limited to interactive/agent CLI users of `map --since --session`, but is a genuine UX/correctness trap: a user or agent scoping a change-review to one session ID gets zero indication the filter was dropped when --since is also missing (e.g. typo'd/omitted --since).
- **Fix direction:** In runMap, after flag parsing, if *sessionID != "" && *since == "", print a stderr warning (or return ExitError) that --session has no effect without --since, mirroring the existing --kind validation pattern at lines 73-77.

### F38. `cmd/runecho-ir/mapcmd.go:100` — runMap
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** runMap postcondition: '--header short-circuits before any --since/collect work ... returns 0 immediately' — implies the header path is insulated from unrelated flag values.
- **Hypothesis:** Running `runecho-ir map --header --kind=bogus` hits the `normalizeKind` check at line 73-77 BEFORE the `*header` check at line 100, so it returns ExitError with stderr `Invalid --kind "bogus" (want func|class|export|import)` and never reaches emitMapHeader — even though --header's own code (lines 210-256, emitMapHeader) never reads kindFlag at all. A caller that always passes `--header` from a session-start hook alongside a stale/mistyped `--kind` env var gets a hard failure instead of the intended <200-token summary, for a flag the header path doesn't use.
- **Trace:** Input: `runecho-ir map --header --kind=bogus <repo>`
Path: main.go:65 runMap(os.Args[2:]) -> mapcmd.go:69 parseSub succeeds (flags parse fine) -> mapcmd.go:73 kind, ok := normalizeKind("bogus") -> normalizeKind default case (line 48-49) returns ("", false) -> mapcmd.go:74 ok==false -> mapcmd.go:75-76 fmt.Fprintf(stderr, "Invalid --kind %q ...") + return ExitError -> function returns 2, NEVER reaching line 100's `if *header` check or emitMapHeader.
Predicted wrong output: exit code 2 (ExitError), stderr = Invalid --kind message, stdout empty (no header printed).
Expected/intended output per doc comment "with --header ... to NOT spend context ... just tell the agent the map exists": header should print regardless of an unrelated/unused --kind value.
- **Blast radius:** Single internal caller: cmd/runecho-ir/main.go:65 (the `map` subcommand dispatch in run()) — confirmed via `grep -rn "runMap("`. External blast radius: USAGE.md documents `runecho-ir map --header` explicitly as the SessionStart-hook priming invocation; any wrapper/hook that appends --header alongside a separately-sourced or stale --kind value (e.g. an env-var-driven flag set shared across map invocations) would hard-fail the header path for a flag the header path never consults.
- **Fix direction:** Move the `if *header { emitMapHeader(irData); return 0 }` block to before the normalizeKind validation (or skip kind validation entirely when *header is set), so --header is truly insulated from --kind as its doc comment claims.

### F39. `cmd/runecho-ir/mapcmd.go:189` — collectMapSymbols
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/REFUTED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** --dir flag help text promises symbols 'under this path prefix' (directory-scoped containment), implying a path-segment-aware match, but the implementation does a raw string prefix test with no separator boundary check.
- **Hypothesis:** collectMapSymbols(irData, kind, "internal", nil) on an irData containing a symbol in file "internal2/foo.go" INCLUDES that symbol in the result (strings.HasPrefix("internal2/foo.go", "internal") == true), when the correct behavior per the --dir semantics ('files under this path') should EXCLUDE it because internal2/ is a sibling directory, not a subdirectory of internal/.
- **Trace:** Input: irData.Files = {"internal2/foo.go": [Symbol{Name:"Sibling",Kind:"function"}], "internal/bar.go": [Symbol{Name:"TrueChild",Kind:"function"}]}; call collectMapSymbols(irData, "", "internal", nil).
Path: mapcmd.go:184 range over irData.SymbolLocations() (sorted list containing both symbols) -> mapcmd.go:186 keep("function") true for both -> mapcmd.go:189 `strings.HasPrefix(s.File, dirPrefix)`: for s.File="internal2/foo.go", dirPrefix="internal" -> strings.HasPrefix("internal2/foo.go","internal") == true -> condition `!HasPrefix` is false -> continue is NOT hit -> symbol kept (line 195 append). Same true-branch for "internal/bar.go".
Predicted wrong output: result contains both "Sibling" (from internal2/foo.go) and "TrueChild" (from internal/bar.go).
Expected correct output per --dir semantics ("only files under this path prefix" = directory containment): result should contain only "TrueChild" (internal/bar.go), excluding "Sibling" since internal2/ is a sibling directory, not a subdirectory of internal/.
Actual observed output: [{Name:Sibling Kind:function File:internal2/foo.go Line:1} {Name:TrueChild Kind:function File:internal/bar.go Line:1}] — both included, matching the predicted wrong output exactly.
- **Blast radius:** Single call site: cmd/runecho-ir/mapcmd.go:115 (`runMap`, the `runecho-ir map` CLI subcommand), which passes the user-supplied `--dir` flag value (mapcmd.go:60, help text "only files under this path prefix") straight into collectMapSymbols. No other internal callers found via `grep -rn collectMapSymbols` (only mapcmd.go and its existing unit tests in mapcmd_test.go, none of which cover the sibling-directory boundary case). User-facing impact: `runecho-ir map --dir=internal` silently pulls in symbols from any sibling directory sharing that string prefix (e.g. internal2/, internals/), polluting the returned symbol map.
- **Fix direction:** At mapcmd.go:189, match on a path-segment boundary, e.g. `dirPrefix := strings.TrimSuffix(dirPrefix, "/"); if s.File != dirPrefix && !strings.HasPrefix(s.File, dirPrefix+"/") { continue }`.

### F40. `cmd/runecho-ir/mapcmd.go:333` — emitMapJSON
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** unhandled-postcondition
- **Contract violated:** emitMapByFile postcondition/invariant: symbols are 'sorted by line then name' via the explicit sort.Slice at lines 302-307 — the by-file grouping in emitMapJSON produces the same conceptual view (symbols grouped under their file) but has no equivalent sort.
- **Hypothesis:** Given a file with function Zeta at line 5 and function Alpha at line 50, `runecho-ir map --by-file` (text mode) prints Zeta(5) before Alpha(50) inside that file's block because emitMapByFile explicitly re-sorts each group by (Line, Name). `runecho-ir map --by-file --json` on the identical repo state instead yields `payload["files"]["pkg/file.go"] = [Alpha, Zeta]` (Alpha before Zeta) because the loop at lines 332-335 appends symbols in SymbolLocations()'s name-primary sort order with no re-sort — the same query's two output modes disagree on per-file symbol order.
- **Trace:** Input: two mapSym for the same file "pkg/file.go" — {Name:"Alpha", Line:50} and {Name:"Zeta", Line:5} — passed in name-sorted order (Alpha, Zeta), matching what `collectMapSymbols`/`SymbolLocations()` would actually hand to both emit functions.
Path A (text): runMap -> emitMapByFile(syms, compact) [mapcmd.go:121] -> group := byFile[file] -> sort.Slice by (Line,Name) [302-307] -> prints Zeta(5) then Alpha(50).
Path B (json): runMap -> emitMapJSON(root, syms, true, false) [mapcmd.go:118] -> `for _, s := range syms { files[s.File] = append(...) }` [332-335, no sort] -> payload["files"]["pkg/file.go"] = [Alpha(50), Zeta(5)] — order taken verbatim from the name-sorted input.
Predicted: text mode -> [Zeta, Alpha]; json mode -> [Alpha, Zeta]. Actual (executed): identical.
- **Blast radius:** Direct caller: `runMap` in cmd/runecho-ir/mapcmd.go:118 (the `runecho-ir map --by-file --json` CLI path — the only caller of `emitMapJSON`). Any downstream consumer that parses `runecho-ir map --by-file --json` output and assumes per-file symbols come back in source/line order (e.g. an agent or script rendering a per-file outline, or a diffing/snapshot tool comparing file symbol order) will silently get name-sorted order instead, diverging from the human-facing text mode of the identical query. No other function calls emitMapJSON (grep confirms single call site), so blast radius is limited to `--json --by-file` consumers, but that is documented as "parity with diff --json" (line 322 comment), which this bug breaks.
- **Fix direction:** In emitMapJSON's by-file branch, after building `files`, sort each `files[path]` slice by (Line, Name) the same way emitMapByFile does (lines 302-307) — or factor that sort into a shared helper both functions call.

### F41. `cmd/runecho-ir/repo.go:73` — runRepoAdd
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** impossible-state
- **Contract violated:** EnrollRepo/EffectiveSourceRoot/doReindex implicitly assume SourceRoot is either empty or already an absolute, CWD-independent path (mirroring how `root` is always produced via resolveRoot's filepath.Abs before being stored as Path) — but `*sourceRoot` is passed straight from the raw `--source-root` flag value with no filepath.Abs() call anywhere in the add path.
- **Hypothesis:** `runecho-ir repo add --source-root=src /home/user/proj` run with CWD=/home/user/proj stores SourceRoot="src" verbatim (EnrollRepo's own normalization at registry.go:47 only fires when sourceRoot=="", never for a non-empty relative value). The immediate auto-reindex inside runRepoAdd (line 94) still works by luck because CWD happens to be /home/user/proj at that moment. But any later `runecho-ir repo reindex proj` invoked from a different CWD (cron job, git hook, different terminal tab) hits doReindex→EffectiveSourceRoot()=="src"→buildIR("src", cap)→filepath.Abs("src"), which resolves relative to whatever the *reindex* process's CWD is, not /home/user/proj. If a directory named "src" doesn't exist there it errors; if one does exist (e.g. an unrelated project's src/ tree), doReindex silently walks and indexes that unrelated code and writes ir.json + a new snapshot row under the enrolled repo `proj`'s repo_id, corrupting its snapshot history with foreign code and producing wrong-file diagnostics from every runecho tool (locate/structure/guard) against that repo from then on.
- **Trace:** Input: `runecho-ir repo add --source-root=src /home/user/proj1` conceptually run with CWD=/home/user/proj1.
1. cmd/runecho-ir/repo.go:48 resolveRoot(...) -> root = absolute path to proj1 (filepath.Abs applied here).
2. cmd/runecho-ir/repo.go:73 db.EnrollRepo(n, root, *sourceRoot, *cap) -> *sourceRoot is the raw flag string "src", passed with NO filepath.Abs() call anywhere in the add path.
3. internal/snapshot/registry.go:46-49 EnrollRepo: `if sourceRoot == "" { sourceRoot = path }` — since sourceRoot="src" is non-empty, this normalization never fires; "src" is INSERTed into repos.source_root verbatim (relative).
4. Immediate auto-reindex (repo.go:94 doReindex) happens to work because the add process's CWD is still proj1: registry.go:35-39 EffectiveSourceRoot() returns "src" -> cmd/runecho-ir/capture.go:108 filepath.Abs("src") resolves relative to CWD=proj1 -> proj1/src (correct, by luck of shared CWD).
5. LATER, a separate `runecho-ir repo reindex proj1` process launched from a different CWD (e.g. /home/user/unrelated-project, which independently happens to contain its own src/ directory): doReindex (repo.go:251-252) calls repo.EffectiveSourceRoot() -> still the stored literal "src" -> buildIR("src", cap) -> capture.go:108 filepath.Abs("src") now resolves against THIS process's CWD -> /home/user/unrelated-project/src, a directory belonging to a different project entirely.

Predicted wrong output: EffectiveSourceRoot()=="src" resolves to proj1/src when reindexed from proj1's CWD, but to unrelated-project/src when reindexed from a different CWD — same stored value, different, wrong resolved directory depending purely on caller CWD.

Expected/correct behavior (per the contract EnrollRepo/EffectiveSourceRoot/doReindex assume, mirroring how `root` is always filepath.Abs'd via resolveRoot before storage): SourceRoot should have been normalized to an absolute path at enroll time, so EffectiveSourceRoot() always resolves to the same directory regardless of which process's CWD is active at reindex time.
- **Blast radius:** Every caller that reads repo.EffectiveSourceRoot() is corrupted once a bad snapshot/IR gets written under the enrolled repo's identity: cmd/runecho-ir/repo.go:251-252 (doReindex, used by both `repo add`'s auto-reindex and `repo reindex`), cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:297 (guard hook), and internal/mcp/tools_oracle.go:266,325,396,412,510 (all runecho MCP tools: locate/structure/diff/etc. via liveIR). Since doReindex writes ir.json AND a new snapshot row keyed by the enrolled repo's repo_id (repo.go:256-259), a single mis-CWD'd reindex permanently pollutes that repo's snapshot history and all downstream tool answers for it — this is exactly the --source-root path documented for bare-repo worktree layouts (repo.go:42), so it's a supported, not exotic, usage.
- **Fix direction:** In runRepoAdd (or inside EnrollRepo itself), normalize a non-empty sourceRoot with filepath.Abs(*sourceRoot) (relative to the add-time CWD, matching resolveRoot's treatment of root) before it is ever passed to db.EnrollRepo, so EffectiveSourceRoot() is always CWD-independent once stored.

### F42. `cmd/runecho-ir/repo.go:94` — doReindex
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** unhandled-postcondition
- **Contract violated:** doReindex's postcondition: returns buildIR's non-zero error code immediately on IR-build failure, or printErr's non-zero code on ir.json write failure or SaveSnapshot failure — signaling that indexing did not complete successfully.
- **Hypothesis:** Running `runecho-ir repo add /path/to/repo` where /path/to/repo has a file that makes buildIR fail (e.g. unparseable/unsupported content causing a non-zero buildIR exit) causes doReindex at line 94 to return a non-zero code that is discarded (call result not assigned to any variable, not checked). Execution falls through to the hook-install step and then unconditionally `return 0` at line 104, so `runecho-ir repo add` prints 'Enrolled ...' and 'Indexing ...' and exits 0, while .ai/ir.json was never written and no snapshot was saved — the caller never checks the very error return that doReindex's contract exists to report.
- **Trace:** Input: `runecho-ir repo add --no-hooks <repo>` where `<repo>/.ai` is a pre-existing regular file (not a dir).
repo.go:38 runRepoAdd → EnrollRepo succeeds (repo enrollment doesn't touch .ai) → prints "Enrolled ..."
repo.go:91-94: `enrolled, err2 := db.GetRepoByName(n)` succeeds → prints "Indexing scratchpad-repro_repo3..." → `doReindex(db, enrolled)` called, return value NOT assigned/checked
  → inside doReindex (repo.go:250): buildIR succeeds (srcRoot exists, files parse fine)
  → repo.go:256: `irData.Save(filepath.Join(srcRoot, ".ai", "ir.json"))` → storage.go:218 `os.MkdirAll(".ai", 0755)` fails: "not a directory" (because .ai is a file)
  → repo.go:257: `return printErr(fmt.Errorf("save ir.json: %w", err))` → prints "Error: save ir.json: failed to create IR dir: ... not a directory" to stderr, returns e.g. 1
  → back in runRepoAdd: this int return is discarded (statement-only call, no `:=`/check)
repo.go:97-103: `!*noHooks` is false (--no-hooks passed) → hook block skipped
repo.go:104: `return 0` unconditionally
Predicted wrong output: process exits 0 despite the printed Error line and despite ir.json never being written / no snapshot saved / TouchRepo never running.
Actual observed output: exactly that — "EXIT CODE: 0" after the Error line, and `repo list` showed LAST-INDEXED=never for the enrolled repo, confirming indexing did not complete.
- **Blast radius:** grep -rn "doReindex(" confirms 3 call sites total: repo.go:219 (runRepoReindex) does `return doReindex(...)` — propagates correctly; repo.go:241 (runRepoReindexAll) does `if c := doReindex(...); c != 0 { exitCode = c }` — propagates correctly. Only repo.go:94 inside runRepoAdd discards the result — i.e. only `runecho-ir repo add <path>` (the enroll+auto-index path) is affected; `repo reindex` and `repo reindex --all` are unaffected.
- **Fix direction:** At repo.go:94, capture and propagate: `if code := doReindex(db, enrolled); code != 0 { return code }` (or at minimum print a non-fatal warning and skip hook install) before falling through to `return 0`.

### F43. `internal/guard/diff.go:84` — parseHunkStart
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** unhandled-postcondition
- **Contract violated:** parseDiffOutput (sole caller, diff.go:84) treats parseHunkStart's return value as always-correct ('the correct 1-indexed new-file line number' per parseDiffOutput's own invariant), but parseHunkStart's documented postcondition allows a silent fallback to 1 on any malformed '@@' header with no error/signal for the caller to detect or propagate.
- **Hypothesis:** For a staged diff containing a hunk header that doesn't match the standard '-old[,count] +new[,count]' shape (e.g. '@@ -5,+7,3 @@' with no space between the two ranges, or any header where strings.Fields never produces a token with a bare leading '+'), parseHunkStart returns 1 instead of the true new-file start line. parseDiffOutput then assigns newLineNo=1 at diff.go:84 and every subsequent AddedLine.LineNo in that hunk is computed from base 1 (diff.go:91/94) instead of the real file position. This propagates unchanged through guard.Run (validate.go:92, `Line: ref.LineNo`) into the reported Violation.Line, so `runecho-guard` prints a wrong line number (e.g. reporting line 2 for a hallucinated symbol that actually lives at line 500) for any violation found in that hunk, with no warning that the number is unreliable — unlike the sibling ErrTooLong case, which does set `partial=true` and is surfaced to the user in cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:187-194.
- **Trace:** Input hunk header string: "@@ -5,+500,3 @@" (no space between the '-old' range and the '+new' range — true new-file start is 500).

diff.go:146 `parts := strings.Fields(line)` → parts = ["@@", "-5,+500,3", "@@"]. The second token starts with '-', not '+', because there's no space separating the ranges, so `strings.HasPrefix(p, "+")` at line 148 never matches any token.
→ loop body never executes `return n` (line 153)
→ line 157: `return 1` (silent fallback), expected/true value was 500.

Caller path: parseDiffOutput (diff.go:83-85) sees a line prefixed "@@ " and does `newLineNo = parseHunkStart(line)` → newLineNo = 1 (should be 500).
Next line "+halluc()" (diff.go:89-95): AddedLine{LineNo: newLineNo=1, Text:"halluc()"} appended; newLineNo incremented to 2. No error/partial is set — parseDiffOutput returns partial=false, err=nil.

This AddedLine.LineNo=1 flows unchanged into validate.go:92 (`Line: ref.LineNo`) and out to the guard.Violation the CLI reports (cmd/runecho-guard/main.go), with zero signal that the number is unreliable — unlike the sibling `ErrTooLong` path (diff.go:104-111) which does set `partial=true`, surfaced at main.go:187 area.
- **Blast radius:** Sole caller of parseHunkStart is parseDiffOutput (internal/guard/diff.go:84). Sole caller of parseDiffOutput is ParseStagedDiff (diff.go:39), which is the only diff-parsing entry point used by guard.Run's staged-diff validation path (internal/guard/validate.go) — feeding AddedLine.LineNo into every reported Violation.Line surfaced by `runecho-guard` (cmd/runecho-guard/main.go). Confirmed via grep -rn (no other callers of parseDiffOutput/parseHunkStart in non-test code); codegraph MCP not invoked here since the caller set is small and fully enumerated by grep with high confidence.
- **Fix direction:** Have parseHunkStart return (int, bool) (or an error) so parseDiffOutput can detect the malformed-header case and set partial=true (mirroring the existing ErrTooLong handling) instead of silently trusting a fabricated line-1 fallback.

### F44. `internal/guard/diff.go:144` — parseHunkStart
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** unhandled-postcondition
- **Contract violated:** Function should return the actual new-file start line number parsed from the '@@ -old +new @@' header; on failure it should signal that no valid number could be extracted rather than returning a plausible-looking value.
- **Hypothesis:** Input line '@@ -12,3 +bogus,3 @@' (non-numeric new-count field, e.g. a corrupted or hand-edited diff) makes parseHunkStart return 1 instead of erroring or signaling failure. parseDiffOutput then sets newLineNo=1 for that hunk, so the first added line in the hunk gets AddedLine.LineNo=1 (and subsequent ones 2,3,...) instead of the true line numbers starting near 12 — the guard then reports a violation at line 1 of the file when the actual added code is around line 12.
- **Trace:** Input: line = "@@ -12,3 +bogus,3 @@" (simulating a corrupted/hand-edited diff header).

internal/guard/diff.go:146 `parts := strings.Fields(line)` -> ["@@","-12,3","+bogus,3","@@"]
line 147-148: loop finds p="+bogus,3" (HasPrefix "+", not "+@@")
line 149: seg = "bogus,3" (TrimPrefix "+")
line 150: strings.Cut(seg, ",") -> seg="bogus"
line 151: strconv.Atoi("bogus") -> err != nil, so the `if err == nil { return n }` branch is skipped
loop ends (no other '+'-prefixed field) -> line 157: `return 1`

Caller: internal/guard/diff.go:84 `newLineNo = parseHunkStart(line)` inside parseDiffOutput, then each subsequent '+' line in the hunk gets `AddedLines = append(..., AddedLine{LineNo: newLineNo}); newLineNo++` (lines 90-94).

Predicted wrong output: parseHunkStart returns 1 (same as if the hunk legitimately started at line 1); parseDiffOutput assigns LineNo=1,2,3... to the hunk's added lines instead of ~12,13,14, so a guard violation gets reported at file line 1 instead of the true location near line 12.
Expected/correct behavior: signal failure (e.g. return an error/ok bool, or a sentinel that parseDiffOutput treats as "skip/partial", per the file's own `partial` convention already used elsewhere in this function for other malformed input) rather than returning a value indistinguishable from a valid line-1 hunk.
- **Blast radius:** parseHunkStart has exactly one caller: parseDiffOutput (internal/guard/diff.go:84), which is itself only called from the exported ParseStagedDiff (internal/guard/diff.go:39). ParseStagedDiff has exactly one caller in the repo: cmd/runecho-guard/main.go — i.e. the precommit/hook guard's line-number attribution for every added line in every staged diff it evaluates. A corrupted hunk header (malformed diff, e.g. from a bad merge tool, manual edit, or non-standard git wrapper) causes the guard to misreport the violating line as line 1 of the file for the rest of that hunk.
- **Fix direction:** Change parseHunkStart to return (int, bool) (or a sentinel like -1) so parseDiffOutput can detect the parse failure and either skip the hunk / mark the FileDiff as partial (mirroring the existing `partial` convention already used elsewhere in this function), rather than silently defaulting to a plausible line number.

### F45. `internal/guard/dropped_import.go:112` — firstUnqualifiedUseLines
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** firstUnqualifiedUseLines' invariant (dropped_import.go:107-139, contract's 'invariants' field): 'open is force-reset ... whenever the LineNo sequence is discontinuous' — this reset is the ONLY defense against literal-tracking state bleeding across unrelated hunks. It requires the caller's `lines` to carry real gaps at real boundaries.
- **Hypothesis:** For a MultiEdit tool call with edits [A, B], cmd/runecho-guard/main.go's hookText (main.go:597-614) builds newText by `strings.Join(parts, "\n")` over each edit's NewString, then DroppedImportRefs (dropped_import.go:76) calls `firstUnqualifiedUseLines(lang, TextToAddedLines(newText))`. TextToAddedLines (util.go:11-18) numbers lines 1,2,3,... contiguously by splitting the joined string on "\n" — it has no notion of the real per-edit file positions, so consecutive LineNo values NEVER skip at the A/B join point, and the `open=""` reset at dropped_import.go:112-114 never fires there. Concrete input: edit A's NewString is `DESC = """first line of a multi-line docstring` (a legitimate self-contained replacement of just the opening line of an existing multi-line string whose closing `"""` sits on an untouched line elsewhere in the file — so this edit alone is valid and balanced from the file's real perspective), and edit B's NewString (a different, unrelated hunk in the same MultiEdit call) removes `from ulid import ULID` and elsewhere in the same NewString still calls `ULID()`. Because A's snippet ends with an unterminated triple-quote, stripLiteralsStateful carries `open="\"\"\""` into B's joined snippet with no reset, so B's `ULID()` call is blanked out as 'inside a string literal.' firstUnqualifiedUseLines then returns no entry for "ULID", so at dropped_import.go:78-81 `uses["ULID"]` is 0 and the dropped-import finding for ULID is silently omitted — the exact runtime-breaking bug (NameError from a dropped-but-still-used import) DroppedImportRefs exists to catch is missed for any MultiEdit call where an earlier edit's replacement text ends inside an unterminated string/comment.
- **Trace:** Input (mirrors main.go hookText's MultiEdit join at cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:597-614, strings.Join(parts, "\n") over each edit.NewString):
  editA.NewString = `DESC = """first line of a multi-line docstring`   (valid on its own; closing """ lives untouched elsewhere in the real file)
  editB.NewString = "import os\nresult = ULID()"   (unrelated hunk; drops `from ulid import ULID`, still calls ULID())
  newText = strings.Join([editA, editB], "\n") =
    "DESC = \"\"\"first line of a multi-line docstring\nimport os\nresult = ULID()"

Path:
  cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:493 DroppedImportRefs(lang, oldText, newText)
   -> internal/guard/dropped_import.go:76 uses := firstUnqualifiedUseLines(lang, TextToAddedLines(newText))
      TextToAddedLines (util.go:11-18) numbers the joined text's 3 lines contiguously 1,2,3 — no gap at the A/B boundary (line 2 = "DESC = ..., line 2 = import os, line 3 = result = ULID()"; actual lines: 1="DESC=\"\"\"first line...", 2="import os", 3="result = ULID()")
   -> dropped_import.go:112-114 loop: i=1 (line 2, "import os"): l.LineNo(2) == prevNo(1)+1 -> no reset; i=2 (line 3, "result = ULID()"): l.LineNo(3) == prevNo(2)+1 -> no reset. The `open=""` reset NEVER fires because LineNo is contiguous end-to-end across the synthetic join.
   -> dropped_import.go:116 stripLiteralsStateful carries open="\"\"\"" from line 1 into lines 2 and 3, blanking "import os" and "result = ULID()" as string-literal content.
   -> dropped_import.go:133 uses map never gets an "ULID" entry.
  Back in DroppedImportRefs (dropped_import.go:78-81): uses["ULID"] == 0 -> ULID is silently dropped from the `dropped` findings.

Predicted wrong output: DroppedImportRefs returns [] (no ULID finding).
Expected/correct output: DroppedImportRefs should return [{Name: "ULID", LineNo: 3}] since ULID is imported in oldText, not re-imported/rebound in newText, and still called unqualified in newText.
- **Blast radius:** Single call site: cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:493 (guard.DroppedImportRefs), invoked from the PreToolUse MultiEdit handling path for Python/JS files (hookText's MultiEdit branch at main.go:597-614 is the only path that synthetically joins multiple edits' NewString without real line-number gaps). No other callers of DroppedImportRefs or firstUnqualifiedUseLines exist in the repo (grep confirmed). Impact: any MultiEdit tool call with ≥2 edits where an earlier edit's NewString ends inside an unterminated string/comment causes the dropped-import guard to silently miss a real dropped-but-still-used import in a later, unrelated edit within the same call — exactly the runtime NameError class this guard exists to catch.
- **Fix direction:** In hookText's MultiEdit branch (main.go), join edits with a sentinel that forces a real LineNo discontinuity per edit (e.g. build each edit's AddedLines independently with a synthetic gap, or number lines with a jump between edits) instead of a plain "\n" string join fed through TextToAddedLines' contiguous 1,2,3... numbering — restoring the reset condition at dropped_import.go:112-114.

### F46. `internal/guard/dropped_import.go:190` — locallyBoundNames
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** postconditions: 'Returns the set of identifiers that appear in any recognized binding-target position... Python: ...def-parameter list (181-192)'
- **Hypothesis:** For oldText 'from lib import y\nprint(y)\n' and newText 'def foo(\n    y,\n):\n    return y\n', rePyDefParams (`^\s*(?:async\s+)?def\s+\w+\s*\(([^)]*)\)`) requires both the opening and closing parens on the same physical line. Because locallyBoundNames processes text line-by-line via TextToAddedLines with no cross-line state, the multi-line signature's first line 'def foo(' has no closing paren and never matches, and the continuation line '    y,' doesn't start with 'def' either, so "y" is never added to bound. DroppedImportRefs(LangPython, oldText, newText) returns [{Name:y, LineNo:4}], a false-positive dropped-import finding on code where "y" is a normal (PEP8-style multi-line) function parameter, not a lingering use of the deleted import. Verified by direct execution: DroppedImportRefs returns exactly that non-empty result.
- **Trace:** Input: oldText = "from lib import y\nprint(y)\n", newText = "def foo(\n    y,\n):\n    return y\n" (lang=LangPython).

Path: DroppedImportRefs (dropped_import.go:32) computes oldImps={y} (from `from lib import y`), newImps={} (no import line survives). It then calls bound := locallyBoundNames(LangPython, newText) (line 50).

locallyBoundNames (line 167) iterates TextToAddedLines(newText) one line at a time with no cross-line state:
- line1 "def foo(" — rePyDefParams = `^\s*(?:async\s+)?def\s+\w+\s*\(([^)]*)\)` requires a closing `)` on the same line; "def foo(" has none, so no match. "y" is not added.
- line2 "    y,": doesn't start with "def", rePyDefParams doesn't match; assignLHS/rePyForTarget/reAsBind/reWalrus also don't match a bare "y,". "y" not added here either.
- line3 "):" and line4 "    return y": no binding regex matches.
Result: bound = {} (empty) — "y" never gets locally bound.

Back in DroppedImportRefs (line 60-68): for name="y" in oldImps, newImps["y"] doesn't exist (still dropped-worthy), bound["y"] doesn't exist → dropped=["y"].
firstUnqualifiedUseLines then finds "y" first unqualified use — line 2 ("    y,", not an import line, not qualified) → uses["y"]=2.
Final: out = [{Name:"y", LineNo:2}].

Predicted (hypothesis) output: [{Name:y, LineNo:4}]. Actual executed output: [{Name:"y", LineNo:2}] — same false-positive class (non-empty dropped-import finding on a legitimate multi-line def parameter), but the specific LineNo differs (2, the parameter line, not 4, the return line) because firstUnqualifiedUseLines reports the FIRST unqualified use, which is the parameter-list line itself, not the return statement. The core defect — locallyBoundNames' line-by-line regex cannot see across the multi-line def signature, so a valid PEP8 multi-line parameter is misclassified as a lingering use of a dropped import — is confirmed exactly as hypothesized.</trace>
<parameter name="evidence">Command: go test ./internal/guard/ -run TestFocusVerify_PyDefParamsMultiline -v
Output:
=== RUN   TestFocusVerify_PyDefParamsMultiline
DroppedImportRefs result: []guard.DroppedImport{guard.DroppedImport{Name:"y", LineNo:2}}
    zz_focus_verify_pydefparams_test.go:14: FALSE POSITIVE REPRODUCED: []guard.DroppedImport{guard.DroppedImport{Name:"y", LineNo:2}}
--- PASS: TestFocusVerify_PyDefParamsMultiline (0.00s)
PASS
ok  	github.com/inth3shadows/runecho/internal/guard	0.006s

Scratch file internal/guard/zz_focus_verify_pydefparams_test.go was created for this repro and deleted afterward; `git status --porcelain | grep -v '^??'` and `git diff --stat` show no tracked-file changes (only pre-existing unrelated untracked scratch files from other sessions remain, none touched by this verification).
- **Blast radius:** DroppedImportRefs is called from cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:493 (`droppedImps = guard.DroppedImportRefs(lang, oldText, text)`), which is the live runecho-guard hook invoked on every Python/JS Edit/MultiEdit — so any multi-line `def` signature (or any other multi-line binding form the regexes assume is single-line) whose parameter name matches a just-removed import name will surface as a spurious "dropped import" guard finding in real editing sessions, on legitimate PEP8-style code.
- **Fix direction:** Give locallyBoundNames real cross-line state for the Python def-params case (e.g., accumulate lines from a `def ...(` that lacks a matching `)` until one closes, then run rePyDefParams/reIdentAll over the joined signature) instead of matching rePyDefParams against a single physical line.

### F47. `internal/guard/extract.go:740` — stripLiteralsStateful
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** postcondition: "A single-line `\"`/`'` string can never leave open set — per the docstring these 'do not span lines' — an unterminated one just blanks to EOL."
- **Hypothesis:** JS added-line 1 `var s = "Hello \` (backslash-newline is a valid ECMAScript LineContinuation inside a string literal) followed by added-line 2 `World"); realCall();`. On line 1, the backslash is the last byte (i+1==n), so the `b[i]=='\\' && i+1<n` escape branch is never taken; the code falls into the default `out[i]=' '` path, the for-loop exits at EOL, and the function returns with `open` unchanged ("") instead of signaling an in-progress string. ExtractRefs then processes line 2 with open=="", treating `World` as bare code (harmless here) but then hitting the `"` — which is actually the string's real closing quote — and (mis)treating it as a brand-new string opener with no lang/isFStringPrefix gate for JS. That new 'string' has no second `"` before EOL, so the scanner blanks everything after it to end of line, including `realCall();`. `realCall` is a genuine call and is silently erased from `scan`, so reCallIdent never sees it — a false negative in exactly the class (silently missed hallucinated call) the function's own design doc says is the worst outcome to avoid.
- **Trace:** internal/guard/extract.go, single-line `"`/`'` handling at lines 737-753:
```
quote := c
i++
for i < n && b[i] != quote {
    if b[i] == '\\' && i+1 < n {   // line 740
        out[i] = ' '; i++; out[i] = ' '; i++
        continue
    }
    out[i] = ' '; i++
}
if i < n && b[i] == quote { i++ }
```

Input (JS, two consecutive AddedLines):
  line 1 (LineNo=1): `var s = "Hello \`   (trailing backslash is the LAST byte, i+1==n)
  line 2 (LineNo=2): `World"); realCall();`

Path:
1. Line 1 → stripLiteralsStateful(LangJS, line1, open=""). At the '\\' before EOL, `i+1<n` is false (i+1==n), so the escape branch (line 740) is skipped; falls to the default case `out[i]=' '; i++` (line 747-748), then `i==n`, outer `for i<n` (line 739) exits. `if i<n && b[i]==quote` (line 750) is false. Function returns `(out, open)` with `open` UNCHANGED = "" — the in-progress string is not signaled to the caller, contra the intended "unterminated single-line string blanks to EOL" contract which still requires distinguishing "genuinely closed" from "not closed."
   Actual: scan1 = `var s = "       ` (7 chars after `"` blanked, backslash blanked too), open1 = "".
2. Line 2 → stripLiteralsStateful(LangJS, line2, open=""). Since open=="", the continuation branch (line 566) is skipped. Scanner treats `World` as bare code (harmless), then hits `"` at index 5 — actually the real string's closing quote — and (mis)opens it as a brand-new single-quote string (line 686, JS has no isFStringPrefix gate). No second `"` appears before EOL, so the single-line handler blanks index 5 through EOL, erasing `); realCall();` entirely.
   Actual: scan2 = `World"              ` (everything after the misidentified opening quote, including `realCall();`, replaced with spaces).
3. ExtractRefs (extract.go:456) runs `reCallIdent.FindAllStringSubmatchIndex` against `scan2` — `realCall(` no longer exists in the blanked text, so no Ref is produced for line 2.

Predicted wrong output: `refs` contains no `Ref{Name:"realCall", LineNo:2}`.
Expected/correct output: `refs` should contain `Ref{Name:"realCall", LineNo:2}` (it is a genuine call).
- **Blast radius:** ExtractRefs is called from internal/guard/validate.go:77 (guard.ValidateFileDiffs — the pre-commit/pre-push hallucinated-call guard) and internal/ir/generator.go:523 (guard.TextToAddedLines feed into IR reference indexing). Any JS diff containing a backslash-newline inside a single-quoted/double-quoted string literal (a valid ECMAScript LineContinuation) will silently drop all calls made on the line where the string actually closes — a false negative in the exact "silently missed hallucinated call" class the guard exists to prevent.
- **Fix direction:** In the single-line `"`/`'` branch (extract.go:737-753), when the loop exits because `i==n` without finding the closing quote (i.e., the string was not actually terminated on this line, including the backslash-at-EOL case), return `open` set to a sentinel like `string(quote)` instead of leaving it as the incoming `open` unchanged, so the next line's stripLiteralsStateful call knows it's still inside a single-line string and blanks through to the real closing quote instead of reopening at it.

### F48. `internal/guardstats/guardstats.go:36` — Load/LoadReader
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** unhandled-postcondition
- **Contract violated:** LoadReader's postcondition: on a non-EOF read error it returns (out, error) where out is the partial slice of already-decoded Decisions accumulated before the failure — callers that do `if err != nil { return err }` without inspecting `out` silently discard already-decoded records.
- **Hypothesis:** In cmd/runecho-ir/guardstats.go runGuardStats (line 36), `decisions, err := guardstats.Load(path)` is followed by `if err != nil { if os.IsNotExist(err) {...}; return printErr(err) }` (lines 37-43) — this discards the `decisions` return value entirely on any non-IsNotExist error. Given a decisions.jsonl where the first N lines parse successfully and a later read fails with a genuine I/O error (not JSON/ts malformation, which LoadReader already tolerates, but e.g. a transient disk read error or a reader that returns io.ErrUnexpectedEOF partway through), Load returns (N valid Decisions, err). runGuardStats then calls printErr(err) and exits with a nonzero code, producing NO guard-stats report at all, when the postcondition-documented partial-success contract would allow it to still run Aggregate over the N decisions already parsed and print a report covering the readable prefix of the log.
- **Trace:** Input: io.Reader emitting 3x `{"v":1,"ts":"2026-07-01T00:00:00Z","mode":"guard","decision":"ask","symbols":["Foo"]}\n` then a Read() returning (0, errBoom) where errBoom is a non-EOF sentinel error.
Path: LoadReader (internal/guardstats/guardstats.go:61) loop -> br.ReadString('\n') succeeds 3x, json.Unmarshal+time.Parse succeed each time, out grows to len 3 -> 4th ReadString call returns readErr=errBoom (not io.EOF) -> line 87-89: `if readErr != nil { if readErr == io.EOF {...}; return out, fmt.Errorf("scan decision log: %w", readErr) }` -> returns (out=[3 Decisions], err=wrapped errBoom).
Load (line 96-103): `f, err := os.Open(path); ...; return LoadReader(f)` -> same tuple propagates unchanged for a real file whose Read() fails transiently mid-stream.
runGuardStats (cmd/runecho-ir/guardstats.go:36-43): `decisions, err := guardstats.Load(path)` binds decisions=[3 Decisions], err=non-nil, non-IsNotExist -> `if err != nil { if os.IsNotExist(err) {...(false)...}; return printErr(err) }` -> function returns immediately; `decisions` variable is never read again.
Predicted wrong output: guard-stats subcommand prints only an error and exits nonzero, producing NO report, despite 3 valid decisions being decoded.
Expected (postcondition-honoring) output: a report (via Aggregate/Format) computed over the 3 readable decisions, with a diagnostic note about the truncated tail.
Actual observed output (via direct execution of the real LoadReader, the exact function whose contract is in question): err=scan decision log: simulated transient disk read error, len(out)=3 — matches the predicted defect exactly.
- **Blast radius:** Single call site: runGuardStats (cmd/runecho-ir/guardstats.go:36), the entire `runecho-ir guard-stats` subcommand. Any transient/partial read failure in decisions.jsonl (mid-file I/O error, not a JSON/ts malformation which LoadReader already tolerates, and not file-not-found) causes the subcommand to print an error and exit nonzero with zero report output, instead of reporting over the readable prefix as LoadReader's postcondition allows.
- **Fix direction:** In runGuardStats, when err != nil and !os.IsNotExist(err), still run Aggregate/Format over the returned `decisions` (if non-empty) and print the report plus a stderr warning noting the log was read only partially, rather than discarding `decisions` and returning printErr(err) unconditionally.

### F49. `internal/guardstats/guardstats.go:46` — Aggregate
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** unhandled-postcondition
- **Contract violated:** Aggregate's precondition: topN negative disables truncation entirely (line 202 `topN >= 0` guard), 0 yields an empty TopSymbols, positive caps it — this negative-value special case is not surfaced anywhere in the CLI's flag documentation.
- **Hypothesis:** cmd/runecho-ir/guardstats.go defines `top := fs.Int("top", 10, "number of top flagged symbols to show")` (line 20) with no lower-bound validation (only `*days <= 0` is checked at line 25), then passes `*top` straight into `guardstats.Aggregate(decisions, since, *top)` (line 46). Running `runecho-ir guard-stats --top=-1` (a plausible typo for 'no limit' or an off-by-one from '--top=1') silently switches Aggregate into unbounded mode, printing every distinct flagged symbol instead of the flag's documented 'top N' semantics, with no warning that a negative value means something categorically different from a small positive one.
- **Trace:** Input: 5 ask-decisions each flagging one distinct symbol (Alpha..Echo), since = now-24h.
Path: cmd/runecho-ir/guardstats.go:20 top=fs.Int(...) [no bound check, only *days checked at :25] -> :46 guardstats.Aggregate(decisions, since, *top) -> guardstats.go:139 Aggregate(decisions, since, topN=-1) -> loop :150-190 builds symbolCounts{Alpha:1,...,Echo:1} -> :192-201 sorted into 5 SymbolCount entries -> :202 `if topN >= 0 && len(symbols) > topN` evaluates false because topN(-1) >= 0 is false -> truncation branch (:203) skipped entirely -> :205 s.TopSymbols = all 5 entries.
Predicted wrong output (per hypothesis): TopSymbols contains all 5 symbols instead of being empty/small, with no warning distinguishing this from documented "top N" semantics.
Actual output (executed): topN=-1 -> len(TopSymbols)=5 (all symbols): [{Alpha 1} {Bravo 1} {Charlie 1} {Delta 1} {Echo 1}]. Contrast run topN=2 -> len=2: [{Alpha 1} {Bravo 1}], confirming the documented "top N" path works normally and only the negative case silently switches behavior.
- **Blast radius:** Single caller: cmd/runecho-ir/guardstats.go:46 (`runGuardStats`), the only production call site of guardstats.Aggregate (verified via `grep -rn "guardstats.Aggregate"` across the repo, excluding tests — one match). Impact is confined to the `runecho-ir guard-stats` CLI subcommand's `--top` flag; no other caller or internal consumer exists.
- **Fix direction:** In cmd/runecho-ir/guardstats.go, either reject negative `*top` alongside the existing `*days <= 0` validation (simplest — matches the days precedent) or, if unbounded-via-negative is intentionally kept as a power-user escape hatch, document it explicitly in the flag's usage string (e.g. `"number of top flagged symbols to show (negative = show all)"`).

### F50. `internal/guardstats/guardstats.go:46` — Aggregate
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** Aggregate precondition/behavior: topN < 0 means 'unlimited' (checked via `topN >= 0` at line 202); topN == 0 yields an empty TopSymbols slice. Nothing in Aggregate validates topN, so it is entirely the caller's job to enforce sane input.
- **Hypothesis:** runGuardStats validates `*days` (`if *days <= 0 { ...Usage error... }` at line 25-28) but performs no equivalent validation on `*top` before calling `guardstats.Aggregate(decisions, since, *top)` at line 46. Running `runecho-ir guard-stats --top=-1` sets topN=-1, which flows straight into Aggregate; the `topN >= 0` guard at guardstats.go:202 is false, so the truncation `symbols = symbols[:topN]` is skipped entirely and every flagged symbol is returned instead of being limited (or rejected), contradicting the flag's documented purpose ('number of top flagged symbols to show') which gives no indication that a negative value silently means 'show all'.
- **Trace:** Input: `runecho-ir guard-stats --top=-1` -&gt; cmd/runecho-ir/guardstats.go:20 `top := fs.Int("top", 10, ...)` sets *top=-1 with no guard (only `*days` is checked at line 25-28) -&gt; line 46 `stats := guardstats.Aggregate(decisions, since, *top)` passes topN=-1 into internal/guardstats/guardstats.go -&gt; guardstats.go:139 `func Aggregate(decisions []Decision, since time.Time, topN int) Stats` -&gt; symbolCounts built normally (lines 148-190) -&gt; line 202 `if topN >= 0 && len(symbols) > topN {` evaluates to `false` (since -1 >= 0 is false) -&gt; truncation at line 203 `symbols = symbols[:topN]` is SKIPPED -&gt; line 205 `s.TopSymbols = symbols` retains ALL symbols, unbounded.

Predicted wrong output: with 5 distinct flagged symbols and topN=-1, TopSymbols has length 5 (unlimited), not length 0/negative/error as the flag's stated purpose ("number of top flagged symbols to show") would imply for an invalid/negative count.
Expected (if validated like --days): either a Usage error before reaching Aggregate, or truncation to empty/rejected input — not silent full-list passthrough.
- **Blast radius:** grep -rn "guardstats.Aggregate|runGuardStats" across the repo (excluding tests) shows exactly one call site: cmd/runecho-ir/main.go:73 invokes runGuardStats(os.Args[2:]) for the `guard-stats` subcommand, which is the only caller of guardstats.Aggregate. Blast radius is the single user-facing CLI command `runecho-ir guard-stats --top=&lt;N&gt;` — a negative --top silently dumps every flagged symbol instead of erroring or limiting, which could be surprising/noisy output but is not a crash or data-corruption risk (Aggregate itself remains correct per its own contract; the gap is purely in caller-side input validation).
- **Fix direction:** Add a guard in runGuardStats (cmd/runecho-ir/guardstats.go) analogous to the *days check, e.g. `if *top &lt; 0 { fmt.Fprintln(os.Stderr, "Usage: ... (--top must be >= 0)"); return ExitError }`, before line 46.

### F51. `internal/guardstats/guardstats.go:52` — LoadReader
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** Docstring (line 51-52): "...one longer than bufio.Scanner's fixed token cap is skipped, not treated as an error"
- **Hypothesis:** LoadReader(r) where r yields one JSONL line of ~100KB (exceeding bufio.Scanner's default 64KB MaxScanTokenSize) containing valid JSON with a valid RFC3339 `ts` field SHOULD, per the docstring's literal claim, skip that line and return it absent from the output slice. It ACTUALLY returns a []Decision containing that record fully decoded, because the function was deliberately rewritten to use bufio.Reader.ReadString (which grows its buffer without a size cap) instead of bufio.Scanner specifically so oversized lines are NOT skipped — the docstring still describes Scanner's discarded failure mode as if it applies to this implementation.
- **Trace:** Input: one JSONL line = {"v":1,"ts":"2026-07-01T00:00:00Z","mode":"guard","repo":"r","file":"f.go","lang":"go","decision":"ask","reason":"<100KB of 'x'>","symbols":["a"]}\n  — total line length 102,533 bytes, vs bufio.MaxScanTokenSize = 65,536 bytes.

Path: LoadReader(r) [guardstats.go:62] -> br := bufio.NewReader(r) [64] -> loop: line, readErr := br.ReadString('\n') [66] reads the full 102,533-byte line (ReadString grows its internal buffer, no cap) -> line = strings.TrimSuffix(...) [67] -> line != "" true [68] -> json.Unmarshal succeeds (valid JSON) [70] -> time.Parse(RFC3339, "2026-07-01T00:00:00Z") succeeds [71] -> Decision appended to out [72-81] -> next ReadString returns io.EOF [85-86] -> return out, nil [87].

Predicted-per-docstring output: out = [] (line skipped for exceeding Scanner's cap).
Actual output: out = [Decision{Mode:"guard", Repo:"r", Decision:"ask", TS:2026-07-01 00:00:00 UTC, ...}] — len(out) == 1.
- **Blast radius:** grep -rn "guardstats.LoadReader\|guardstats.Load(" shows the only callers are guardstats.Load (guardstats.go:103, a thin wrapper) and the guard-stats CLI subcommand (cmd/runecho-ir) that calls guardstats.Load to build the aggregated report. No caller relies on oversized-line skipping; the defect is purely a documentation/contract-vs-implementation mismatch, not a crash or data-corruption path — impact is that anyone reading the docstring to reason about report completeness/large-record safety is misled into thinking huge lines are silently dropped when they are actually fully included (and, since ReadString is uncapped, a maliciously/accidentally huge single line can grow the read buffer unbounded — no size ceiling at all).
- **Fix direction:** Update the doc comment (guardstats.go:51-53) to say a malformed line or one with an unparseable ts is skipped, and drop/replace the Scanner-cap clause with an accurate statement that ReadString imposes no size limit so oversized-but-valid lines are still decoded (optionally note the resulting unbounded-memory tradeoff instead of a nonexistent skip behavior).

### F52. `internal/guardstats/guardstats.go:66` — LoadReader
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** Docstring (lines 51-53): "one longer than bufio.Scanner's fixed token cap is skipped, not treated as an error"
- **Hypothesis:** Given a JSONL line over 64KB (bufio.Scanner's default MaxScanTokenSize) that is otherwise well-formed JSON with a valid RFC3339 ts field (e.g. an 'ask' decision whose Symbols array is huge), the docstring says this record is skipped/dropped like a malformed line; the implementation instead uses bufio.Reader.ReadString, which has no size limit, so the line is parsed successfully and the Decision IS appended to the returned slice — the exact opposite of the documented behavior. Only JSON-unmarshal failures and bad timestamps are actually skipped; line length never causes a skip.
- **Trace:** Input: one JSONL line, 450,137 bytes (> bufio.Scanner's 65536-byte default MaxScanTokenSize), well-formed JSON: {"v":1,"ts":"2026-07-04T00:00:00Z","mode":"ask","repo":"r","file":"f.go","lang":"go","decision":"ask","reason":"unresolved","symbols":[...10000 entries...]}.

Path through internal/guardstats/guardstats.go:
- L64 br := bufio.NewReader(r)
- L66 line, readErr := br.ReadString('\n')  -> reads the entire 450,137-byte line in one call; ReadString has no size cap, so readErr == nil (full line, trailing \n present)
- L67 TrimSuffix removes trailing \n
- L68 line != "" -> true
- L70 json.Unmarshal([]byte(line), &raw) -> err == nil (valid JSON)
- L71 time.Parse(time.RFC3339, raw.TS) -> err == nil (valid ts "2026-07-04T00:00:00Z")
- L72-81 Decision{...} appended to out
- L85-90 next ReadString returns io.EOF -> return out, nil

Predicted WRONG output per docstring (lines 51-53): len(out) == 0 (oversized line silently skipped, same treatment as a malformed line).
Actual output observed: len(out) == 1, with the full 10000-element Symbols slice intact — the record was parsed and kept, not skipped.
- **Blast radius:** Only one non-test caller of guardstats.Load/LoadReader in the whole repo: cmd/runecho-ir/guardstats.go:36 (the `runecho-ir guard-stats` CLI subcommand added in PR #100, per grep -rn "guardstats\.\(Load\|LoadReader\)" excluding _test.go). Effect there: an oversized ask/defer record (e.g. an "ask" with a very large Symbols array) is retained and folded into the aggregated report (ByRepo/ByLang counts, TopSymbols ranking, DeferReasons) instead of being silently dropped — which is actually the intended fail-open behavior per the code comment, just not what the opening docstring sentence says.
- **Fix direction:** Edit the doc comment on LoadReader (guardstats.go lines 51-53): drop "or one longer than bufio.Scanner's fixed token cap" from the skip-list and instead state that oversized lines are handled in full (no length limit) via bufio.Reader.ReadString, consistent with the rationale already given two paragraphs later (lines 58-61) — a doc fix, not a code fix.

### F53. `internal/guardstats/guardstats.go:151` — Aggregate
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** Docstring (lines 137-138): "'outcome' and 'refresh' (mode 'e6') records are excluded — a different signal, not what this report covers."
- **Hypothesis:** Aggregate(decisions=[]Decision{{TS: since, Mode: "e6", Decision: "ask", Repo: "foo", Symbols: []string{"Bar"}}}, since, topN) SHOULD exclude this record entirely per the docstring's stated mode-e6 exclusion, producing TotalAsk=0 and an empty ByRepo. It ACTUALLY computes TotalAsk=1, ByRepo["foo"]=Counts{Ask:1}, and TopSymbols=[{Bar,1}], because the filter at line 151 only checks d.Decision ("ask"/"defer") and never inspects d.Mode — any record whose Mode happens to be "e6" but whose Decision field is "ask" or "defer" is silently counted, contradicting the documented exclusion.
- **Trace:** Input: Aggregate([]Decision{{TS: since, Mode: "e6", Decision: "ask", Repo: "foo", Symbols: []string{"Bar"}}}, since, 10)
Path: line 150 (for _, d := range decisions) -> line 151 (if d.Decision != "ask" && d.Decision != "defer" { continue }) — d.Decision=="ask" so condition is false, no continue; d.Mode is never read anywhere in the loop -> line 154 (d.TS.Before(since) is false since TS==since) -> line 158 (switch d.Decision) -> case "ask" (line 159): s.TotalAsk++ (line 160) -> s.ByRepo["foo"].Ask++ (lines 161-165) -> symbolCounts["Bar"]++ (lines 171-173) -> sorted into s.TopSymbols.
Predicted wrong output (per hypothesis): TotalAsk=1, ByRepo["foo"]=Counts{Ask:1}, TopSymbols=[{Bar,1}].
Expected correct output per docstring (lines 137-138): TotalAsk=0, ByRepo empty, TopSymbols empty (record should be excluded because Mode=="e6").
- **Blast radius:** grep -rn "guardstats.Aggregate" shows the sole caller is cmd/runecho-ir's guard-stats subcommand (added in commit 0f2449c per recent history), which feeds Aggregate's output directly into the CLI report/JSON output — so any decisions.jsonl containing e6 (auto-fresh-IR refresh) records with decision "ask"/"defer" pollutes the guard-stats report's totals, per-repo/per-lang counts, and top-symbols ranking, silently contradicting the documented exclusion and issue #87's parser-gap signal intent.
- **Fix direction:** Add a mode-exclusion check in the loop, e.g. `if d.Mode == "e6" { continue }` (or an explicit allowlist of expected modes) immediately alongside the existing d.Decision filter at line 151.

### F54. `internal/guardstats/guardstats.go:171` — Aggregate
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** impossible-state
- **Contract violated:** Aggregate's postcondition states TopSymbols ranks 'the topN most-frequently-flagged symbols... from ask records' Symbols field' — read naturally this means frequency across distinct ask events (how many times has this symbol been flagged), matching the doc's framing of a per-decision 'flag'.
- **Hypothesis:** Aggregate assumes each entry in a single Decision's Symbols slice represents a distinct flagged occurrence, but the only real producer (cmd/runecho-guard/main.go lines 520-551) builds `syms` by unconditionally concatenating four independent, non-deduplicated categories: violations (line 529: `syms = append(syms, v.Symbol)`), dangling (536), droppedImps (543), and duplicates (550). If the same symbol name legitimately shows up in two of these categories within one edit (e.g. a hunk that both references an unresolved symbol `Bar` AND removes an unrelated-but-same-named `Bar` still referenced elsewhere, or a symbol that is both a dangling reference and a duplicate-definition hit), the single logged ask decision has Symbols=["Bar","Bar"]. In Aggregate's loop `for _, sym := range d.Symbols { symbolCounts[sym]++ }` (lines 171-173), this increments symbolCounts["Bar"] by 2 from ONE ask event. stats.TopSymbols then reports {Name:"Bar", Count:2} — indistinguishable from a symbol that was actually flagged across two separate ask decisions/edits — silently inflating its rank in the top-flagged-symbols report relative to symbols that only ever appear once per array.
- **Trace:** Input: two ask Decisions passed to Aggregate (internal/guardstats/guardstats.go):
  d1 = {Decision:"ask", Symbols:["Bar","Bar"]}  // simulates one hunk where "Bar" is both a dangling ref (line 536: syms=append(syms,d.Symbol)) and a duplicate-definition hit (line 550: syms=append(syms,d.Symbol)) in the same edit
  d2 = {Decision:"ask", Symbols:["Foo"]}         // a separate ask event flagging "Foo" once

Path: Aggregate loop at line ~170: `case "ask": ... for _, sym := range d.Symbols { symbolCounts[sym]++ }` (lines 170-172).
  - Processing d1: symbolCounts["Bar"] incremented twice (171->172 twice) -> symbolCounts["Bar"]=2, from ONE ask event.
  - Processing d2: symbolCounts["Foo"] incremented once -> symbolCounts["Foo"]=1.
Then symbols built into []SymbolCount and sorted by Count desc, Name asc (lines ~189-196).

Predicted wrong output: TopSymbols = [{Bar,2},{Foo,1}] — Bar outranks Foo even though both were flagged by exactly one ask event each; Bar's rank inflation comes purely from intra-event duplicate array entries, indistinguishable from being flagged across two separate ask decisions.
Expected (per-ask-event / "flag frequency") output if de-duplicated within each Decision's Symbols: {Bar,1} and {Foo,1} tied.

Actual observed output matches the predicted wrong output exactly.
- **Blast radius:** Only one real caller: cmd/runecho-ir/guardstats.go:46 (`guardstats.Aggregate(decisions, since, *top)`), which feeds the `runecho-ir guard-stats` CLI subcommand's TopSymbols report — the only consumer of this output is that CLI's human-facing "most-frequently-flagged symbols" table.
- **Fix direction:** De-duplicate each Decision's Symbols slice before incrementing (e.g. `for _, sym := range uniqueStrings(d.Symbols) { symbolCounts[sym]++ }`, or increment via a per-decision `map[string]bool` seen-set) so each ask event contributes at most one count per symbol name.

### F55. `internal/ir/generator.go:280` — UpdateCtx
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** unhandled-postcondition
- **Contract violated:** The Stats type's SupportedSeen/ParseErrors/Indexed fields are documented as an 'honest-coverage' triple where every SupportedSeen file is accounted for by either landing in Indexed or being counted in ParseErrors (generator.go:78-83). Callers cmd/runecho-ir/repo.go:122-138 ('runecho-ir repo list') and internal/mcp/tools_oracle.go:463-478 (status tool) render ParseErrors and Coverage side by side as if `100% - coverage% == ParseErrors/SupportedSeen`, i.e. they consume ParseErrors as the complete explanation for any coverage shortfall.
- **Hypothesis:** Run `runecho-ir repo reindex <name>` on a repo where one previously-hashed file becomes unreadable between the os.Stat size-check and HashFile call (e.g. permission changed, or the file is deleted mid-walk after the stat but before the hash read) — generator.go:280-284 hits the HashFile error branch, warns, and `return nil`s without incrementing stats.ParseErrors, while stats.SupportedSeen was already incremented at line 266. `runecho-ir repo list` then shows ERRORS unchanged from before but COVER dropped below 100%, with no ParseErrors entry accounting for the missing file — an operator following the documented ERRORS/COVER relationship undercounts the true failure and cannot find which file silently vanished from the IR.
- **Trace:** Concrete input: a temp dir with two Go files, good.go and bad.go, both initially readable. Call g.Generate(dir) to build an initial IR (both indexed, stats {SupportedSeen:2, Indexed:2, ParseErrors:0}). Then chmod bad.go to 0000 (unreadable, confirmed non-root uid=1000 ericm so this genuinely blocks read) and call g.UpdateCtx(ctx, initialIR, dir).

Path: UpdateCtx -> walkSourceFiles visits bad.go -> callback (generator.go:265) stats.SupportedSeen++ (now 2) -> line 267 cap not reached -> line 275 os.Stat succeeds (chmod doesn't change size, size <= maxParseBytes) so the size-guard branch is skipped -> line 280 HashFile(absPath) -> hasher.go:19 os.Open fails with "permission denied" -> line 281 err != nil -> line 282 g.warn(...) -> line 283 return nil. stats.ParseErrors is NOT incremented on this path (compare to the sibling error branches at 277 and 292 which both do `stats.ParseErrors++`). bad.go is never written into updated.Files.

Predicted wrong output: stats.SupportedSeen=2, stats.Indexed=1, stats.ParseErrors=0 (2 != 1+0), bad.go absent from updated.Files.
Expected/correct output per the documented contract: SupportedSeen should equal Indexed+ParseErrors, i.e. ParseErrors should be 1.
- **Blast radius:** grep confirmed both documented callers consume the same Stats fields directly from UpdateCtx's return value: cmd/runecho-ir/repo.go:132-138 (`runecho-ir repo list`, prints r.ParseErrors and a Coverage-derived `cover` string side by side) and internal/mcp/tools_oracle.go:463-478 (status tool, emits `parse_errors` and `coverage_percent` as sibling fields). repo.go:263 also persists stats.ParseErrors/stats.SupportedSeen via db.TouchRepo, so the undercount is durably stored, not just a transient print — any downstream snapshot/history query built on repo table stats inherits the gap.
- **Fix direction:** Add `stats.ParseErrors++` in the HashFile-error branch (generator.go:281-283), mirroring the size-guard and parseFile-error branches, so every SupportedSeen file that doesn't land in Indexed is accounted for in ParseErrors.

Actual: SupportedSeen=10, Indexed=9, ParseErrors=0 — the missing file is invisible to Stats, so Coverage() and any caller computing 'files skipped due to error' as SupportedSeen-Indexed-ParseErrors get 0 instead of 1.

- **Fix direction:** In generator.go's HashFile-error branch (lines 280-284), add `stats.ParseErrors++` before `return nil`, mirroring the oversized-file guard (line 277) and the parseFile-failure branch (line 292).

### F57. `internal/ir/generator.go:337` — UpdateFile
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: REFUTED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** unhandled-postcondition
- **Contract violated:** UpdateFile's postcondition guarantees error is always nil (every one of its 8 return statements passes nil), yet the caller in cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:337 branches on `err != nil` to decide the 'update-fail' outcome.
- **Hypothesis:** Call refreshIRForFile on an enrolled repo whose existing IR is version-current, where the just-edited file has a syntax error that makes parseFile fail (e.g. an in-progress multi-edit leaves the file momentarily unparseable): gen.UpdateFile returns (existing, false, nil) per its 'parse failed — keep the prior entry' branch (generator.go:361-363). Because err is nil, the `err != nil` check at main.go:337 never fires, so 'update-fail' is dead/unreachable code and this genuine failure is instead funneled into the `if !changed` branch at line 340, which returns "unchanged" — indistinguishable in the RUNECHO_DEBUG trace from a truly no-op edit, and the stale pre-edit IR/snapshot is silently kept.
- **Trace:** Input: root = tmp dir; main.go initially "package main\n\nfunc Foo() {}\n"; gen := NewGenerator(...); existing, _, _ := gen.Generate(root) (baseline IR, Version==IRVersion==6, contains main.go).
Edit: main.go rewritten to add `func Bar() {}` (a real, meaningful structural change).
Force failure: gen.maxParseBytes = len(edited)-1, so info.Size() > g.maxParseBytes inside parseFile (generator.go:431-433) is true.
Call: updated, changed, err := gen.UpdateFile(existing, root, filePath)
Path: generator.go:316 entry -> 317 existing.Version==IRVersion so no early return -> 320-333 path resolution succeeds (file is inside root) -> 337-340 files map copied -> 342 os.Stat succeeds, not a stat error -> 352 not a dir, g.supportsExtension(".go")==true -> 359 default branch: g.parseFile(absFile) called -> inside parseFile, os.Stat succeeds, info.Size() (46 bytes) > g.maxParseBytes (45) -> parseFile returns (FileIR{}, fmt.Errorf("skipping oversized file...")) -> back in UpdateFile line 360: perr != nil is true -> line 362: `return existing, false, nil`.
Actual output: updated == existing (same pointer, stale IR still has only Foo, not Bar), changed == false, err == nil.
Predicted wrong output (per claim): err is nil despite a genuine parse failure, so main.go:337's `err != nil` check never fires; execution instead falls into `if !changed { return "unchanged" }` at line 340 — confirmed structurally (only one caller exists and its logic is exactly this).
- **Blast radius:** Single production caller: cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:337, inside refreshIRForFile — the PostToolUse auto-fresh-IR hook (`grep -rn "\.UpdateFile(" --include="*.go" | grep -v _test.go` returns exactly this one call site). Impact is scoped to the guard hook's dogfood trace/telemetry and to the IR staying stale on a real parse failure during an edit; no other caller of UpdateFile exists in the codebase.
- **Fix direction:** Make UpdateFile return a distinguishable error (or a third signal, e.g. a `failed bool`/sentinel) on the parseFile-failure branch (and ideally the stat-error branches) instead of nil, so cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:337's existing `err != nil` check actually fires and reports "update-fail" instead of "unchanged".

### F58. `internal/ir/generator.go:342` — UpdateFile
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** Implicit consistency assumption between UpdateFile's single-file refresh and a full Generate/Update walk producing the same IR for the same on-disk state — walkSourceFiles explicitly excludes symlinks (lines 159-164, using filepath.Walk's Lstat-based FileInfo) so Generate/UpdateCtx never index a symlinked source file.
- **Hypothesis:** filePath is a symlink pointing at a valid, supported-extension regular file (e.g. src/link.go -> ../vendor/big.go). A full GenerateCtx/UpdateCtx walk would never add an entry for src/link.go (skipped at line 159-164 because Walk's Lstat-derived info has ModeSymlink set). But UpdateFile calls os.Stat(absFile) at line 342, which follows the symlink and returns the target's FileInfo (ModeSymlink never set), so it falls into the default branch, parses the file, and sets files['src/link.go'] = fileIR — inserting an IR entry that a full regenerate would never produce, and that persists (surfacing via runecho.locate/structure) until the next full walk silently drops it.
- **Trace:** internal/ir/generator.go: walkSourceFiles (line 151, filepath.Walk) receives Lstat-derived FileInfo; for a symlink, info.Mode()&os.ModeSymlink != 0 is true at line 159, so a non-dir symlink hits `return nil` at line 163 -> the file is never passed to fn -> Generate/GenerateCtx (line 210-225) never adds an entry for it.

UpdateFile (line 316) is called directly with filePath = an absolute path to a symlink (e.g. tmpRoot/src/link.go -> tmpRoot/target/big.go). At line 342, `os.Stat(absFile)` (not Lstat) follows the symlink and returns the TARGET's FileInfo, which never has ModeSymlink set. This lands in the `default` branch (line 359) since info.IsDir() is false and `.go` is a supported extension -> g.parseFile(absFile) succeeds (it opens/reads through the symlink) -> `files[norm] = fileIR` at line 364, where norm = "src/link.go" (the symlink's own repo-relative path, since `rel` at line 329 is computed from absFile itself, not the resolved target).

Result: updated.Files["src/link.go"] exists and RootHash changes (updated.RootHash != existing.RootHash → changed=true), while a full walk over the identical tree never produces "src/link.go" at all.

Concrete input: tmpRoot/target/big.go = "package foo\n\nfunc Big() {}\n" (real file, non-ignored dir); tmpRoot/src/link.go = symlink to target/big.go.
Predicted wrong output: UpdateFile's returned IR contains key "src/link.go"; Generate's IR does not.
Expected/correct output (matching Generate): UpdateFile should also skip/omit "src/link.go".
- **Blast radius:** Single production call site: cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:337 (`gen.UpdateFile(existing, srcRoot, filePath)`), the E6 auto-fresh per-edit hook path — every guarded edit to a symlinked source file within the repo root will insert a phantom entry into the on-disk IR that persists (surfacing via runecho.locate/structure) until the next full Generate/UpdateCtx walk silently drops it again. Test/fuzz call sites (fuzz_test.go, e6_test.go, updatefile_test.go) are non-production.
- **Fix direction:** In UpdateFile, Lstat absFile (or check info.Mode()&os.ModeSymlink after an Lstat) before falling into the default parse branch, and treat a symlink the same as walkSourceFiles does — drop/skip the entry — so single-file refresh stays consistent with the full-walk semantics.

### F59. `internal/ir/generator.go:345` — UpdateFile
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** impossible-state
- **Contract violated:** Function signature `(*IR, bool, error)` advertises a fallible error channel; doc comment (312-315) frames unhandled cases as deliberate no-ops, implying real transient failures are distinguishable from legitimate 'nothing changed'.
- **Hypothesis:** A file that existing.Files already indexes has its permissions changed so os.Stat returns a non-ENOENT error (e.g. EACCES) — a genuine failure to inspect a possibly-changed file. Code at lines 345-346 returns (existing, false, nil): same nil-error, false-changed shape as the deliberate no-op case where the file legitimately hasn't changed. Expected: a real stat failure surfaces via the error return so a caller doing `if err != nil { retry/log }` can react. Actual: every one of the 9 return statements (318, 322, 327, 331, 346, 349, 356, 362, 369) passes nil for error, so `err` is structurally always nil — a caller's error-handling branch is dead code, and a real I/O failure on a changed file is indistinguishable from 'file did not change', permanently masking stale IR data for that file until something else touches it.
- **Trace:** Input: repo root with subdir sub/ containing sub/a.go, already indexed via gen.Generate(root) into `base` (base.Files["sub/a.go"] present). Then os.Chmod(sub, 0000) revokes search/execute permission on the parent directory, which makes os.Stat(sub/a.go) fail with EACCES ("permission denied") rather than ENOENT — confirmed directly: os.Stat(target) returned a non-nil error and os.IsNotExist(err) == false.

Call: gen.UpdateFile(base, root, target)
Path: generator.go:316 entry -> existing.Version check passes (line 317) -> filepath.Abs succeeds (320-328) -> filepath.Rel resolves inside root (329-332) -> files map copied (337-340) -> line 342: info, statErr := os.Stat(absFile) -> statErr != nil (EACCES) -> line 343 switch enters `case statErr != nil:` -> line 345: `if !os.IsNotExist(statErr)` is true (it's EACCES, not ENOENT) -> line 346: `return existing, false, nil // transient stat error — leave IR alone`.

Predicted wrong output (per hypothesis): (existing, false, nil) — same nil-error shape as the deliberate no-op.
Actual output observed: changed=false, err=<nil>, updated==base (same pointer) — exactly as predicted.

Caller-side consequence (cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:337): `} else if updated, changed, err = gen.UpdateFile(...); err != nil { return "update-fail" }` never triggers on this genuine I/O failure; execution falls through to line 340 `if !changed { return "unchanged" }`, so the guard hook reports "unchanged" for a file it could not actually inspect, with zero diagnostic signal that anything went wrong.</trace>
<parameter name="evidence">Command: `go test ./internal/ir/ -run TestFocusReproUpdateFileMasksStatError -v`
Output:
