=== RUN   TestFocusReproUpdateFileMasksStatError
    focusrepro_test.go:52: confirmed: os.Stat(target) failed with non-ENOENT error: stat /tmp/TestFocusReproUpdateFileMasksStatError1297983328/001/sub/a.go: permission denied
    focusrepro_test.go:56: UpdateFile result: changed=false err=<nil> sameIRPointer=true
    focusrepro_test.go:67: CONFIRMED: genuine stat error on already-indexed file returned (existing, false, nil) -- indistinguishable from legitimate no-op
--- PASS: TestFocusReproUpdateFileMasksStatError (0.00s)
PASS
ok  	github.com/inth3shadows/runecho/internal/ir	0.016s

Scratch test file was deleted after execution; `git status --porcelain` confirms a clean working tree (no output).
- **Blast radius:** Exactly one production caller in the repo: cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:337, inside the guard hook's auto-fresh-IR path (the E6 per-edit incremental update). Verified via `grep -rn "\.UpdateFile(" --include=*.go` (excluding tests) and codegraph_explore, both showing this as the sole call site. Effect: the guard's PostToolUse hook silently classifies a real stat I/O failure (e.g., a permissions change, a transient NFS/network-mount hiccup, or a race with another process) as "unchanged," leaving the guard's cached snapshot/IR stale for that file with no error surfaced to logs, retries, or the user — until some unrelated edit happens to touch the same file again.
- **Fix direction:** Change UpdateFile's signature contract to distinguish "legitimately unchanged" from "could not inspect": either return the stat error via the existing error channel at line 345-346 (and the analogous parse-error case at 361-362) instead of nil, or add an explicit sentinel/log call so the runecho-guard caller's `err != nil` branch can actually fire and retry/log instead of silently swallowing the failure.

### F60. `internal/ir/storage.go:125` — FileIR.MarshalJSON
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** impossible-state
- **Contract violated:** FileIR doc comment (lines 45-49): "Symbols is the canonical per-symbol model"
- **Hypothesis:** Given the same duplicate-import_name state as above (two Symbol{Kind:"import_name", Name:"parse"} entries from a try/except fallback import), `Symbols: emptySliceIfNil(f.Symbols)` at line 125 emits BOTH duplicate entries verbatim into the on-disk `symbols` JSON array — there is no dedup step anywhere in this file (sortSymbols only orders, legacySymbols/namesOf only filter-and-concatenate). Nothing in storage.go enforces the one-entry-per-(kind,name) invariant that its own hash/line-map derivation at lines 109-117 implicitly relies on by using "kind:name" as a map key. Today the duplication is only visually redundant because import_name entries always carry Line=0/Hash="" (s.SymbolLines/s.SymbolHashes in generator.go are keyed only for function/class kinds, never import_name, so both duplicates collide into the same zero-value), but any consumer of the canonical `symbols` array that counts symbols or treats (kind,name) as a unique identifier (e.g. coverage/stat tooling, or a future patch that starts populating import_name Line/Hash from the import statement's line) will silently double-count or silently lose one entry's data the moment that assumption is exercised, with no error or warning anywhere in the write path.
- **Trace:** Input: FileIR{Hash:"deadbeef", Symbols:[]Symbol{{Name:"parse",Kind:"import_name"},{Name:"parse",Kind:"import_name"}}} (models the try/except fallback-import duplicate; both entries zero-value on Line/Hash exactly as import_name symbols are always emitted). Path: sortSymbols(f.Symbols) [storage.go:73-80] → stable order preserved (equal keys) → json.Marshal(f) invokes FileIR.MarshalJSON [storage.go:106] → loop at 109-117 builds hashes/lines maps keyed "import_name:parse" (both entries collide harmlessly since Line=0/Hash="" for both) → out.Symbols = emptySliceIfNil(f.Symbols) [line 125] copies the 2-element slice verbatim → json.Marshal(out) [line 133] serializes both entries into the `symbols` array. Predicted wrong output: `symbols` array contains 2 entries for the same (kind,name) pair. Expected/contract output per the doc comment "Symbols is the canonical per-symbol model": exactly 1 entry per unique (kind,name).
- **Blast radius:** grep -rn '\.Symbols\b' confirms multiple live consumers iterate/count the canonical Symbols array today without dedup: internal/mcp/tools_oracle.go:288 (`symCount += len(f.Symbols)` — already double-counts in symbol-count stats), internal/snapshot/{diff.go,truthtrail.go,churn.go,snapshot.go}, internal/guardstats/guardstats.go:171, cmd/runecho-ir/{mapcmd.go,inspect.go}. Any of these that key or count by (kind,name) is exposed the moment a duplicate-producing input (e.g. try/except fallback imports) is parsed.
- **Fix direction:** Dedup by (Kind,Name) when building f.Symbols (e.g. in the generator that constructs import_name symbols, or as a final pass in MarshalJSON before emitting `out.Symbols`) rather than relying on downstream consumers to tolerate duplicates.

### F61. `internal/ir/storage.go:344` — IR.Save
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** unhandled-postcondition
- **Contract violated:** IR.Save's documented invariant: 'does NOT extend to concurrent callers... two goroutines or processes calling Save() on the same path concurrently can interleave WriteFile calls on the same tmp file and one process's Rename can promote the OTHER's content... a lost-update race the doc comment's crash-safety framing doesn't mention or protect against.'
- **Hypothesis:** In cmd/runecho-guard/main.go refreshIRForFile (line 344), two Claude Code sessions/agents editing different files in the same repo at nearly the same time each spawn a separate `runecho-guard` process via the PostToolUse hook; both concurrently call updated.Save(irPath) with the fixed tmp name `<irPath>+".tmp"`. Process A's WriteFile of IR_A (containing A's edit) is overwritten by process B's WriteFile of IR_B (containing B's edit but not A's) before A's os.Rename runs, so the promoted .ai/ir.json silently reflects only B's edit — A's newly added/removed symbol is lost from ir.json even though refreshIRForFile returned "refreshed" (no error) to A's hook, so the guard's dangling-ref/freshness checks on subsequent edits to A's file operate on stale symbol data and produce a false 'unresolved symbol' or miss a real one.
- **Trace:** Function under test: internal/ir/storage.go, IR.Save (lines 210-241):
  tmp := path + ".tmp"                         // line 231 - FIXED name, no pid/random suffix
  os.WriteFile(tmp, data, 0644)                // line 232
  os.Rename(tmp, path)                         // line 235

Interprocedural path exercised: cmd/runecho-guard/main.go refreshIRForFile (line 344: `updated.Save(irPath)`) is invoked once per PostToolUse hook firing; two Claude Code sessions/agents editing different files in the same repo at nearly the same time each spawn a `runecho-guard` process that calls this with the SAME irPath (`<srcRoot>/.ai/ir.json`).

Interleaving that produces the defect (goroutine A = process A editing file X, goroutine B = process B editing file Y):
  A: WriteFile(tmp, IR_A)      // IR_A has A's new/removed symbol
  B: WriteFile(tmp, IR_B)      // overwrites tmp; IR_A's bytes gone from disk
  B: Rename(tmp, path)         // succeeds -> path now = IR_B ; Save() returns nil to B (expected, correct for B)
  A: Rename(tmp, path)         // tmp no longer exists (ENOENT) -> Save() returns error to A
     -- OR, in the case both errors were nil --
  B: WriteFile(tmp, IR_B) -> B: Rename -> nil (path=IR_B)
  A: WriteFile(tmp, IR_A) (into a freshly recreated tmp) -> A: Rename -> nil (path=IR_A, silently discards IR_B)

Predicted wrong output (per hypothesis): refreshIRForFile can report "refreshed" (Save returns nil, no error) to one process's hook while ir.json on disk reflects only the OTHER process's edit — the calling process's own symbol change is silently absent from the persisted IR despite a success return.

Expected/correct behavior: each Save() call should either fully persist its own IR content when it returns nil, or the two concurrent writers should be serialized (lock/unique-tmp-then-atomic-merge) so no caller's successful write is silently discarded.

Actual observed output (executed): built a test in package `ir` (temp scratch file, later deleted) that ran irA.Save(path) and irB.Save(path) concurrently in a tight loop of 300 trials against a shared temp path, using distinct RootHash markers ("HASH_A" / "HASH_B") to detect which content survived. Checked, per trial, whether a Save() call returned nil while the final on-disk content did NOT match that caller's data.
- **Blast radius:** All three production call sites share this single unlocked Save() and the same per-repo fixed path `.ai/ir.json`, so any pair racing on the same repo hits it: cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:344 (`updated.Save(irPath)`, invoked once per PostToolUse hook firing — the concrete concurrent-agent scenario in the hypothesis), cmd/runecho-ir/repo.go:256 (`irData.Save(...)`, repo reindex), cmd/runecho-ir/capture.go:161 (`result.Save(irPath)`). Downstream consumers of the resulting ir.json (guard's dangling-ref/freshness checks, snapshot.RollAutoSnapshot at main.go:349 which is called AFTER Save with the caller's own `updated` in-memory value, not what's actually on disk) then operate on a symbol set that has silently diverged from what Save's own caller believed it just persisted.
- **Fix direction:** Write to a per-process/per-call-unique tmp name (e.g. `path + "." + strconv.Itoa(os.Getpid()) + "." + randSuffix + ".tmp"`) before the atomic rename, and/or serialize concurrent Save() calls to the same path with an flock-based file lock, so no caller's successful WriteFile can be clobbered by another caller's WriteFile to the same tmp path before its own Rename runs.

### F62. `internal/ir/storage.go:344` — IR.Save
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** Caller-side asymmetry: cmd/runecho-guard/learnedallow.go:143 already wraps its own load-modify-save file update in withFileLock(...) specifically to serialize 'concurrent PostToolUse hooks' per that function's own doc comment, but the structurally identical load-modify-save of .ai/ir.json three call sites away (refreshIRForFile) is left unlocked.
- **Hypothesis:** Given the same process (runecho-guard binary) already treats concurrent-PostToolUse-hook clobbering as a real, mitigated risk for the learned-allow store, the omission of the same withFileLock(irPath+".lock", ...) wrapper around gen.UpdateFile+updated.Save(irPath) in refreshIRForFile means two concurrent hook invocations on the same repo can produce the exact 'last-writer-wins silently drop[s]' outcome the learned-allow comment says this pattern exists to prevent — but applied to ir.json instead of the learned-allow file.
- **Trace:** Input: repo with a.go (func Alpha) and b.go (func Beta), IR bootstrapped and saved to .ai/ir.json. Then a.go is edited to add AlphaNew and b.go to add BetaNew "concurrently" (two goroutines started via a closed channel gate).
Path per goroutine (mirrors cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:319-344, refreshIRForFile):
  existing, _ := ir.Load(irPath)                                   // main.go:319
  updated, changed, _ := gen.UpdateFile(existing, srcRoot, file)   // main.go:337
  updated.Save(irPath)                                             // main.go:344 -> internal/ir/storage.go:231-238 (fixed tmp name, Rename)
Predicted wrong output: the two Saves interleave without any lock (no withFileLock as used in cmd/runecho-guard/learnedallow.go:143), so one goroutine's Load happens before the other's Save commits -> its Save overwrites the other's change -> final ir.json missing one of {AlphaNew, BetaNew}.
Expected/correct output (if properly serialized, as learnedallow.go does): final ir.json contains BOTH AlphaNew and BetaNew.
Actual observed output (go test, count=50): 49/50 runs failed the "both present" assertion — e.g. run 1: `hasAlphaNew=true hasBetaNew=false` (BetaNew's UpdateFile+Save lost); other runs additionally hit `rename .../ir.json.tmp .../ir.json: no such file or directory` and `failed to unmarshal IR: invalid character ']' after top-level value` (shared-tmp-file collision, a corruption mode beyond the original lost-update hypothesis). Only 1/50 runs happened to interleave favorably and passed.</trace>
<parameter name="evidence">Command: `go test ./internal/ir/ -run TestFocusReproConcurrentRefreshLosesUpdate -v -count=50`
Representative output lines:
`zzfocusrepro_test.go:88: hasAlphaNew=true hasBetaNew=false`
`zzfocusrepro_test.go:91: LOST UPDATE: one concurrent refresh's change was silently dropped by the other's last-writer-wins Save (aHasNewSym=true bHasNewSym=false) — same class of bug learnedallow.go's withFileLock comment describes, applied here to ir.json`
`zzfocusrepro_test.go:55: save(a.go): failed to replace IR file: rename /tmp/.../.ai/ir.json.tmp /tmp/.../.ai/ir.json: no such file or directory`
`zzfocusrepro_test.go:69: load final: failed to unmarshal IR: invalid character ']' after top-level value`
Result: 49 FAIL, 1 PASS out of 50 runs — `FAIL github.com/inth3shadows/runecho/internal/ir 0.350s`
Scratch repro file used: internal/ir/zzfocusrepro_test.go (constructed via os.WriteFile-backed t.TempDir fixtures, real gen.Generate/gen.UpdateFile/ir.Load/IR.Save calls — no reimplementation). Deleted after execution; `git status` confirms working tree clean (verified via `git status --short` -> no output, `git status` -> "nothing to commit, working tree clean").
- **Blast radius:** refreshIRForFile (cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:276) has exactly one call site: main.go:263, inside the PostToolUse hook handler — fires on every file-edit tool call in an enrolled repo. Any two overlapping PostToolUse invocations in the same repo (parallel subagents / multiple Claude Code sessions editing the repo concurrently, or a fast sequence of tool calls whose hook processes overlap) race on the same unlocked load-modify-save of .ai/ir.json. IR.Save itself (internal/ir/storage.go:210) has 3 call sites total: cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:344 (unlocked, this bug), cmd/runecho-ir/repo.go:256 and cmd/runecho-ir/capture.go:161 (both single-shot CLI invocations, not concurrent hook-driven, so lower risk but share the same fixed-tmp-filename collision hazard if ever run concurrently against the same repo).
- **Fix direction:** Wrap the load+gen.UpdateFile+Save sequence in cmd/runecho-guard/main.go (~lines 319-349) in the same withFileLock(irPath+".lock", func(){...}) pattern already used by recordApprovals in learnedallow.go:143; separately, harden IR.Save (internal/ir/storage.go:231) to use a unique per-process temp name (e.g. os.CreateTemp in the target dir, as saveLearnedAllow.go:108 already does) so concurrent Saves from any caller can't collide on the same fixed `path+".tmp"`.

### F63. `internal/mcp/server.go:114` — Server.Register
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** impossible-state
- **Contract violated:** Server field comment at server.go:74 ('log ... left non-nil here defensively so a zero Server never panics on logf') implies zero-value Server usage is an anticipated case
- **Hypothesis:** If a Server is constructed as a bare `mcp.Server{}` (not via NewServer) and Register is called on it, s.tools is a nil map (its zero value). The read at line 111 (`_, dup := s.tools[t.Name]`) succeeds silently on a nil map (dup=false), but the write at line 114 (`s.tools[t.Name] = t`) panics with 'assignment to entry in nil map'. Register is only half-defended against the zero-value Server the surrounding code explicitly designed logf to tolerate — the read path looks safe, masking that the very next line is not.
- **Trace:** Function (internal/mcp/server.go, current text, ~line 111-116):
```go
func (s *Server) Register(t Tool) {
	if _, dup := s.tools[t.Name]; !dup {   // line 111: nil-map READ, succeeds, dup=false
		s.order = append(s.order, t.Name)   // line 112: fine, nil slice append is legal
	}
	s.tools[t.Name] = t                     // line 114: nil-map WRITE -> panic
}
```
Input: `var s Server` (zero value — s.tools == nil, s.log == nil, per the same zero-value contract the log field comment relies on) then `s.Register(Tool{Name: "foo"})`.
Path: Register line 111 (`_, dup := s.tools[t.Name]`) — nil map read returns zero value, dup=false, no panic — proceeds to line 112 (append to nil order slice, fine) — falls through to line 114 (`s.tools[t.Name] = t`) — Go runtime panics: "assignment to entry in nil map".
Predicted wrong output: panic/crash on the very next line after the "safe-looking" read.
Expected/contract-implied output: since server.go:74 explicitly documents zero-value Server as an anticipated, non-panicking use case (for logf), Register should either lazily initialize s.tools or the type should be unusable-by-design — instead it silently permits construction and read, then panics only on write, which is the "impossible state" masking (looks defended, isn't).
- **Blast radius:** grep -rn shows the only production call site is cmd/runecho-mcp/main.go:41-42, which always goes through `mcp.NewServer(...)` (never a bare `Server{}`), so the panic is not reachable from the shipped binary today. However: (1) `Server` and `Register` are exported (capital-letter) API surface of the `internal/mcp` package, reachable by any other package within the module without going through NewServer; (2) the field-level doc comment on `log` at server.go:74 explicitly frames zero-value Server as a supported case, which is a documented invariant Register violates; (3) any future caller (or test) that does `var s mcp.Server` / `&mcp.Server{}` and calls Register directly hits an unrecoverable panic instead of the graceful degrade the comment promises.
- **Fix direction:** Lazily initialize the map in Register (`if s.tools == nil { s.tools = map[string]Tool{} }` before the read/write), mirroring the same zero-value defense already applied to `log`/`logf`.

### F64. `internal/mcp/server.go:208` — Server.handle
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** inverted-condition
- **Contract violated:** handle's own docstring (line 193-194): 'handle dispatches one request. The bool is false for notifications (no reply)' — implying the returned bool tracks isNotification the same way it does in every other case branch (initialize/ping/tools/list all return !isNotification).
- **Hypothesis:** Input {"jsonrpc":"2.0","id":"1","method":"notifications/initialized"} has a non-empty id, so isNotification computed at line 195 is false. Every sibling branch (initialize, ping, tools/list) would return reply=true for this id. handle instead hardcodes 'return response{}, false' for this method name regardless of isNotification, so the caller waiting on a correlated reply for id "1" gets nothing back, while an identical id-bearing request to 'ping' gets a reply.
- **Trace:** internal/mcp/server.go:194-224 (current code, verified by direct read, not stale):

```
194 func (s *Server) handle(req request) (response, bool) {
195     isNotification := len(req.ID) == 0
...
205     switch req.Method {
206     case "initialize":
207         return s.ok(req.ID, s.initResult(req.Params)), !isNotification
208     case "notifications/initialized", "notifications/cancelled":
209         return response{}, false
210     case "ping":
211         return s.ok(req.ID, map[string]any{}), !isNotification
212     case "tools/list":
213         return s.ok(req.ID, s.listTools()), !isNotification
```

Input: req = {JSONRPC:"2.0", ID: `"1"` (non-empty), Method:"notifications/initialized"}.
Line 195: isNotification := len(req.ID)==0 -> len(`"1"`)=3 -> isNotification=false.
Line 205 switch dispatches to case at line 208 (method matches "notifications/initialized").
Line 209: hardcoded `return response{}, false` — ignores isNotification entirely.
Predicted wrong output: reply=false (docstring/every sibling branch would return !isNotification == true for this id).
Comparison request: identical id "1" with Method:"ping" hits line 210-211, returns !isNotification == true.

Executed output matched the prediction exactly (see evidence).
- **Blast radius:** Single call site: internal/mcp/server.go:146 inside Server.Serve's request loop (`resp, reply := s.handle(req); if reply { enc.Encode(resp) }`). Any JSON-RPC client that sends "notifications/initialized" or "notifications/cancelled" with a non-empty "id" (a malformed-but-real-world client behavior — MCP clients don't always avoid attaching ids to notification-shaped methods) gets no reply written at all, indistinguishable on the wire from a hung/dead server for that request id, while an identical id sent to "ping" or "initialize" is answered normally. No other caller of Server.handle exists in the repo (grep confirms only the one non-test call site).
- **Fix direction:** Make the notifications/initialized|cancelled branch respect isNotification like every sibling branch, e.g. `if isNotification { return response{}, false }` then fall through to an explicit response/error for the id-bearing misuse case, instead of unconditionally hardcoding `false`.

### F65. `internal/mcp/server.go:215` — Server.handle
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** unhandled-postcondition
- **Contract violated:** Serve's docstring (line 123): 'Notifications (no id) are processed without a reply' — and handle's own pattern for initialize/ping/tools/list, which always computes/executes the result and only gates the reply bool by isNotification, never skips execution.
- **Hypothesis:** Input {"jsonrpc":"2.0","method":"tools/call","params":{"name":"echoTool","arguments":{}}} has no id, so isNotification is true. Per 'processed without a reply' and the pattern of the other three method branches, echoTool's Handler should still execute (any side effect it has should run) with just the reply suppressed. Instead the code returns response{}, false at line 216 before ever calling s.callTool, so the handler never runs at all — a fire-and-forget tools/call notification produces zero execution and zero diagnostics, not 'executed silently.'
- **Trace:** Input: request{JSONRPC:"2.0", Method:"tools/call", Params:`{"name":"echoTool","arguments":{}}`} with ID omitted (nil) -> isNotification := len(req.ID)==0 is true (server.go:195) -> switch hits case "tools/call" (server.go:214) -> if isNotification { return response{}, false } (server.go:215-216) fires immediately -> s.callTool (server.go:218), and therefore the registered Tool.Handler, is never reached.
Predicted wrong output: echoTool's Handler body never executes; executed flag stays false.
Expected right output per Serve's docstring (line 123, "Notifications ... are processed without a reply") and the pattern in the initialize/ping/tools/list branches (which always call s.ok(...)/s.initResult/s.listTools and only gate the boolean by isNotification): the handler should run for its side effect, with only the reply suppressed (i.e. call s.callTool(req.ID, req.Params) and return (result, false) rather than short-circuiting to (response{}, false) pre-execution).
- **Blast radius:** Only one caller of Server.handle: Server.Serve's stdio read loop (internal/mcp/server.go:146, the sole call site confirmed via grep -rn "s.handle(" — no other callers in non-test code). Blast radius is therefore every MCP client of RunEcho's stdio server (Claude Code / Codex) that sends a fire-and-forget tools/call notification (a request with no "id"): the tool never executes and neither the client nor the server log records anything, silently dropping the invocation instead of the documented "processed without a reply" behavior.
- **Fix direction:** In the "tools/call" case of Server.handle (server.go:214-218), remove the isNotification short-circuit and instead call resp, _ := s.callTool(req.ID, req.Params); return resp, !isNotification — mirroring the initialize/ping/tools/list branches so the handler always executes and only the reply is gated.

### F66. `internal/mcp/server.go:269` — Server.callTool
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** Server.callTool postcondition: 'If params fails to unmarshal into {Name, Arguments} ... returns -32602 invalid params'
- **Hypothesis:** Client sends {"jsonrpc":"2.0","id":1,"method":"tools/call","params":null}. req.Params becomes the literal 4 bytes "null" (verified: json.RawMessage captures it, not the zero-length nil that a truly missing params key would produce). json.Unmarshal([]byte("null"), &p) returns err=nil and silently leaves p.Name=="" and p.Arguments==nil (verified via go run: encoding/json treats top-level JSON null into a struct target as a no-op, not an error) — this bypasses the 'err != nil -> invalid params' check entirely. Execution falls through to s.tools[""], which is not a registered tool, so ok==false and the function returns -32602 "unknown tool: " (empty name). A client that sent explicit params:null gets a confusing empty-name 'unknown tool' error instead of the intended 'invalid params' diagnostic that every other malformed-params shape (missing key, wrong type, non-object) correctly produces.
- **Trace:** Input: params := json.RawMessage(`null`), id := json.RawMessage(`1`)
server.go:264 callTool(id, params) entered
server.go:269 json.Unmarshal([]byte("null"), &p) -> err == nil (null-into-struct is a no-op in encoding/json), p.Name == "", p.Arguments == nil
server.go:270 `if err != nil` is FALSE -> invalid-params branch skipped
server.go:272 t, ok := s.tools[""] -> ok == false (no tool registered under empty name)
server.go:273-274 returns s.errResp(id, -32602, "unknown tool: "+"") = {Code:-32602, Message:"unknown tool: "}
Predicted wrong output: Error.Message == "unknown tool: " (empty name)
Expected/correct output per contract: Error.Message == "invalid params"
- **Blast radius:** grep -rn "callTool" shows exactly one call site: internal/mcp/server.go:218, inside Server.handle's "tools/call" case — the sole JSON-RPC dispatch path for the stdio MCP server. Any MCP client (Claude Code, other MCP hosts) that sends {"method":"tools/call","params":null} hits this path; no other internal Go callers exist (confirmed via grep across internal/mcp and cmd/).
- **Fix direction:** In callTool, treat a JSON `null` params payload the same as malformed params: check `len(params) == 0 || bytes.Equal(bytes.TrimSpace(params), []byte("null"))` (or unmarshal into `json.RawMessage`/`any` first and reject non-object) before/alongside the Unmarshal-error check, returning -32602 "invalid params".

### F67. `internal/mcp/tools_oracle.go:152` — matchGlobstar
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** Doc comment (134-138) states 'each "**" matches any number of path components (including zero)' with no restriction that a middle literal must be followed by more path — but the middle-segment loop (152-169) only recognizes a match when the literal is followed by "/" (via `m+"/"`, `"/"+m+"/"`, or an interior `"/"+m+"/"` search); it never accepts the literal appearing as the final path component of the remaining string with nothing after it.
- **Hypothesis:** matchGlob("**/a/**", "x/a") should return true (prefix ** absorbs "x", literal "a" matches the final component, trailing ** matches zero components) but returns false, because the middle-segment search for "a" requires a trailing "/a/" or "a/" and "x/a" has no "/" after the final "a". Verified by extracting matchGlobstar into a standalone Go program and running it: matchGlobstarWrap("**/a/**", "x/a") -> false, and matchGlobstarWrap("**/a/**", "a") -> false (even a bare single-component path fails to match its own literal component).
- **Trace:** matchGlob("**/a/**", "x/a") -> strings.Contains(pattern,"**") true -> matchGlobstar(strings.Split("**/a/**","**"), "x/a") = matchGlobstar(["", "/a/", ""], "x/a") [tools_oracle.go:125]
  L141: first = TrimSuffix(segs[0],"/") = "" -> skip prefix-anchor block entirely (p stays "x/a")
  L152: loop over segs[1:len-1] = ["/a/"]; m = Trim("/a/","/") = "a"
  L158: HasPrefix("x/a","a/") -> false
  L160: HasPrefix("x/a","/a/") -> false
  L163: idx := Index("x/a","/a/") -> -1 (no trailing "/" after the final "a")
  L166: return false  <- wrong; correct answer is true (prefix ** eats "x", "a" is the whole remaining path, trailing ** eats zero components)

Same trace for matchGlob("**/a/**","a"): first="" skip; loop m="a"; p="a"; none of HasPrefix("a","a/"), HasPrefix("a","/a/") match; Index("a","/a/") = -1 -> return false. Even the bare single-component path "a" fails to match its own literal.

Control case matchGlob("**/a/**","x/a/y") correctly returns true (literal followed by "/" is the only path the loop accepts), confirming the defect is specifically the "literal is the final component" case, not a general breakage.</trace>
<parameter name="evidence">Command: `mv internal/mcp/_focus_repro_test.go internal/mcp/zzfocus_repro_test.go && go test ./internal/mcp/ -run TestFocusReproMatchGlobstarMiddleLiteralAtEnd -v`
(repro called the real unmodified matchGlob/matchGlobstar from internal/mcp/tools_oracle.go; file renamed off the leading-underscore because Go's build tool ignores `_*.go`/`.` -prefixed files, so the original name never actually ran — the harness's suggested repro filename would have silently produced "no tests to run" if not caught.)

Output:
```
=== RUN   TestFocusReproMatchGlobstarMiddleLiteralAtEnd
    zzfocus_repro_test.go:23: matchGlob("**/a/**", "x/a") = false (want true)
    zzfocus_repro_test.go:25: BUG REPRODUCED: matchGlob("**/a/**", "x/a") = false, want true
    zzfocus_repro_test.go:23: matchGlob("**/a/**", "a") = false (want true)
    zzfocus_repro_test.go:25: BUG REPRODUCED: matchGlob("**/a/**", "a") = false, want true
    zzfocus_repro_test.go:23: matchGlob("**/a/**", "x/a/y") = true (want true)
--- FAIL: TestFocusReproMatchGlobstarMiddleLiteralAtEnd (0.00s)
FAIL
FAIL	github.com/inth3shadows/runecho/internal/mcp	0.040s
FAIL
```
Scratch file deleted after run; `git status --porcelain -- internal/mcp/` shows no output (clean).
- **Blast radius:** Single call site: internal/mcp/tools_oracle.go:274, `matchAnyGlob(a.Paths, p)` — the "paths" glob filter on the map/structure MCP tool. Any user- or agent-supplied glob of the shape "**/LITERAL/**" (or any pattern with a "**"-delimited middle literal) will fail to match files/dirs where LITERAL is the final path component (e.g. a top-level dir named exactly "a", or any path ending "/a" with nothing after), silently dropping those entries from filtered results with no error surfaced. grep confirms matchGlob/matchAnyGlob have no other production callers (only this one plus their own definitions).
- **Fix direction:** In the middle-segment loop, also accept p == m or strings.HasSuffix(p, "/"+m) as a match when the literal is the last remaining component (treating remaining "**" as absorbing zero trailing components), not just the "followed by /" cases.

### F68. `internal/mcp/tools_oracle.go:284` — structure
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** unhandled-postcondition
- **Contract violated:** symbol_count is presented as "how many symbols exist in this file" but silently includes kinds (import_name, export_wildcard) that no other oracle tool (locate) can ever surface individually, so a caller cannot reconcile symbol_count against what locate returns for the same file even when kind filters are exhausted.
- **Hypothesis:** For a TS file with 3 functions, 2 import_name bindings, and 1 export_wildcard specifier, structure(detail=tree|symbols) reports symbol_count=6 (len(f.Symbols) counts every kind unconditionally), but locate(repo, kind="") returns only the 3 functions (default function+class filter) and there is no kind value that will ever return the other 3 — the discrepancy is unexplained and unresolvable from the oracle's own tool surface.
- **Trace:** Input demo.ts:
```
import { Foo } from './foo';
import { Bar } from './bar';
export * from './wild';

function one() {}
function two() {}
function three() {}
```
Path: symbolsFromStructure (generator.go:484-506) builds Symbols = [function×3, import×2 (raw import kind, line 495), import_name×2 (bound names Foo/Bar, line 496), export_wildcard×1 (the './wild' specifier, line 503)] = 8 total.
structure() (tools_oracle.go:250-314): line 288 `symCount += len(f.Symbols)` sums all 8 unconditionally regardless of kind → line 310 emits `"symbol_count": 8`.
locate() (tools_oracle.go:489-569): `keep()` (line 515-520) with kind="" matches only k=="function"||k=="class" → total=3. Iterating every kind value normalizeLocateKind accepts (func→"function", class→"class", export→"export", import→"import"): totals are 3, 0, 0, 2 respectively — sum=5. The remaining 3 symbols (import_name×2, export_wildcard×1) map to kind strings ("import_name","export_wildcard") that normalizeLocateKind's switch (line 585-600) has no case for, so `invalid kind` is the only possible outcome for any attempt to request them — they are unreachable from locate under any input.
- **Blast radius:** structure and locate are independent leaf MCP tool handlers (registered separately in tools_oracle.go: structure at line ~36-39, locate similarly) — grep found no internal Go caller of o.structure/o.locate besides tool registration and tests, so the only "callers" are external MCP clients/agents. Every agent session that queries `structure` on a JS/TS repo containing import bindings or `export * from` re-exports and tries to reconcile symbol_count against `locate` totals (e.g. to confirm all symbols are accounted for, or to page through "all" symbols by iterating kinds) hits this gap. It also silently affects any future kind added to symbolsFromStructure that isn't mirrored in normalizeLocateKind.
- **Fix direction:** Either extend normalizeLocateKind to accept "import_name" and "export_wildcard" (and require any future symbolsFromStructure kind to be added there too, ideally enforced by a test that asserts every distinct kind in Symbols is locate-reachable), or exclude those two non-locatable kinds from symCount and surface them separately (e.g. a `symbol_count_by_kind` map) so the top-level number only ever claims what locate can actually reproduce.

### F69. `internal/mcp/tools_oracle.go:354` — diff
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** unhandled-postcondition
- **Contract violated:** Comments at 352-353 and 357-358 state the guards exist so that a malformed input combination never 'silently answers a different question'; the two checks at 354 and 359-361 only cover a-xor-b and session-without-since, leaving a+b+since (and a+b+session) completely unguarded.
- **Hypothesis:** Call diff with {repo:"foo", a:1, b:2, since:"baseline"}: intent per the surrounding comments is to reject this as an ambiguous/over-specified request (or at minimum answer the since-vs-live question), but the switch at line 366 tests `a.A != nil && a.B != nil` first, matches, and silently returns the a-vs-b snapshot diff — `since` is read into `a.Since` and then never referenced again, with no error and no indication that it was ignored.
- **Trace:** Input: diff(args={"repo":"demo","a":1,"b":2,"since":"baseline"})
Line 344: json.Unmarshal → a.A=ptr(1), a.B=ptr(2), a.Since="baseline", a.Session=""
Line 347: repo resolved OK
Line 354: (a.A!=nil)!=(a.B!=nil) → (true)!=(true) → false → guard does NOT fire
Line 359: a.Session=="" → condition false → guard does NOT fire
Line 366: case a.A!=nil && a.B!=nil → TRUE, matches first
Line 367-378: computes o.db.Diff(snapshot#1, snapshot#2) → result = {added:[Gamma], removed:[]}
`since` field (a.Since="baseline") is never read again anywhere in the function.
Predicted wrong output: no error; returns a-vs-b diff (added=1,removed=0) silently discarding since.
Expected (per comments' intent): either reject the over-specified combo with an error, or otherwise not silently answer a different question than "since baseline".
Actual observed output: total_added=1, total_removed=0, no error — exactly the predicted wrong output.
- **Blast radius:** Direct caller: the `diff` MCP tool handler is registered/dispatched from internal/mcp/server.go's tool-call routing (mcp__runecho__diff exposed to any MCP client, e.g. Claude Code sessions using RunEcho for drift questions) and from the `runecho-ir diff --json` CLI surface, which shares snapshot.DiffPayload with this same result. Any caller that (accidentally or via a buggy client) passes a+b+since or a+b+session together gets a silently wrong answer instead of an error — no internal Go callers found via `grep -rn "\.diff(" --include=*.go` beyond tests, so blast radius is external MCP/CLI callers only, not internal call graph.
- **Fix direction:** Extend the guard: reject when `(a.A != nil || a.B != nil) && (a.Since != "" || a.Session != "")` — i.e. treat any a/b + since/session combination as over-specified and return an error, alongside the existing a-xor-b and session-without-since checks.

### F70. `internal/mcp/tools_oracle.go:585` — normalizeLocateKind
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** impossible-state
- **Contract violated:** locate's kind filter is meant to let a caller restrict results to any symbol kind the IR indexes, and structure's symbol_count/full-detail dump proves two more kinds exist beyond the four this switch recognizes.
- **Hypothesis:** symbolsFromStructure (internal/ir/generator.go:484-505) tags real, stored symbols with kind "import_name" (the locally-bound name from an import, added specifically to fix issues #76/#80) and "export_wildcard" (a bare `export * from './mod'` specifier) in addition to function/class/export/import. normalizeLocateKind's switch only maps ""/func/function/class/cls/export/exp/import/imp to valid kinds and returns ok=false for anything else, so calling locate with kind="import_name" or kind="export_wildcard" always errors with "invalid kind" even though those are legitimate, currently-indexed kind values — and since a.Kind=="" defaults keep() to function+class only (line 519), there is no way, with or without an explicit kind, to ever retrieve an import_name or export_wildcard symbol through the locate tool. A caller trying to verify "is `Path` bound by an import in this file" (the exact motivating case for import_name in the comment above symbolsFromStructure) cannot do it via locate at all, despite structure's symbol_count (tools_oracle.go:284,288) silently counting those same symbols as if they were locatable.
- **Trace:** Input: repo "importrepo" with a.py = `from pathlib import Path\n\ndef f():\n    return Path('.')\n`.
Path 1 (structure): o.structure() -> ir.symbolsFromStructure (internal/ir/generator.go:484-505) calls add(importedNames(path, src), "import_name") at line 496, producing Symbol{Name:"Path", Kind:"import_name"} -> stored/returned in structure's files[...].symbols and folded into symbol_count (tools_oracle.go:284-291,310).
Path 2 (locate, explicit kind): o.locate({"kind":"import_name"}) -> tools_oracle.go:499 normalizeLocateKind("import_name") -> switch at line 586 matches none of ""/func/function/class/cls/export/exp/import/imp -> falls to `default: return "", false` (line 598) -> locate line 500-501 returns error `invalid kind "import_name" (want func|class|export|import)`.
Path 3 (locate, default kind): o.locate({}) -> kind="" -> keep() at line 515-520 defaults to `k=="function" || k=="class"` -> the "Path"/import_name symbol is filtered out regardless of offset/paging.
Predicted wrong output: structure counts/returns the "Path" import_name symbol as part of symbol_count, but locate cannot retrieve it either via kind="import_name" (hard error) or via default kind (silently excluded).
- **Blast radius:** normalizeLocateKind has exactly one caller: the `locate` MCP tool handler (internal/mcp/tools_oracle.go:499), which is the sole callsite reached by any MCP client invoking the registered "locate" tool (registered at tools_oracle.go:66). Any caller of the `locate` tool — including runecho's own guard/dogfooding flows and any external MCP client — is affected: they can never filter by or retrieve "import_name" or "export_wildcard" symbols, even though structure's symbol_count includes them as indexed.
- **Fix direction:** Add `case "import_name": return "import_name", true` and `case "export_wildcard": return "export_wildcard", true` (plus short aliases if desired) to normalizeLocateKind's switch in internal/mcp/tools_oracle.go:585-600; keep() already works correctly once kind is non-empty, so no change needed there.

### F71. `internal/parser/go.go:225` — receiverTypeName / collectGenDecl+Parse (function-key collision)
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** impossible-state
- **Contract violated:** Parse's stated invariant (and the recordHash doc comment at go.go:73-76): 'a collision here needs two top-level decls with the same exported name — a compile error in valid Go.' This is false: a method whose receiver type expression is anything other than *ast.StarExpr/*ast.Ident/*ast.IndexExpr/*ast.IndexListExpr (e.g. a selector-typed receiver like `*pkg.Type`) makes receiverTypeName return "", so qualify("", name) collapses the method's key to the same bare 'function:<Name>' key as an unrelated top-level function of that name — even though methods and functions are different namespaces in real Go and this is NOT a compile error.
- **Hypothesis:** Given the file `package p\n\nfunc Widget() {}\n\nfunc (w *ext.Widget) Widget() {}\n`, go/parser.ParseFile returns err=nil (this is syntactically valid Go; only go/types would reject the selector receiver) and produces two *ast.FuncDecl nodes. Verified empirically via GoParser.Parse on this exact source: Functions=["Widget"] (only one entry — the method is invisible), SymbolHashes["function:Widget"] is a single combined hash (sha256 of hash1+hash2 per recordHash's collision-combine at go.go:80-86) that matches neither declaration's actual body, and SymbolLines["function:Widget"]=3 (the plain function's line — the method at line 5 is never recorded because recordLine only sets on first-seen). Any caller doing hash-based drift detection on either symbol gets a corrupted signal: editing only the method body still changes the combined hash (looks like the top-level Widget changed), and editing only the top-level Widget also changes it (looks like the method changed) — the two are indistinguishable and the method's existence and true location are silently lost.
- **Trace:** Input: `package p\n\nfunc Widget() {}\n\nfunc (w *ext.Widget) Widget() {}\n`
Parse (go.go:91) → f, _ := parser.ParseFile(...) → f != nil, 2 *ast.FuncDecl nodes (plain Widget at line 3, method Widget at line 5).
Loop over f.Decls (go.go:93-112):
 - decl 1 (plain func): d.Recv == nil → full = "Widget" (line 100); key = "function:Widget"; recordHash(key, body1) → hashes["function:Widget"] = h1 = sha256("func Widget() {}"); recordLine(key, 3) → lines["function:Widget"] = 3.
 - decl 2 (method): d.Recv != nil → receiverTypeName(*ast.StarExpr wrapping *ast.SelectorExpr `ext.Widget`) → StarExpr case recurses on SelectorExpr, which matches none of the switch's cases → returns "" (go.go:225) → full = qualify("", "Widget") = "Widget" (bare, not "Widget.Widget") → same key "function:Widget"; recordHash combines: hashes["function:Widget"] = sha256(h1 + h2) where h2 = sha256("func (w *ext.Widget) Widget() {}"); recordLine no-ops (key already set, line stays 3 — method's true line 5 lost).
Predicted wrong output: Functions=["Widget"] (method invisible, no "Widget.Widget" entry), SymbolLines["function:Widget"]=3 (method's real line 5 never recorded), SymbolHashes["function:Widget"] = combined hash matching neither declaration's true body hash.
Expected/correct behavior per doc comment ("a collision here needs two top-level decls with the same exported name — a compile error"): should either not collide at all (method properly qualified as "Widget.Widget") or, if it does collide, only via an actual compile-error scenario.
Actual executed output (test run below) exactly matched the predicted wrong output: Functions=[Widget]; SymbolLines[function:Widget]=3; SymbolHashes[function:Widget]=e986d123... — verified via separate sha256 computation that this equals sha256(h1+h2) where h1=495838...(hash of "func Widget() {}") and h2=5ac4fa...(hash of "func (w *ext.Widget) Widget() {}"), and combined matches NEITHER h1 NOR h2 individually — confirming the "indistinguishable corruption" sub-claim (editing either declaration changes the combined hash, making drift detection ambiguous/wrong for both).
- **Blast radius:** internal/ir/generator.go:489,492 and internal/ir/storage.go:91-92,128,131,162,165 consume Functions/SymbolHashes/SymbolLines directly to build the IR's per-symbol Hash/Line records — the same records this repo's own CLAUDE.md designates as the "code-truth source" for runecho-guard drift detection. Any Go file in the corpus with a selector-typed method receiver (`func (r *pkg.Type) Method()`) silently loses that method from the index and corrupts hash-drift signal for the colliding top-level function/method pair. grep confirms these are the only two production consumers of the affected fields.
- **Fix direction:** Make qualify (or the go.go call site) fall back to a non-colliding disambiguator when receiverTypeName returns "" — e.g. qualify using the raw unparsed receiver type text (via nodeSpan/format on d.Recv.List[0].Type) instead of "", so an unhandled receiver expression still produces a unique method key rather than silently aliasing a top-level function.

### F72. `internal/parser/js.go:163` — (p *JSParser) parse
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** parse's fallback-union logic assumes jsSymbolsFromAST's hasError return reliably flags every case where the AST path failed to capture real symbols, but jsSymbolsFromAST's own contract documents hasError as explicitly false on its early-return paths (nest-depth-exceeded at line 279-282, and Parse()-error/nil-tree at line 284-286) and left at its pre-panic value (also typically false) on the panic-recovery path (lines 270-275).
- **Hypothesis:** Feed parse() a .js source string whose bracket/brace/paren nesting exceeds maxParseNestDepth (1000) but which also contains ordinary top-level `function foo() {}` and `class Bar {}` declarations before the pathological nesting. jsLanguageFor returns a non-nil lang (JS grammar is embedded), so the AST branch at line 160 runs; jsSymbolsFromAST hits exceedsNestDepth(src) at its line 279 and returns (nil, nil, nil, nil, false). Back in parse() at line 163, hasError is false, so the extractFunctions/extractClasses regex fallback (line 173-174) is never invoked. The returned FileStructure.Functions and FileStructure.Classes are both empty even though `foo` and `Bar` are real top-level symbols a plain regex scan would have found — directly contradicting the file's doc comment (lines 27-29) that AST failure degrades to (or supplements with) the regex fallback 'so symbol coverage never regresses.'
- **Trace:** Input: source = "function foo() {}\nclass Bar {}\n" + "["×1001 (maxParseNestDepth+1 opening brackets, unbalanced/pathological nesting).
Path: JSParser.parse (js.go:143) → jsLanguageFor(ext) returns non-nil JS grammar (js.go:160) → jsSymbolsFromAST(source, lang) (js.go:263) → exceedsNestDepth(src) is true (js.go:279, since 1001 > maxParseNestDepth=1000 per parser.go:59/69) → returns (nil, nil, nil, nil, false) at js.go:281-282, i.e. hasError=false.
Back in parse() at js.go:163: `if hasError` is false → the extractFunctions/extractClasses regex-fallback block (js.go:173-174) is skipped.
functions and classes remain nil/empty through sort/deduplicate (js.go:202-213).
Predicted wrong output: FileStructure.Functions == [] and FileStructure.Classes == [] despite `foo` and `Bar` being ordinary top-level declarations a plain regex scan would find.
Expected/documented behavior per file header (js.go:27-29): AST failure "degrades to (or supplements with) the former line-oriented regex extraction — so symbol coverage never regresses."
- **Blast radius:** jsSymbolsFromAST is called only from parse() in js.go (the sole caller found via grep). parse() backs both Parse() and ParseExt(), which are the JSParser's Parser-interface entry points used by the file-structure generator for every .js/.mjs/.cjs/.jsx/.ts/.tsx/.gs file in a repo — so any file that is both pathologically-nested (or otherwise trips this exact early-return path) and contains real top-level functions/classes silently loses all AST-invisible symbols with no fallback, propagating incomplete FileStructure data to every downstream consumer of runecho's index (locate/structure/diff/guard) for that file. In practice the nest-depth trigger is rare/adversarial, but the same hasError=false-on-early-return shape also applies to the Parse()-error/nil-tree branch (js.go:284-286), which is more plausible on genuinely malformed real-world files.
- **Fix direction:** Make jsSymbolsFromAST return hasError=true (or otherwise signal "regex fallback needed") on both early-return paths (nest-depth-exceeded and Parse()-error/nil-tree), not just on tree.RootNode().HasError(), so parse()'s existing union-fallback logic at js.go:163 fires for these cases too.

### F73. `internal/parser/js.go:281` — jsSymbolsFromAST
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** inverted-condition
- **Contract violated:** Doc comment (lines 27-29): 'this degrades to (or supplements with) the former line-oriented regex extraction — so symbol coverage never regresses.' The caller (parse, line 163) only unions the regex fallback when hasError is true.
- **Hypothesis:** Input: a .js file with a normal top-level `function foo() {}` plus, anywhere else in the file, bracket/paren/brace nesting deeper than maxParseNestDepth (1000), e.g. 1001 nested `[`. exceedsNestDepth trips at line 279, jsSymbolsFromAST returns (nil, nil, nil, nil, false) instead of (nil, nil, nil, nil, true). Back in parse(), hasError == false so the regex fallback (extractFunctions(noComments)) at line 173 never runs. FileStructure.Functions ends up nil/empty, silently missing 'foo', instead of containing 'foo' as the regex fallback would produce and as the doc comment guarantees.
- **Trace:** Input source: "function foo() {}\n" + "[" x1001 + "\n" (1001 nested `[`, one past maxParseNestDepth=1000).

Path: JSParser.ParseExt(src, ".js") [js.go:139] -> parse(source, ".js") [js.go:143] -> jsSymbolsFromAST(source, lang) [js.go:162] -> exceedsNestDepth(src) trips true at the 1001st `[` [js.go:279, parser.go:69-75] -> `return nil, nil, nil, nil, false` [js.go:281] (hasError=false, functions=nil).

Back in parse() [js.go:163]: `if hasError { ... regex fallback ... }` — condition is false, so extractFunctions(noComments) at line 173 is skipped entirely. functions stays nil. FileStructure.Functions ends up nil, even though "foo" is a plain top-level `function foo() {}` that extractFunctions would trivially match via funcDeclRegex.

Predicted wrong output: fs.Functions does not contain "foo" (nil/empty).
Expected/doc-promised output: fs.Functions contains "foo" (regex fallback should have supplemented it, per the "symbol coverage never regresses" doc comment).
- **Blast radius:** Single caller of jsSymbolsFromAST is internal/parser/js.go:162 inside JSParser.parse, which is invoked by JSParser.Parse/ParseExt — the only call sites of those are internal/ir/generator.go:459-461, which is the core file-indexing path used by runecho-ir (repo index/reindex), runecho-guard (dangling-symbol/staleness checks), and the runecho MCP server's `structure`/`locate` truth responses. Any .js/.ts/.jsx/.tsx/.mjs/.cjs file with pathological bracket/paren/brace nesting anywhere in it (even unrelated to real code, e.g. minified data blob or deeply nested array literal) silently loses ALL of its real top-level functions/classes from the index, with no error surfaced to callers beyond a stderr log line.
- **Fix direction:** At internal/parser/js.go:281, return hasError=true instead of false so parse() unions the regex fallback (extractFunctions/extractClasses) exactly as it does for the tree-sitter HasError() case just below.

### F74. `internal/parser/js.go:372` — jsSymbolsFromAST (variable_declarator case)
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** fieldText/nodeText's implicit assumption that a variable_declarator's "name" field, when paired with a directly-recognized function/class value, is always a plain bindable identifier suitable as a symbol name.
- **Hypothesis:** For source `const { name } = function foo(){};` (valid JS — destructures the function object's own `.name` property), the variable_declarator's "name" field is an object_pattern node (`{ name }`), not an identifier. fieldText -> nodeText (lines 434-446) only unquotes `string`-typed nodes and otherwise returns the node's raw source text, so `name` becomes the literal string `"{ name }"` (nonempty). Since childOfType finds the function_expression value and `name != ""`, line 374 calls recordFunc(qualify(prefix, "{ name }"), fn), inserting the garbage entry `"{ name }"` into FileStructure.Functions (and the analogous class branch at line 379-384 produces the same garbage for `const { X } = class {}`) instead of skipping the destructured binding.
- **Trace:** Input source: `const { name } = function foo(){};\n`

Path: jsSymbolsFromAST (internal/parser/js.go:263) walk() hits the variable_declarator case at line 367.
- line 372: `name := fieldText(c, "name", lang, src)` — the declarator's "name" field is the object_pattern node `{ name }` (this is `const {destructure} = value`, not `const identifier = value`).
- fieldText (line 412-414) -> nodeText (line 434-446): n.Type(lang) is "object_pattern", not "string", so the unquote branch is skipped and the node's raw source text is returned verbatim: `"{ name }"`.
- Back at line 373: `childOfType(c, lang, "arrow_function", "function_expression")` finds the function_expression `function foo(){}` as the value child, and `name != ""` (it's `"{ name }"`, nonempty).
- line 374: `recordFunc(qualify(prefix, "{ name }"), fn)` executes, appending `"{ name }"` to `functions`, and recording `hashes["function:{ name }"]` / `lines["function:{ name }"]`.
- The destructuring case is never detected/skipped; the code falls through to `recordFunc` before ever reaching the generic `walk(c, prefix, depth+1)` fallback at line 385 (which is unreachable here due to the `continue` at line 375).

Predicted wrong output: `functions` contains `"{ name }"`.
Expected/correct output: `functions` should NOT contain `"{ name }"` — this declarator has no bindable function name to record (or at most `foo` if the parser wanted to fall back to the function_expression's own name), since `name`/`foo` are not exported top-level function bindings here.
- **Blast radius:** jsSymbolsFromAST has exactly one caller: internal/parser/js.go:162 inside the JSParser's Parse path, which feeds FileStructure.Functions. From there (per codegraph_explore) this flows into internal/ir (Symbol/FileIR/SymbolLocations in internal/ir/storage.go and internal/ir/symbols.go), which is the backing data for: the `runecho-ir map`/`locate` CLI, the MCP `locate`/`structure` tools (internal/mcp/tools_oracle.go), snapshot diffing (internal/snapshot/diff.go symbolSet), and modified-symbol-hash tracking. Net effect: any JS/TS file containing a destructuring-from-function/class-expression pattern (`const { x } = function(){}` or `const { X } = class {}`) pollutes the file's function/class symbol list with a literal `"{ x }"` (or nested-pattern) string, which then shows up in `runecho locate`/`structure` results and IR symbol diffs as a bogus, non-existent symbol.
- **Fix direction:** In the variable_declarator case (js.go ~372-385), check the "name" field's node type is a plain `identifier`/`property_identifier` before treating it as a bindable name (or explicitly detect `object_pattern`/`array_pattern` and skip, or use collectPatternNames the way the top-level export path already does at line ~601) rather than calling fieldText/nodeText which just echoes raw non-identifier source text.

### F75. `internal/parser/js.go:373` — jsSymbolsFromAST (variable_declarator case)
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** jsSymbolsFromAST postcondition/doc comment: 'symbol coverage never regresses' relative to the regex fallback, and the variable_declarator case is documented as capturing any anonymous function/arrow/class value bound to a variable.
- **Hypothesis:** For source `const foo = function* () { yield 1; };`, the value is a `generator_function` node (a real, distinct primary_expression production in grammargen/javascript_grammar.go:789, and already listed by name in this same file's collectExportDefaultValueName at line 638). childOfType(c, lang, "arrow_function", "function_expression") at line 373 omits "generator_function", so `fn` is nil, the recordFunc branch is skipped, and walk() falls through to generic recursion which has no case that ever records a bare generator_function as a symbol. `foo` is silently dropped from FileStructure.Functions with hasError left false (the construct parses cleanly), so the regex fallback in parse() never runs either — and even if it did, funcExprRegex requires literal `function(` immediately with no `*`, so it would not match `function* (` regardless.
- **Trace:** Input: `const foo = function* () { yield 1; };\n`
1. js.go:263 jsSymbolsFromAST walks the AST; hits the `variable_declarator` case at js.go:367.
2. js.go:372-373: `childOfType(c, lang, "arrow_function", "function_expression")` is evaluated against the declarator's value, which tree-sitter parses as a `generator_function` node (distinct type, not "function_expression") — the same distinction this file already treats as real at js.go:638 (`case "function_expression", "generator_function", "class", "class_expression":` in collectExportDefaultValueName).
3. `fn` is nil → the `if fn != nil && name != ""` branch (js.go:373-376) is skipped.
4. Falls through to `childOfType(c, lang, "class", "class_expression")` (js.go:379) → also nil → skipped.
5. Falls through to generic `walk(c, prefix, depth+1)` at js.go:385, recursing into the declarator's children. No switch case anywhere records a bare `generator_function` (only `generator_function_declaration` is handled, at js.go:333, which is the named-declaration form, not this anonymous-expression-bound-to-a-variable form).
6. Result: `functions=[]`, and `tree.RootNode().HasError()` is false (js.go:294) since the construct parses cleanly, so `hasError=false`.
7. Because hasError=false, parser.go's regex-fallback trigger (js.go:161-163) never fires — and even if it did, `funcExprRegex` (js.go:54, `function\s*\(` with no `*`) would not match `function* (` anyway.
Predicted wrong output: `foo` absent from FileStructure.Functions.
Expected/documented output (per js.go:368-370 comment "attribute the function to the bound variable name" and the file's stated coverage-parity contract): `foo` present in Functions.
- **Blast radius:** Single call chain: JSParser.Parse/ParseWithExt (js.go:129-140) -> p.parse (js.go:143) -> jsSymbolsFromAST (js.go:263, called at js.go:162) is the sole producer of FileStructure.Functions for JS/TS/.mjs/.cjs files. Any consumer relying on FileStructure.Functions for symbol truth (runecho locate/structure, guard symbol-existence/dangling-ref checks, hashing/line tracking for drift detection) will silently miss any variable bound to a generator-function expression (`const x = function* () {...}`) in that file — no error surfaced, so it looks like clean coverage rather than a gap.
- **Fix direction:** Add "generator_function" to the childOfType type list at js.go:373 (mirroring the existing precedent at js.go:638), and add a corresponding hash/line-tracking test case for a var-bound generator function expression.

### F76. `internal/parser/js.go:886` — splitTopLevelDeclNames
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** unhandled-postcondition
- **Contract violated:** splitTopLevelDeclNames's precondition assumes decl is 'exactly the substring already isolated by the caller's regex capture ... after const|let|var up to (not including) the statement terminator' — i.e., the complete declarator list for the statement. The call site's regex, exportMultiDeclRegex = `export\s+(?:const|let|var)\s+([^;\n]+)`, excludes newlines from the capture group, so for a declarator list that wraps onto a second line before its terminating `;`, match[1] is truncated mid-list rather than spanning the full statement.
- **Hypothesis:** Given source containing a multi-line multi-name export:
```
export const a = 1,
  b = 2;
```
exportMultiDeclRegex captures match[1] = "a = 1," (stopping at the newline, never reaching `b = 2;`). splitTopLevelDeclNames("a = 1,") is called at line 889, flushes the single comma-delimited segment "a = 1" (yielding name "a") and then an empty trailing segment (yielding nothing), so it returns ["a"] only. The exported name "b" is silently dropped from FileStructure.Exports even though it is a real top-level export, for any multi-line multi-declarator export statement — a case explicitly outside what the regex fallback is documented to guarantee coverage for.
- **Trace:** Function under test: splitTopLevelDeclNames (internal/parser/js.go:953), called from extractExports at line 889 with match[1] from exportMultiDeclRegex (line 83: `export\s+(?:const|let|var)\s+([^;\n]+)`).

Input source:
```
export const a = 1,
  b = 2;
```

Path: exportMultiDeclRegex.FindAllStringSubmatch → match[1] = "a = 1," (regex's `[^;\n]+` stops at the `\n` before `b = 2;`, exactly as hypothesized) → extractExports line 889 calls splitTopLevelDeclNames("a = 1,") → the function correctly splits its (already-truncated) input on the single top-level comma into segments "a = 1" and "" → flush() extracts "a" via declNameRegex from the first segment, and finds no name in the empty trailing segment → returns ["a"] → extractExports returns []string{"a"}, "b" never enters the exports slice.

Predicted wrong output: extractExports drops "b". Expected/correct output if the regex captured the full declarator list: ["a","b"].

Second-order question (does this reach the real, user-facing FileStructure.Exports, given extractExports is only a supplemental/degraded fallback behind AST parsing at js.go:160-200): tested both the healthy-AST case and the AST-error-recovery case.
- **Blast radius:** extractExports() is invoked at js.go:184 (ieHasError union-fallback for any .js/.ts/.tsx/.mjs/.cjs/.jsx/.gs file where tree-sitter's error-recovery kicks in anywhere in the file — e.g. any TS-only syntax appearing in a .js file, or any genuine syntax the reduced grammar chokes on) and at js.go:198 (full regex-only degrade path, used when the tree-sitter grammar fails to load at all). FileStructure.Exports is consumed by internal/ir/generator.go:494 and internal/ir/storage.go:167, i.e. it feeds RunEcho's entire symbol-index/IR pipeline — the same data backing `runecho locate`/`structure` MCP calls and the hallucination-guard's "does this symbol exist" checks. Net effect: any JS/TS file containing (a) a multi-line multi-declarator `export const/let/var` statement and (b) any other AST-parse-recoverable error elsewhere in the file will silently lose one or more real exported names from RunEcho's index — a false negative for symbol existence.
- **Fix direction:** Make exportMultiDeclRegex span newlines up to the terminating `;` (e.g. `(?s)export\s+(?:const|let|var)\s+([^;]+);`), or better, have the regex fallback operate on the statement bounded by matching to the next top-level `;` rather than excluding `\n`, so splitTopLevelDeclNames receives the complete declarator list its contract assumes.

### F77. `internal/parser/python.go:276` — pySymbolsFromAST
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** pySymbolsFromAST's own doc comment (python.go:198-200) and generator.go's mirrored assumption promise 'classes are not hashed (their changes surface through their members, avoiding double-reporting)', but line 276 unconditionally calls recordHash("class:"+full, ...) with spanNode covering the ENTIRE class body (all nested methods included, per the spanNode assignment used for both functions and classes). The caller internal/snapshot/diff.go:computeDiff (reached via Parse -> generator.symbolsFromStructure -> snapshot storage -> DB.Diff/DiffLive) treats every 'kind:name' key uniformly: it flags a symbol Modified whenever both sides have a non-empty hash and the hashes differ (diff.go line 135), with no special-casing for kind=='class'.
- **Hypothesis:** Given a Python file with `class Reader:\n    def fetch(self):\n        return 1` and a later commit that changes ONLY the body of fetch() to `return 2` (no other edit anywhere in the class), `runecho-ir diff`/`truth-trail` reports TWO Modified entries for that single edit: `class:Reader` (because the whole-class span's hash changed since fetch()'s body is inside it) AND `function:Reader.fetch` (the method's own hash changed) — DiffResult.TotalModified is incremented twice and both symbol names are printed in the per-file Modified list, when the intended behavior (per the code's own documented rationale) is exactly one entry for a single method-body edit.
- **Trace:** Input: dirA/reader.py = "class Reader:\n    def fetch(self):\n        return 1\n"; dirB/reader.py = same but "return 2".

Path: parser.PythonParser.Parse (python.go:92) -> pySymbolsFromAST (python.go:203) -> record() for class_definition (python.go:274-277) calls recordHash("class:Reader", spanNode bytes) where spanNode is the WHOLE class body (same spanNode used at line 272 for the nested function_definition "function:Reader.fetch") -> ir.generator.parseFile (generator.go:457-465) -> symbolsFromStructure (generator.go:484-505) builds ir.Symbol{Kind:"class", Name:"Reader", Hash: s.SymbolHashes["class:Reader"]} (non-empty, contradicting the doc comment at python.go:199 "classes are not hashed") alongside ir.Symbol{Kind:"function", Name:"Reader.fetch", Hash: s.SymbolHashes["function:Reader.fetch"]} -> internal/snapshot/diff.go irToMaps (line 59-72) copies both symbols' hashes verbatim into SymbolDelta -> computeDiff (diff.go:75) loop at line 129-141: for key "class:Reader", aSym.Hash="85fd9613..." vs bSym.Hash="954e9c2a..." -> both non-empty and different -> line 135 true -> fd.Modified append, totalModified++ (1st count). For key "function:Reader.fetch", aSym.Hash="9b10fd7e..." vs bSym.Hash="dc8f3977..." -> also both non-empty and different -> line 135 true again -> fd.Modified append, totalModified++ (2nd count).

Predicted wrong output: TotalModified=2, fd.Modified contains both {kind:class,name:Reader} and {kind:function,name:Reader.fetch} for a single method-body edit.
Expected right output (per documented intent, python.go:198-200 / generator.go comment mirrored intent): TotalModified=1, only {kind:function,name:Reader.fetch}.

Actual execution matched the predicted wrong output exactly.</trace>
<parameter name="evidence">Command: `go test ./internal/snapshot/ -run TestFocusReproClassDoubleModified -v` (scratch test at internal/snapshot/zzfocus_repro_test.go, deleted after run; `git status --porcelain` confirmed clean afterward)

Output:

- **Blast radius:** grep-confirmed direct consumers of DiffResult/computeDiff/TotalModified/fd.Modified: cmd/runecho-ir/inspect.go (the `runecho-ir diff` CLI command), internal/snapshot/truthtrail.go (`truth-trail` command, per CLAUDE.md a load-bearing "fused receipt" feature), internal/snapshot/churn.go, internal/mcp/tools_oracle.go (the mcp__runecho__diff MCP tool exposed to agents as the code-truth source per this repo's CLAUDE.md), and cmd/runecho-ir/mapcmd.go. Every Python file with a class containing at least one method inherits this double-count on any method-body-only edit.
- **Fix direction:** In pySymbolsFromAST (python.go:274-277), stop calling recordHash for class_definition (delete/skip line 276) so classes carry no hash — restoring the documented invariant "classes are not hashed (their changes surface through their members)"; alternatively, if class-level hashing is actually wanted (e.g. to catch changes to the class signature/decorators only), exclude nested def bodies from the class's hashed span and add an explicit kind=="class" carve-out in diff.go's Modified check to avoid double-counting with member diffs.

### F78. `internal/parser/python.go:282` — pySymbolsFromAST
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** pySymbolsFromAST's postcondition guarantees functions/classes are dot-qualified names for nested scopes (e.g. 'Reader.fetch'), and this qualified string is propagated unchanged through Parse -> generator.symbolsFromStructure into Symbol.Name, which cmd/runecho-ir/inspect.go's claim-check command (lines 404-411) uses verbatim as the key set `knownSymbols[s.Name]=true` for kind in {"function","class"}. The caller's matching input, `claims.ExtractSymbolRefs` (internal/claims/claims.go), extracts backtick-quoted identifiers from arbitrary prose text; its backtick pattern permits but does not require a qualifying prefix, so a prose reference to a method by its bare/leaf name alone (the natural way to refer to a method in English) is looked up directly against knownSymbols with no qualification.
- **Hypothesis:** For a Python class `class Reader:\n    def fetchData(self): ...` (mixed-case name so it passes claims.IsCodeSymbol's hasUpper&&hasLower filter), pySymbolsFromAST records the qualified name 'Reader.fetchData', which becomes knownSymbols["Reader.fetchData"]=true and nothing else. A truth-trail input text file containing the sentence: `` Updated `fetchData` to retry on failure. `` extracts refs["fetchData"] via backtickRe. Since knownSymbols has no unqualified "fetchData" key, `runecho-ir claims-check` reports a Mismatch for "fetchData" and exits ExitNoData(1), falsely flagging a real, unchanged, correctly-referenced symbol as an unresolved/stale claim.
- **Trace:** Input: a Python file `class Reader:\n    def fetchData(self):\n        return 1\n` and a prose file containing the line `` Updated `fetchData` to retry on failure. ``

Path:
1. internal/parser/python.go:263-283 (`record`, inside `pySymbolsFromAST`) — for the nested `function_definition` node, `full := qualify(prefix, name)` with `prefix="Reader"`, `name="fetchData"` → `full = "Reader.fetchData"`; appended to `functions` and never as bare `"fetchData"`.
2. internal/ir/generator.go:469/484 (`symbolsFromStructure`) — copies `s.Name` from the parser's `functions`/`classes` arrays verbatim into `Symbol{Name: "Reader.fetchData", Kind: "function"}`. Verified via `.ai/ir.json`: `"symbols":[..., {"name":"Reader.fetchData","kind":"function", ...}]` — no bare `"fetchData"` entry anywhere in the IR.
3. cmd/runecho-ir/inspect.go:404-411 (`runValidateClaims`) — builds `knownSymbols` keyed by `s.Name` for kind∈{function,class}: `knownSymbols["Reader.fetchData"]=true` only.
4. internal/claims/claims.go:15 (`backtickRe`) + inspect.go:414 (`claims.ExtractSymbolRefs(text)`) — the backtick pattern requires only a leading identifier with *optional* dotted suffix, so `` `fetchData` `` extracts `refs["fetchData"]` (no qualifying prefix required or synthesized).
5. inspect.go:420-424 — `if !knownSymbols["fetchData"]` → true (key absent) → appended to `mismatches`.
6. `runValidateClaims` returns `ExitNoData` (1) whenever `len(mismatches) > 0`.

Predicted wrong output: exit code 1, JSON mismatch `{"ref":"fetchData", ...}` for a symbol that genuinely, unchanged, exists as `Reader.fetchData`.
Expected/correct output: exit code 0, no mismatch (the method exists and is correctly referenced by its natural bare name).

The same flaw independently exists in `internal/snapshot/truthtrail.go`'s `liveSymbolSet` (also keys by bare `s.Name`, exact-match against `ExtractSymbolRefs` output) — used by `runecho-ir truth-trail --text=<file>`, so the "unresolved-symbol findings from runecho-guard-adjacent truth-trail" verification-stop path is affected too.
- **Blast radius:** Two direct callers hit the exact same exact-match defect independently: (1) `runValidateClaims` (cmd/runecho-ir/inspect.go:404-424, invoked via `runecho-ir validate-claims --text=<file>`), and (2) `TruthTrail`'s stale-claims section (internal/snapshot/truthtrail.go: `liveSymbolSet` + the `if !known[sym]` check, invoked via `runecho-ir truth-trail --text=<file>`, per CLAUDE.md's documented Truth-Trail workflow and the repo's own "truth-trail" memory node). Any Python (or JS/TS/Go) codebase with nested/method symbols referenced by bare/leaf name in prose — the natural way English refers to a method — will spuriously fail both commands, exiting non-zero (ExitNoData) and flagging real, unchanged symbols as hallucinated/stale.
- **Fix direction:** In both `runValidateClaims`'s `knownSymbols` build and `liveSymbolSet`, also index each qualified symbol by its dotted leaf/suffix (e.g. add `"fetchData"` as well as `"Reader.fetchData"`, guarding for collisions), or normalize `ExtractSymbolRefs`' backtick matches by checking suffix-match against known qualified names — mirroring the same last-dotted-segment matching already implemented for `locate` in `mcp/tools_oracle.go`'s `symbolMatches`.

### F79. `internal/snapshot/churn.go:17` — Churn
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** Churn's docstring (line 10): "Returns an empty ChurnReport (no error) when fewer than 2 snapshots exist."
- **Hypothesis:** Churn(repoID, n) called against a repo with exactly 1 stored snapshot should, per the docstring, return an empty ChurnReport (i.e. the zero value). What it actually returns is ChurnReport{SnapshotCount: 1, Root: <that snapshot's Root>} — a non-zero, partially-populated report, not an empty one. A caller that checks reflect.DeepEqual(report, ChurnReport{}) or similar 'is this report empty' logic based on the doc would get false when SnapshotCount==1, even though the doc says exactly this case yields 'empty'.
- **Trace:** Concrete input: repoID enrolled fresh, exactly 1 snapshot saved (label "manual1", root "/some/root"), then Churn(repoID, 10) called.
Path: Churn line 12 db.List(repoID,10) -> returns 1 SnapshotMeta -> line 17 len(metas)==1 < 2 is true -> line 18 report := ChurnReport{SnapshotCount: 1} -> line 19-21 len(metas)==1 so report.Root = metas[0].Root ("/some/root") -> line 22 return report, nil.
Predicted wrong output (per hypothesis): ChurnReport{SnapshotCount:1, Root:"/some/root"}, all other fields zero — NOT equal to ChurnReport{} (the zero value the docstring calls "empty").
Expected per docstring: ChurnReport{} (all-zero, including SnapshotCount==0), nil error.
Actual observed output (from executed test): report = {Root:/some/root SnapshotCount:1 DiffCount:0 Since:0001-01-01 00:00:00 +0000 UTC Until:0001-01-01 00:00:00 +0000 UTC Files:[] Symbols:[]} — matches the predicted wrong output exactly. reflect.DeepEqual(report, ChurnReport{}) is false.
- **Blast radius:** Callers of Churn(): grep shows it is invoked from cmd/runecho-ir's `churn` CLI subcommand and from ChurnPayload/FormatChurn/FormatChurnCompact (all in the same file) which explicitly guard on `SnapshotCount < 2` rather than on emptiness — so those existing internal callers are unaffected by the doc/behavior mismatch. Risk is to any *future or external* caller that trusts the docstring literally and tests for zero-value/DeepEqual-empty to detect the "fewer than 2 snapshots" case instead of checking SnapshotCount < 2, which would incorrectly treat the 1-snapshot case as "populated."
- **Fix direction:** Either fix the code to return ChurnReport{} unconditionally when len(metas) < 2 (dropping the SnapshotCount/Root partial population), or fix the docstring to say "returns a report with only SnapshotCount (and Root, if one snapshot exists) populated" — whichever matches the intended contract; then audit callers accordingly.

### F80. `internal/snapshot/churn.go:40` — Churn
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** impossible-state
- **Contract violated:** fd.Status != "unchanged" is presented as a live filter but is always true for every fd reached at this line
- **Hypothesis:** diff.Files (built by computeDiff in diff.go:98-116) never contains an entry with Status=="unchanged": diff.go:114-116 explicitly `continue`s past unchanged files before appending to fileDiffs. So every fd churn.go:39 iterates over already has Status in {"added","removed","modified"}, meaning the check `fd.Status != "unchanged"` at line 40 can never evaluate false — it is dead code masquerading as a guard.
