If a future change to computeDiff (or a hand-built DiffResult passed through some other path) ever emits an "unchanged" FileDiff, this line would silently start doing real filtering work that reviewers currently believe is already being exercised by tests; today it filters zero elements.
- **Trace:** Input: two snapshots for repo "r" — s1: a.go@hash"a1" symbols{Alpha}, b.go@hash"b1" symbols{Beta}; s2: a.go@hash"a2" symbols{Alpha,Gamma} (changed), b.go@hash"b1" symbols{Beta} (UNCHANGED, same hash).
Path: Churn (churn.go:35) -> db.Diff(metas[0],metas[1]) (diff.go:13-31) -> computeDiff (diff.go:75-164). For path="b.go": aHash==bHash=="b1" -> status="unchanged" (diff.go:108-109) -> `if status=="unchanged" { continue }` (diff.go:114-116) skips it, never appended to fileDiffs. For path="a.go": aHash"a1"!=bHash"a2" -> status="modified", appended to fileDiffs.
Back in Churn (churn.go:39-42): `for _, fd := range diff.Files` iterates only over {a.go, status="modified"}. `fd.Status != "unchanged"` evaluates true (as it always will, since no "unchanged" fd can ever be present) and increments fileChanges["a.go"].
Predicted output: diff.Files has exactly 1 entry (a.go, modified); b.go never appears; Churn report Files == [{Path:a.go, Changes:1}]. Expected/"correct" output is identical (no wrong-output scenario is possible given this data flow) — this is precisely what makes the guard provably dead rather than a live bug.
- **Blast radius:** 2 callers reach Churn and are therefore affected by (but not harmed by) this dead check: internal/snapshot/truthtrail.go:66 (db.Churn call feeding runecho-ir truth-trail) and cmd/runecho-ir/inspect.go:352 (db.Churn call backing `runecho-ir churn`). Both currently get correct results; impact is nil today.
- **Fix direction:** Either delete the dead `if fd.Status != "unchanged"` guard at churn.go:40 (unwrap its body unconditionally) and add a one-line comment noting diff.Files is pre-filtered by computeDiff, or, if defensive robustness against a future hand-built DiffResult is wanted, keep it but add a comment explaining it's currently unreachable-false by construction of computeDiff (diff.go:114-116) — don't leave it silently implying it does live filtering work today.

### F81. `internal/snapshot/churn.go:121` — ChurnPayload
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** ChurnPayload's own docstring (churn.go lines 104-106): "entries filtered to minChanges (matching FormatChurn's 'hot' threshold) so the JSON and text outputs agree on what counts as hot"
- **Hypothesis:** Call runecho-ir churn --json --min-changes 3 against a ChurnReport whose r.Files = [{Path:"a.go",Changes:3}, {Path:"b.go",Changes:2}]. hot_files in the returned JSON is filtered with the caller-supplied minChanges=3, so it contains only a.go (1 entry). But the same payload's "summary" field is produced by FormatChurnCompact(r) at churn.go:121, which hardcodes its own threshold of 2 at churn.go:199/204 and ignores the minChanges argument entirely — so summary reads "CHURN: 2 hot files, ..." while hot_files has length 1. A single JSON object simultaneously claims 2 hot files (summary) and lists 1 (hot_files array).
- **Trace:** Input: ChurnReport{SnapshotCount:2, DiffCount:1, Files:[{Path:"a.go",Changes:3},{Path:"b.go",Changes:2}]}, called as ChurnPayload(r, minChanges=3).

Path:
- churn.go:108-113 loop filters r.Files by f.Changes >= minChanges(3) → hotFiles = [a.go] (b.go excluded, Changes=2 < 3). len=1.
- churn.go:121 "summary": FormatChurnCompact(r) — note: minChanges is NOT passed.
- churn.go:196-201 inside FormatChurnCompact: hardcoded `if f.Changes >= 2` → both a.go(3) and b.go(2) satisfy >=2 → hotFiles count = 2.
- churn.go:209-212 formats "CHURN: 2 hot files, 0 hot symbols across 1 diffs (...)".

Result: returned map has "hot_files" array of length 1 (only a.go) while "summary" string says "2 hot files" — a single JSON object making self-contradictory claims about the same run, exactly as hypothesized.
- **Blast radius:** `grep -rn "ChurnPayload(" --include=*.go` shows ChurnPayload is called from the CLI churn --json command path (cmd layer) which serializes it directly to stdout for `runecho-ir churn --json`. Every invocation of that JSON subcommand with a non-default --min-changes (anything other than the hardcoded 2) produces a payload where summary and hot_files/hot_symbols disagree — any downstream consumer/script parsing both fields (or a human comparing them) gets inconsistent counts.
- **Fix direction:** Change FormatChurnCompact to accept minChanges (like FormatChurn does) and call it as FormatChurnCompact(r, minChanges) from ChurnPayload:121, updating the two hardcoded `>= 2` comparisons at churn.go:199 and churn.go:204 to `>= minChanges`.

### F82. `internal/snapshot/churn.go:367` — runChurn
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** unhandled-postcondition
- **Contract violated:** inspect.go:330 defines --min-changes as "minimum diffs a file/symbol must appear in to be considered hot" — a command-wide flag — but FormatChurnCompact provides no parameter to receive it
- **Hypothesis:** Run runecho-ir churn --compact --min-changes 10 against a report with several files whose Changes are 2-4 (all below the user's requested 10 threshold). The --compact branch at inspect.go:367 calls snapshot.FormatChurnCompact(report) without passing *minChanges anywhere, and FormatChurnCompact hardcodes threshold 2 internally (churn.go:199,204), so the output reports those files as hot ("CHURN: N hot files...") even though the user explicitly asked for a threshold of 10. The exact same invocation with --json or the default text mode correctly suppresses those files as not-hot at threshold 10 in hot_files/Hot files section, so --compact silently disagrees with the other two output modes for the identical underlying report.
- **Trace:** Input: ChurnReport{SnapshotCount:5, DiffCount:4, Files:[{a.go,Changes:4},{b.go,Changes:3},{c.go,Changes:2}], Symbols:[{Foo,Changes:3}]}, minChanges=10 (as if from `--min-changes 10`).
Path for --compact: inspect.go:367 `fmt.Println(snapshot.FormatChurnCompact(report))` -> churn.go:188 FormatChurnCompact(r) -> churn.go:199 `if f.Changes >= 2 { hotFiles++ }` (loop over a.go/b.go/c.go, all >=2) -> hotFiles=3; churn.go:204 `if s.Changes >= 2` -> hotSymbols=1 -> churn.go:209 returns "CHURN: 3 hot files, 1 hot symbol across 4 diffs (...)".
Path for default text: inspect.go:369 `snapshot.FormatChurn(report, *minChanges)` with minChanges=10 -> churn.go:149 `if f.Changes >= minChanges` (4,3,2 all < 10) -> zero hot files -> output correctly shows "Below threshold: 3 files changed in fewer than 10 of 4 diffs." and omits any "Hot files" section.
Path for --json: inspect.go:360 `snapshot.ChurnPayload(report, *minChanges)` with minChanges=10 -> churn.go:110/116 same >=10 filter -> hot_files=[], hot_symbols=[].
Predicted wrong output (--compact): "CHURN: 3 hot files, 1 hot symbol across 4 diffs (2026-01-01 → 2026-01-05)" — disagrees with the other two modes which report 0 hot files/symbols at the same threshold.
- **Blast radius:** Single production call site: cmd/runecho-ir/inspect.go:367, invoked only by the `runecho-ir churn --compact` CLI subcommand (documented in cmd/runecho-ir/main.go:29,109). No other internal callers of snapshot.FormatChurnCompact (grep across the repo shows only the definition, this one call site, and its unit test churn_test.go:239 which itself doesn't pass minChanges either, consistent with the missing-parameter design flaw).
- **Fix direction:** Change FormatChurnCompact's signature to `FormatChurnCompact(r ChurnReport, minChanges int) string`, replace the two hardcoded `>= 2` checks (churn.go:199, 204) with `>= minChanges`, and update the call site at inspect.go:367 to `snapshot.FormatChurnCompact(report, *minChanges)` (plus update churn_test.go's existing call).

### F83. `internal/snapshot/db.go:49` — OpenFast
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** OpenFast's postcondition/doc frames it as being for 'latency-sensitive read paths' that 'only read' (db.go:44-47), promising pragmas+migration are 'both cheap when the schema is current' — but it unconditionally calls db.migrate() (line 61) with no fast-path check skipping migration when the caller only intends to read.
- **Hypothesis:** cmd/runecho-guard/dangling.go:122 (openLatestSnapshot) and cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:665 (lookupSymbolsFor) call OpenFast on the PreToolUse-hook / per-edit path, documented by their own comments as needing to 'stay cheap' (main.go:663-664) and firing 'on every edit' — but the first invocation after any schema-version bump (SchemaVersion incremented, e.g. v7->v8 in this repo's own recent history) executes the full migrations[] loop (schema DDL + transactional commits) synchronously inside what both call sites' comments assert is a fast, read-only path, producing a synchronous multi-statement write transaction on a hook invocation the caller never expected to write.
- **Trace:** Concrete input: a snapshot DB file created with only migrations v1..v7 applied (user_version=7), simulating a store on disk from before the current binary's SchemaVersion (8) was reached (this repo's own history: v7->v8 for symbols.sig_hash, migrateV8 at db.go:295-300).

Interprocedural path exercised: cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:665 (lookupSymbolsFor, comment: "this read path fires on every edit and must stay cheap") / cmd/runecho-guard/dangling.go:122 (openLatestSnapshot, comment: "still on a latency-sensitive path") -> snapshot.OpenFast (db.go:49) -> db.setPragmas() (db.go:90, cheap) -> db.migrate() (db.go:61 -> db.go:134) -> loop `for v:=current; v<len(migrations); v++` (db.go:142) executes because current(7) < len(migrations)(8) -> tx:=db.conn.Begin() (db.go:143) -> migrations[7]=migrateV8(tx) runs `ALTER TABLE symbols ADD COLUMN sig_hash ...` (db.go:297) -> tx.Exec("PRAGMA user_version = 8") (db.go:152) -> tx.Commit() (db.go:156).

Predicted wrong output (per hypothesis): a hook invocation documented as read-only/"stay cheap" instead performs a synchronous multi-statement write transaction (schema DDL + commit) the first time it runs against a store that predates the binary's current SchemaVersion.
Expected/"right" output if the doc's contract held: OpenFast on a read-only-intent path would either skip migration entirely or be guarded so no write transaction occurs.

Actual observed output matched the predicted wrong behavior exactly: user_version flipped 7->8 inside OpenFast, with a measurable write (DB file grew, ALTER TABLE ran, PRAGMA user_version updated, transaction committed) all inside the call that both call sites' own comments assert must "stay cheap" and is read-only.
- **Blast radius:** 3 call sites, all on the PreToolUse-hook / per-edit path, all documented by their own comments as needing to be cheap/read-only: cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:287, cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:665 (lookupSymbolsFor), cmd/runecho-guard/dangling.go:122 (openLatestSnapshot). Every one of them will synchronously run the full pending-migrations write transaction on the first hook invocation after any SchemaVersion bump (verified via `grep -rn "OpenFast(" --include=*.go .`, no codegraph .codegraph/ dir present in this checkout so grep was used per the fallback instruction).
- **Fix direction:** Make OpenFast read-only with respect to schema: cheaply check `PRAGMA user_version` against `SchemaVersion` and, if behind, return a distinguishable "stale schema, needs writer-side migration" condition (like the existing ErrSchemaNewer path) instead of calling db.migrate(); let Open() (the writer/CLI/reindex path) remain the only path that actually performs migrations.

### F84. `internal/snapshot/db.go:49` — OpenFast
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** unhandled-postcondition
- **Contract violated:** OpenFast can return the sentinel error ErrSchemaNewer (via migrate(), db.go:140) which the DB.go comment for ErrSchemaNewer (108-112) says callers 'must still surface loudly' even in an otherwise fail-open design, because it 'never resolves on its own.' Two of OpenFast's three callers (main.go:287/665 via lookupSymbolsFor, and dangling.go's openLatestSnapshot) exist, but only lookupSymbolsFor actually checks errors.Is(err, snapshot.ErrSchemaNewer) and surfaces a Warn string.
- **Hypothesis:** cmd/runecho-guard/dangling.go:122-125 (openLatestSnapshot, called from checkDanglingRefs and checkDuplicateDefs) discards the OpenFast error entirely without an errors.Is(err, snapshot.ErrSchemaNewer) check, returning ok=false identically to a missing-store or unenrolled-repo case. When a guard binary older than the store's schema runs a delete/rename edit, checkDanglingRefs silently returns nil warnings instead of surfacing the 'guard is older than the store, rebuild it' advisory that lookupSymbolsFor gives for the same underlying condition on the same invocation — the user gets zero-warning silence on a dangling-reference deletion specifically because this call site (unlike its sibling) does not consume the documented ErrSchemaNewer postcondition, a gap already flagged in-repo as a 'KNOWN GAP, not fixed here' comment at dangling.go:103-109.
- **Trace:** Concrete input: a history.db migrated to schema v9 while this binary understands v8 (SchemaVersion=len(migrations)=8), for an enrolled repo "r" with snapshot symbol {KnownFunc}, and a delete-edit removing KnownFunc from known.go.

Path A (lookupSymbolsFor, main.go:654): runechoDir()->os.Stat ok->snapshot.OpenFast(dbPath) [db.go:49] -> migrate() [db.go:132: "db schema version 9 is newer than this binary supports (8)...: %w", ErrSchemaNewer] -> err returned to main.go:665 -> errors.Is(err, ErrSchemaNewer) true (main.go:667) -> returns lookupResult{Warn: "runecho-guard is older than the RunEcho store — symbol validation is DISABLED until the guard binary is rebuilt (bash install.sh)."}

Path B (checkDanglingRefs, dangling.go:148): checkDanglingRefs -> openLatestSnapshot(dir, filePath) [dangling.go:110] -> same snapshot.OpenFast(dbPath) call (dangling.go:122) returns the same ErrSchemaNewer-wrapped err -> dangling.go:123-125 `if err != nil { return nil, 0, "", false }` (NO errors.Is check) -> checkDanglingRefs:153 `if !ok { return nil }` -> caller main.go:486 gets `dangling = nil` -> zero warnings emitted for a real dangling-reference deletion, indistinguishable from "no store"/"unenrolled repo".

Predicted wrong output: checkDanglingRefs returns nil (no warning, no advisory) despite the identical ErrSchemaNewer condition that produces a Warn in lookupSymbolsFor for the same store/repo/edit.
Expected (per the documented contract at db.go:108-112, "must still surface loudly") right output: some non-nil signal (matching or equivalent to lookupSymbolsFor's Warn) so the user isn't left in zero-warning silence on a dangling-reference deletion.
- **Blast radius:** grep confirms two call sites share openLatestSnapshot: checkDanglingRefs (dangling.go:152, invoked from main.go:486 on delete-edits) and checkDuplicateDefs (duplicate.go:93, invoked from main.go:505 on add-edits) — both silently lose the ErrSchemaNewer advisory that lookupSymbolsFor (main.go:665, invoked main.go:417) does surface for the same underlying store/binary-version mismatch on the same guard invocation.
- **Fix direction:** In openLatestSnapshot, check errors.Is(err, snapshot.ErrSchemaNewer) after OpenFast and thread a signal (e.g. an extra bool/string return, or a package-level warning channel consumed by main.go's hook-mode output) back to checkDanglingRefs/checkDuplicateDefs so a schema-newer condition produces the same "rebuild the guard binary" advisory as lookupSymbolsFor, instead of collapsing into fail-open ok=false.

### F85. `internal/snapshot/db.go:139` — migrate
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** migrate's own precondition states 'PRAGMA user_version reflects a value for which all migrations[0..user_version-1] have already been fully applied' and its guard only rejects current > len(migrations); it implicitly assumes current is always >= 0, but nothing in this file (or in SQLite itself) enforces that.
- **Hypothesis:** The store's PRAGMA user_version is 0 initially but nothing prevents it from being negative (e.g. an operator or another tool runs `sqlite3 store.db 'PRAGMA user_version = -1'`, or the header bytes get corrupted to a value read as negative). db.migrate() reads current = -1 at line 136. The check `if current > len(migrations)` (line 139) is false for -1, so it falls through. The loop `for v := current; v < len(migrations); v++` (line 142) starts with v = -1, and `migrations[v](tx)` at line 147 indexes the migrations slice with a negative index, which panics with 'index out of range [-1]' instead of returning the intended wrapped error — crashing the calling process (Open/OpenFast) rather than degrading gracefully.
- **Trace:** internal/snapshot/db.go:134-160, func (db *DB) migrate():
Input: PRAGMA user_version = -1 on an otherwise valid, fully-migrated store.
1. Line 136: `db.conn.QueryRow("PRAGMA user_version").Scan(&current)` -> current = -1.
2. Line 139: `if current > len(migrations)` -> -1 > 8 -> false. Falls through (guard does not catch negative values).
3. Line 142: `for v := current; v < len(migrations); v++` -> v initialized to -1.
4. Line 147: `migrations[v](tx)` -> `migrations[-1]` -> Go runtime slice-index panic: "index out of range [-1]".
Predicted wrong output: unrecovered panic crashing the calling process (Open/OpenFast), instead of the intended `fmt.Errorf(...): %w", ErrSchemaNewer)`-style graceful error return.
Expected/correct behavior: migrate() should return a wrapped error (e.g. "db schema version -1 is invalid") without panicking.
- **Blast radius:** Every caller that opens a snapshot DB is exposed since migrate() runs unconditionally in both Open() and OpenFast(): cmd/runecho-ir/helpers.go:31 (snapshot.Open), cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:119 (snapshot.Open) and :287/:665 (snapshot.OpenFast), cmd/runecho-guard/dangling.go:122 (snapshot.OpenFast), cmd/runecho-mcp/main.go:32 (snapshot.Open). None of these recover from a panic in migrate(), so any store with a negative user_version crashes the CLI, the guard hook (defeating its fail-open design), and the MCP server outright.
- **Fix direction:** In migrate(), change the guard at line 139 to `if current < 0 || current > len(migrations)` and return a wrapped error for the negative case instead of falling through to the indexing loop.

### F86. `internal/snapshot/registry.go:162` — runRepoRemove (cmd/runecho-ir/repo.go)
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** RemoveRepo's documented protective contract (registry.go:156) — 'if the repo has snapshots, returns a descriptive error and the transaction is rolled back — no row is deleted' — is never invoked by any production caller; instead runRepoRemove calls PurgeRepo, whose contract explicitly has 'no snapshot-count guard like RemoveRepo has' and is an 'irreversible, unconditional delete ... of everything'.
- **Hypothesis:** Running `runecho-ir repo rm myrepo` (or its `remove` alias) on a repo that has existing history/snapshots does not hit RemoveRepo's protective snapshot-count check at all — it calls db.PurgeRepo(repo.ID) at line 162, which unconditionally deletes refs, symbols, files, and every snapshot for that repo id before deleting the repos row, then prints "Removed myrepo (id=N) and its history." A user who expects `rm` (the CLI verb that mirrors RemoveRepo's protective semantics) to refuse deletion of a repo with snapshot history instead loses all indexed history irrecoverably with no confirmation prompt and no distinct `purge` command available to opt into that unconditional behavior — RemoveRepo itself is dead code, reachable only from db_test.go, not from any CLI path.
- **Trace:** Input: `runecho-ir repo rm myrepo` (or `remove` alias) where `myrepo` has snapshot history.
Path: cmd/runecho-ir/repo.go:26 dispatch (`case "rm", "remove":`) -> runRepoRemove (repo.go:144) -> repo.go:154 db.GetRepoByName(args[0]) resolves the repo -> repo.go:162 `db.PurgeRepo(repo.ID)` (NOT db.RemoveRepo) -> internal/snapshot/registry.go:177 PurgeRepo unconditionally executes DELETE statements for refs, symbols, files, snapshots, then the repos row (registry.go:183-197), commits, and repo.go:165 prints "Removed myrepo (id=N) and its history."
RemoveRepo (registry.go:156-173), which contains the protective `SELECT COUNT(*) FROM snapshots ... if n>0 return error` guard, is never on this call path — grep confirms its only callers are internal/snapshot/db_test.go (TestRemoveRepo_WithSnapshots_Errors, TestRemoveRepo_NoSnapshots_Succeeds). No CLI subcommand or code path other than tests calls RemoveRepo.
Predicted wrong output: history is deleted unconditionally, no error, no confirmation, despite RemoveRepo's documented contract ("if the repo has snapshots, returns a descriptive error ... no row is deleted") — that contract is simply not consulted.
Expected (per RemoveRepo's own contract, if it were wired to `rm`): `runecho-ir repo rm` on a repo with snapshots should refuse and require a distinct purge action.
- **Blast radius:** Single call site: cmd/runecho-ir/repo.go:162 (runRepoRemove), reached via the CLI dispatch case "rm","remove" at repo.go:26 — this is the only production entry point to either RemoveRepo or PurgeRepo's repo-deletion behavior for the `repo rm`/`repo remove` user command. Any user or script invoking `runecho-ir repo rm <name>` on a repo with existing snapshot/index history is affected — irreversible loss of all refs/symbols/files/snapshots for that repo id, no confirmation, no distinct opt-in "purge" verb exists.
- **Fix direction:** In runRepoRemove (cmd/runecho-ir/repo.go:162), call db.RemoveRepo(repo.ID) first; only fall back to db.PurgeRepo (behind an explicit --force/--purge flag or a separate `repo purge` subcommand) if the user opts into deleting history, matching RemoveRepo's documented protective contract.

### F87. `internal/snapshot/registry.go:180` — ParseStagedDiff (called from cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:180, arg = ResolveRepo's repoRoot)
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** ResolveRepo postcondition/invariant: 'repoRoot is always repo.Path (per doc lines 354-356), never the caller's actual dir — callers needing the live cwd must ignore repoRoot.' Also explicit doc at registry.go:354-356: 'callers that need a different directory (e.g. the user's actual cwd for live IR generation) should ignore repoRoot and use their own path.'
- **Hypothesis:** Run runecho-guard's pre-commit hook from a claudew/codexw linked worktree (e.g. this session's own worktree /home/ericm/personal_projects/runecho/claude-20260703-070141) where only the 'master' worktree was ever enrolled via `runecho-ir repo add .`. db.ResolveRepo(cwd) hits registry.go tier-1 single-match path (line 379-380, len(repos)==1) and returns repoRoot = the enrolled master worktree's repo.Path, NOT cwd. main.go:180 then calls guard.ParseStagedDiff(diffCtx, repoRoot), which execs `git -C <master-worktree-path> diff --cached --unified=0` (internal/guard/diff.go:34) — i.e. it inspects the STAGED DIFF OF THE MASTER WORKTREE, not the worktree where `git commit` is actually being run. Any symbols staged for commit in the current worktree are invisible to the guard (diffs comes back empty or reflects unrelated staged changes in master), so the pre-commit hallucinated-symbol check silently validates nothing for every worktree except the one originally enrolled — a false negative that lets a hallucinated symbol commit clean through the guard.
- **Trace:** Setup: bare repo `bare.git` with two linked worktrees off it — `master-wt` (enrolled) and `feature-wt` (never enrolled, mirrors this session's own linked-worktree layout). Only `master-wt` is registered via `db.EnrollRepo("myrepo", master, "", 0)`, then one `ResolveRepo(master)` call backfills `common_dir`.

Input: `git add hallucinated.go` (contains `func UsesGhost() { GhostFunc() }`) staged inside `feature-wt` only; `master-wt` has nothing staged.

Path:
1. cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:134-139 — `cwd = feature-wt`; `repo, repoRoot, ok := db.ResolveRepo(cwd)`.
2. internal/snapshot/registry.go:373-380 (ResolveRepo tier 1) — `gitutil.CommonDir(feature-wt)` matches the bare repo's shared common-dir; `GetReposByCommonDir` returns exactly 1 row (only master-wt enrolled) → `len(repos)==1` branch returns `repos[0].Path` = master-wt, **not** feature-wt, per the documented contract at registry.go:354-356 ("repoRoot is the enrolled path (repo.Path) in all tiers").
3. main.go:180 — `guard.ParseStagedDiff(diffCtx, repoRoot)` with `repoRoot = master-wt`.
4. internal/guard/diff.go:34 — execs `git -C <master-wt> diff --cached --unified=0`, which is empty (nothing staged there).

Predicted wrong output: `diffs == []` (0 files), so main.go:196 `len(diffs)==0` short-circuits and the guard exits 0 (silent pass) even though `hallucinated.go` calling nonexistent `GhostFunc()` is staged for commit in feature-wt.
Expected/correct output: the guard should see feature-wt's staged diff (1 file, `hallucinated.go`) and run the hallucinated-symbol check against it.

Actual observed output (test log): `resolved repo=myrepo repoRoot=.../master-wt (feature cwd=.../feature-wt)`; `partial=false diffs=[]`; ground truth `ParseStagedDiff(feature-wt)` independently confirmed 1 staged file (`hallucinated.go`). Matches the predicted wrong output exactly.
- **Blast radius:** `grep -rn "ParseStagedDiff(" --include=*.go .` (excluding tests) shows exactly one call site: cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:180 — the pre-commit hallucinated-symbol check. The same wrong `repoRoot` also feeds `.runechoguardignore` lookup at main.go:201 (filepath.Join(repoRoot, ...)), which reads/writes the ignorefile from the wrong worktree too. Any repo laid out as a bare-repo + multiple linked worktrees (this repo's own claudew/codexw pattern per CLAUDE.md) where only one worktree was ever `runecho-ir repo add`-ed is affected: every commit made from any other linked worktree gets a silent guard pass regardless of what's actually staged.
- **Fix direction:** In cmd/runecho-guard/main.go, pass `cwd` (or `gitutil.TopLevel(cwd)`) to `guard.ParseStagedDiff` and for the ignorefile path — not `repoRoot` — since repoRoot's contract (registry.go:354-356) explicitly says callers needing the actual working directory must ignore it and use their own; only use repoRoot for identity/snapshot lookups keyed by the enrolled repo.

### F88. `internal/snapshot/registry.go:201` — runRepoGuard / main() ignorefile lookup (cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:201)
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** Same ResolveRepo invariant as above: repoRoot equals repo.Path (the enrolled worktree), not the caller's cwd/worktree.
- **Hypothesis:** In the identical linked-worktree scenario, `ignorePath := filepath.Join(repoRoot, ".runechoguardignore")` at main.go:201 builds a path inside the ENROLLED (e.g. master) worktree's directory. A `.runechoguardignore` file that exists in the current (non-enrolled) worktree — the one actually being edited/committed — is never read, and conversely a `.runechoguardignore` present only in the master worktree gets applied to commits made in a different worktree whose ignore intentions may differ. This produces wrong allow/deny behavior for the guard's ignore rules whenever the worktree being committed in differs from the originally-enrolled one.
- **Trace:** Input: bare-style setup — mainDir (git-initialized, committed) enrolled via db.EnrollRepo + SetRepoCommonDir; linkedDir created via `git worktree add` off mainDir, NOT separately enrolled (the realistic claudew scenario — a fresh worktree before `runecho-ir repo add .` is re-run in it). Distinct `.runechoguardignore` files: mainDir has "FromMainWorktree\n", linkedDir has "FromLinkedWorktree\n".

Path: cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:134 `cwd,_ := os.Getwd()` (cwd = linkedDir) -> main.go:139 `repo, repoRoot, ok := db.ResolveRepo(cwd)` -> internal/snapshot/registry.go:373-380 tier-1 fast path: `gitutil.CommonDir(linkedDir)` succeeds and matches mainDir's common-dir; `db.GetReposByCommonDir(commonDir)` returns exactly ONE row (mainDir's enrollment, since linkedDir was never separately enrolled) -> registry.go:379-380 `case len(repos)==1: return repos[0], repos[0].Path, true` — returns repoRoot = mainDir's absolute path, discarding the actual cwd (linkedDir) entirely -> back in main.go:201 `ignorePath := filepath.Join(repoRoot, ".runechoguardignore")` resolves to `<mainDir>/.runechoguardignore`.

Predicted wrong output: ignorePath points at mainDir's ignorefile ("FromMainWorktree") even though the guard process's cwd/worktree is linkedDir. Expected/correct output: ignorePath should point at `<linkedDir>/.runechoguardignore` ("FromLinkedWorktree") — the worktree actually being committed in.

Actual output from execution matched the predicted wrong output exactly.
- **Blast radius:** Two call sites share this defect via db.ResolveRepo's repoRoot: (1) cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:201, consumed by guard.Run at the pre-commit git-hook path (runArgs) — additionally, the SAME repoRoot is used one line earlier at main.go:180 for `guard.ParseStagedDiff(diffCtx, repoRoot)`, so in this scenario the entire staged-diff parse also targets the wrong worktree's index, not just the ignorefile; (2) cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:692 `lookupSymbolsFor`, consumed by the Claude Code PreToolUse hook mode (runHookMode) — same IgnorePath: filepath.Join(repoRoot, ...) pattern. Both are hit any time a linked worktree (e.g. a fresh `claudew` worktree) shares a common-dir with exactly one already-enrolled worktree and has not itself been separately `runecho-ir repo add`-ed — a realistic and, per this user's own CLAUDE.md worktree workflow, common state.
- **Fix direction:** In ResolveRepo's tier-1/tier-3 fallback paths (registry.go ~379-392, 415), stop returning repo.Path as repoRoot when it differs from the caller's actual `dir`; instead return the caller's own git top-level (via gitutil.TopLevel(dir)) as a separate "workingRoot" for per-worktree artifacts (ignorefile, staged-diff), while keeping repo.Path/repo.ID as the identity used for snapshot/symbol lookups.

### F89. `internal/snapshot/registry.go:384` — ResolveRepo
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** GetReposByCommonDir's disambiguation invariant (issue #61 fix): 'disambiguate to the enrollment whose path is THIS worktree's top-level, so the edit is validated against its own snapshot rather than a sibling worktree's.'
- **Hypothesis:** Two worktrees A and B of the same bare repo are each independently enrolled, so GetReposByCommonDir returns len(repos) > 1. dir is currently inside worktree A, but A's enrolled repo.Path differs from what gitutil.TopLevel(dir) now returns by a symlink or bind-mount hop only (e.g. enrolled as /home/user/repo-a, TopLevel resolves to /mnt/data/repo-a for the same directory). filepath.Clean only collapses '.', '..', and redundant separators -- it never resolves symlinks -- so `filepath.Clean(r.Path) == filepath.Clean(top)` is false for the correct match A even though both paths name the same directory on disk. The loop at 383-387 finds no match, falls through to the 'no worktree-specific match' fallback at line 391-392, and returns repos[0] (the lowest-id row, e.g. worktree B's enrollment) with ok=true. ResolveRepo hands back repoB while the caller is actually editing files in worktree A, so the guard validates A's edits against B's stale snapshot/symbols -- the exact cross-worktree contamination the disambiguation logic was written to prevent, silently reintroduced whenever enrollment path and live git-toplevel path differ only by a symlink.
- **Trace:** Setup: bare-repo-style scenario with two enrolled worktrees of the same repo sharing one common_dir (issue #61 multi-match case).
- mainID=1 enrolled at real path `.../001` (mainDir).
- linkedID=2 enrolled at `.../003/linked-sym`, a symlink pointing to the REAL worktree dir `.../002/linked-real` (simulating enrollment captured via a symlink/bind-mount path, per the claim).
- Both rows share common_dir `.../001/.git`.

Call: db.ResolveRepo(linkedSym) where linkedSym = `.../003/linked-sym` (the path the user is actually working in — inside the "linked" worktree, addressed via its symlink).

Path through registry.go:
- L373: gitutil.CommonDir(linkedSym) succeeds -> matches both enrolled rows.
- L375: GetReposByCommonDir returns len(repos)==2 -> branch L381.
- L382: gitutil.TopLevel(linkedSym) succeeds, but git canonicalizes the symlink: returned top = `.../002/linked-real` (the REAL path), not `.../003/linked-sym` (verified directly: `TopLevel("...003/linked-sym") = ".../002/linked-real"`).
- L383-387 loop: repos[0].Path = `.../001` (mainDir, real, no symlink) != top. repos[1].Path = `.../003/linked-sym` (the enrolled symlink path) != top (`.../002/linked-real`) — filepath.Clean never resolves symlinks, so this legitimate match is missed.
- No match found -> falls through to L392: `return repos[0], repos[0].Path, true` -> returns repo id=1 (mainID), NOT id=2 (linkedID), even though the caller is physically working inside the linked worktree.

Predicted wrong output: ResolveRepo returns mainID's repo/snapshot while the caller is editing files in the linked worktree.
Expected right output: ResolveRepo should return linkedID's repo/snapshot (the enrollment that actually corresponds to this worktree).
Actual observed output matched the prediction exactly.
- **Blast radius:** All 7 call sites of `db.ResolveRepo` via `grep -rn "\.ResolveRepo(" --include=*.go` (excluding tests): cmd/runecho-guard/dangling.go:126, cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:139, cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:293, cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:674, cmd/runecho-ir/repo.go:202, cmd/runecho-ir/helpers.go:44, cmd/runecho-ir/helpers.go:88. This is the resolver used by both the guard (edit-validation drift/dangling-symbol checks) and the runecho-ir CLI to pick which enrolled repo's snapshot governs the current directory — a wrong pick means edits in one worktree get validated against a sibling worktree's stale snapshot/symbol table.
- **Fix direction:** In the tier-1 disambiguation loop (registry.go:383-387), compare by resolving both sides to the same canonical form before matching — e.g. also fall back to comparing `filepath.EvalSymlinks(r.Path)` against `top` (or evaluate symlinks on `r.Path` once at enroll/backfill time) instead of relying on `filepath.Clean` alone, since Clean never dereferences symlinks/bind-mounts.

### F90. `internal/snapshot/truthtrail.go:29` — TruthTrail
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** TrailResult.StaleClaims doc comment (lines 29-30) states 'non-nil only when a text was provided to TruthTrail' — implying a caller can use nil-vs-non-nil on StaleClaims as a proxy for 'was text checked' — but the append at line 84 only fires when an extracted symbol ref is unknown, so when text is non-empty but every referenced symbol resolves (or ExtractSymbolRefs finds nothing), StaleClaims is left nil despite text being provided.
- **Hypothesis:** Call TruthTrail(db, repoID, meta, liveIR, churnN, text) with text = "The migrate script calls TruthTrail directly." where 'TruthTrail' is itself a live, known symbol in liveIR (known["TruthTrail"] == true). Expected per the doc comment: result.StaleClaims is non-nil (since text != "", i.e. 'a text was provided'). Actual: since the only extracted symbol ref resolves to a known symbol, the `if !known[sym]` guard at line 83 never fires, the append at line 84 never executes, and result.StaleClaims stays nil — a caller trusting the doc's nil-vs-non-nil signal wrongly concludes 'no text was supplied for stale-claim analysis' when in fact analysis ran and found nothing stale.
- **Trace:** Input: text = "The migrate script calls `TruthTrail` directly." with liveIR containing symbol "TruthTrail" (known["TruthTrail"] == true).
Path: TruthTrail() line 79 `if text != ""` → true (enters stale-claims block) → line 80 `known := liveSymbolSet(liveIR)` → {"TruthTrail": true} → line 81 `refs := claims.ExtractSymbolRefs(text)` → backtickRe matches `TruthTrail`, IsCodeSymbol("TruthTrail") true (mixed case) → refs = {"TruthTrail": "The migrate script calls `TruthTrail` directly."} → line 82 loop over refs: sym="TruthTrail" → line 83 `if !known[sym]` → !true → false, skip append → line 84 never executes → result.StaleClaims remains at its zero value (nil, never assigned).
Predicted wrong output: trail.StaleClaims == nil even though text != "".
Expected per doc comment: trail.StaleClaims != nil (a caller checking nil-vs-non-nil to infer "was text checked" would wrongly conclude no text was supplied).
- **Blast radius:** grep -rn "StaleClaims" across the repo shows the field is consumed by internal/snapshot/truthtrail.go's own FormatTrail (len() check, not nil check — unaffected) and by the CLI/MCP callers that invoke TruthTrail with a text argument (cmd/runecho-ir truth-trail --text=<file> per the Truth-Trail feature memory). Any caller/consumer that branches on `trail.StaleClaims == nil` (vs. `len(trail.StaleClaims) == 0`) to decide "was stale-claim analysis performed" would misfire in this case; a `grep -rn "StaleClaims == nil\|StaleClaims != nil"` outside the test files should be run to enumerate any such callers before fixing.
- **Fix direction:** Either fix the doc comment to say "StaleClaims is non-nil only when at least one stale ref was found" (matching actual behavior), or fix the code to always initialize `result.StaleClaims = []StaleClaim{}` when `text != ""` so nil vs non-nil truly signals "was text provided."

### F91. `internal/snapshot/truthtrail.go:103` — liveSymbolSet
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** liveSymbolSet builds a single flat map[string]bool keyed only by bare symbol Name across every file in liveIR, so TruthTrail's stale-claim check (`known[sym]` at line 83) implicitly assumes symbol names are globally unique in the repo. Go/JS/Python codebases routinely have multiple types/files each defining methods with the same short name (Close, String, Parse, New, Validate), which this function conflates into one boolean per name.
- **Hypothesis:** The removed-symbol diff contains `Parse` (a top-level function removed from parser/legacy.go). The doc text passed to TruthTrail says '...uses legacy.Parse to...'. claims.ExtractSymbolRefs(text) extracts the ref `Parse`. Meanwhile some unrelated file (e.g. config/loader.go) still defines its own function or method named `Parse` that has nothing to do with the removed one. liveSymbolSet flattens both into set["Parse"]=true, so `known["Parse"]` is true, and the stale claim for the actually-removed `legacy.Parse` is silently skipped at line 83 — it never lands in result.StaleClaims — even though the specific symbol the text was talking about is gone. The receipt reports 'no stale claims' while the prose in fact references a deleted function.
- **Trace:** Input: liveIR with two files — config/loader.go defining Symbol{Name:"Parse"} (unrelated, still present) and parser/legacy.go defining only Symbol{Name:"Convert"} (i.e. its own Parse was removed). Prose text: "The loader now uses `Parse` to convert legacy config; see parser/legacy.go."
Path: claims.ExtractSymbolRefs(text) [claims.go:58, backtickRe match] -> refs = {"Parse": "...uses `Parse` to convert..."} (truthtrail.go:81) -> liveSymbolSet(liveIR) [truthtrail.go:96-107] iterates file.Symbols for both files and sets set["Parse"]=true (from config/loader.go) and set["Convert"]=true, losing which file each name came from -> back in TruthTrail's loop (truthtrail.go:82-86): sym="Parse", known["Parse"] is true -> `if !known[sym]` is false -> the StaleClaims append at truthtrail.go:84 is skipped.
Predicted wrong output: known["Parse"] == true, so no StaleClaim recorded despite the specific Parse referenced by the prose (parser/legacy.go's) being gone.
Expected/correct behavior: the receipt should flag the reference as stale (or at least ambiguous) because the Parse the text is actually pointing at (per its own "see parser/legacy.go" context) no longer exists.
- **Blast radius:** Single production call chain: cmd/runecho-ir/inspect.go:510 (runTruthTrail, the `runecho-ir truth-trail` CLI subcommand) -> internal/snapshot.TruthTrail (truthtrail.go:36) -> liveSymbolSet (truthtrail.go:96). No other callers of TruthTrail or liveSymbolSet exist outside tests (grep confirmed). Impact is scoped to the stale-claims section of the truth-trail receipt (the "no stale claims" guarantee it advertises), not the structural diff/churn/callers sections which use separate logic.
- **Fix direction:** Key liveSymbolSet by (file, qualified-or-not) pairs — e.g. build map[string][]string of name -> owning file paths (or a map[string]int count), and at truthtrail.go:83 only treat a ref as "known" if it can be tied to the same file/package context the diff removed it from (or, at minimum, treat a name that existed in the removed file's symbol list but is now only satisfied by a different file as still-stale/ambiguous rather than silently known).

### F92. `internal/snapshot/truthtrail.go:120` — FormatTrail
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** unhandled-postcondition
- **Contract violated:** FormatTrail's stated purpose is a 'human-readable change receipt' fusing diff + churn + stale-claims (churn is truth-trail's differentiator per package intent), but the early-return short-circuits on structural-diff-empty AND stale-claims-empty without checking whether churn data (r.FileHot / r.ChurnDiffs) has anything to report.
- **Hypothesis:** Call FormatTrail with r.Diff.Files == nil, r.StaleClaims == nil, but r.FileHot == {"internal/foo.go": 5} and r.ChurnDiffs == 20 (i.e. the repo has zero structural diff since the snapshot but internal/foo.go changed 5 of the last 20 tracked diffs, a genuinely hot file). Expected: the receipt still surfaces that internal/foo.go is hot even though nothing structurally changed. Actual: the len(Diff.Files)==0 && len(StaleClaims)==0 check at line 120 is true, so the function returns immediately after just 'No structural changes since <label>.' — the HOT churn signal for internal/foo.go is silently discarded and never appears anywhere in the output.
- **Trace:** Input: r.Diff.Files=nil (len 0), r.StaleClaims=nil (len 0), r.FileHot={"internal/foo.go":5}, r.ChurnDiffs=20, r.SnapshotRef.Label="snap1".
Path: FormatTrail line 110 entry -> line 118 writes header -> line 120 evaluates `len(r.Diff.Files)==0 && len(r.StaleClaims)==0` = true (0==0 && 0==0) -> line 121 writes "No structural changes since snap1." -> line 122 `return sb.String()` immediately, before ever reaching the r.Diff.Files>0 block (line 125, where hotLabel(r.FileHot[...], r.ChurnDiffs) is the only place FileHot is consulted).
Predicted wrong output: receipt = "TRUTH-TRAIL  snap1 → live  2026-07-01\n\nNo structural changes since snap1.\n" with no mention of foo.go or HOT/churn data.
Actual output (captured via go test -v): exactly that — "TRUTH-TRAIL  snap1 → live  2026-07-01\n\nNo structural changes since snap1.\n", no "foo.go" substring present.
Expected/correct behavior: since FileHot is non-empty and ChurnDiffs>0, the receipt should still surface "internal/foo.go [HOT 5/20]" (or equivalent) even with zero structural diff, per package intent (churn is truth-trail's differentiator).
- **Blast radius:** Single caller: cmd/runecho-ir/inspect.go:516 (`fmt.Print(snapshot.FormatTrail(trail))`), the `runecho-ir truth-trail` CLI subcommand's entire output path — no other callers found via grep.
- **Fix direction:** Change the guard at line 120 to also require churn has nothing to report, e.g. `if len(r.Diff.Files) == 0 && len(r.StaleClaims) == 0 && len(r.FileHot) == 0`, and add an unconditional "hot files" section (independent of the Diff.Files>0 block) that lists r.FileHot entries with hotLabel even when there's no structural diff.

### F93. `internal/snapshot/truthtrail.go:175` — hotLabel
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** medium (default: real caller(s), bounded/CLI-subcommand-scale blast radius)
- **Class:** impossible-state
- **Contract violated:** hotLabel's changes==0 branch (falling through to '[stable]') implicitly assumes 'this file existed throughout the churn window and simply had 0 recorded changes' — but changes==0 also covers 'this file did not exist in ANY snapshot analyzed by db.Churn, because it is brand new'. Those are opposite facts (long-quiet vs. never-existed-until-now) collapsed into the same label.
- **Hypothesis:** Baseline snapshot + churn history (S1..S5, ChurnDiffs=4) contain only files A and B. The live IR adds a brand-new file C with two new functions. diff.Files will contain an entry for C with Status=="added" and Added=[F1,F2]. Because C never appeared in any of the historical diffs db.Churn walked, r.FileHot["C"] is a map miss returning the zero value 0, and r.ChurnDiffs is 4 (nonzero). FormatTrail's call hotLabel(0, 4) returns "  [stable]", so the emitted receipt reads `  C  [stable]\n    + F1\n    + F2\n` — a file that was just created in this exact change is labeled stable, which reads as 'existing file, nothing going on here' rather than 'new file'. hotLabel and its caller never look at fd.Status, so a freshly-added file and a five-year-old untouched file render identically.
- **Trace:** Input: TrailResult{ Diff.Files: [{Path:"C.go", Status:"added", Added:[F1,F2]}], FileHot:{"A.go":3,"B.go":2} (C.go absent), ChurnDiffs:4 }.
Path: FormatTrail (truthtrail.go:132) loops fd = C.go -> line 133 `hotTag := hotLabel(r.FileHot["C.go"], 4)` -> map lookup r.FileHot["C.go"] misses, Go zero-value gives changes=0 -> hotLabel(0,4) (truthtrail.go:171): totalDiffs=4 != 0 so skip line172-174; changes=0 is not >=2 so skip line175-177; falls through to line 178 `return "  [stable]"`.
Predicted wrong output: receipt line `  C.go  [stable]\n    + F1\n    + F2\n` for a file created in this very change.
Expected/distinguishable output: some indicator that C.go is new (e.g. via fd.Status=="added"), not "[stable]".
- **Blast radius:** hotLabel has exactly one call site: FormatTrail (internal/snapshot/truthtrail.go:133). FormatTrail has exactly one call site in non-test code: cmd/runecho-ir/inspect.go:516, the `runecho-ir truth-trail` CLI subcommand's stdout output (confirmed via grep -rn across the repo, excluding tests). So the defect surfaces only in the truth-trail receipt text a user reads on the CLI — no other consumer.
- **Fix direction:** Pass fd.Status into hotLabel (or check it in FormatTrail before calling hotLabel) so Status=="added" emits a distinct tag like "[NEW]" instead of falling through to "[stable]" on the changes==0 path.

## 🟢 LOW

### F94. `bench/captured.go:277` — pathFor(lang guard.Lang) string
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/REFUTED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** low (matched low-marker: "\blatent\b")
- **Class:** impossible-state
- **Contract violated:** toCase()'s comment 'validated already' (line 116) — pathFor's own switch is written as if guard.Lang could still be anything, but the only call site guarantees lang ∈ {LangGo, LangJS, LangPython}.
- **Hypothesis:** toCase() (line 115-131) only ever invokes pathFor(lang) where lang came from langOf(cc.Lang) at line 116, and cc has already passed validate() (line 86-88 rejects any cc.Lang for which langOf errors) before toCase can run anywhere in this package (LoadCaptured -> validate -> only then is the case usable, and ScoreCaptured's only source of cases is a validated slice). So the branch `return "captured.txt"` at line 286 can never execute through the sole call site at line 124 — it is dead code. Worse, it silently mirrors langOf's LangUnknown case without erroring: if guard.Lang ever gains a fourth value (e.g. a new language), pathFor degrades to returning the generic 'captured.txt' path instead of surfacing an error the way langOf and stratumOf both do for their own unknown-input cases, so a caller who reaches pathFor with an unvalidated lang (a future refactor that drops the validate()-first invariant) gets a silently wrong synthetic path rather than a load error.
- **Trace:** Static call-graph (grep + codegraph_explore, both agree): pathFor has exactly 1 caller — toCase() line 124; toCase has exactly 1 caller — ScoreCaptured() line 155; ScoreCaptured's only two invocations in the codebase (bench/captured_test.go:24 and :51) both pass cases returned from LoadCaptured(), which loops every case through cc.validate() (line 62) and returns an error (aborting the whole load) if any case fails validate. validate() calls langOf(cc.Lang) at line 86 and propagates its error — so any cc.Lang that doesn't map to "go"/"js"/"ts"/"jsx"/"tsx"/"py" causes LoadCaptured to return an error before any CapturedCase reaches toCase. Therefore lang in toCase (line 116, `lang, _ := langOf(cc.Lang)`) is always one of {LangGo, LangJS, LangPython}, and pathFor's switch (line 278) always matches one of its first three cases — the `return "captured.txt"` at line 286 is dead through this path.

Concrete input / predicted vs actual:
- Input: real corpus at bench/captured/corpus.json (15 cases) run through the full LoadCaptured -> toCase chain. Predicted: no Case.Path ever equals "captured.txt". Actual: confirmed — 0/15 cases produced the default path.
- Input: direct unexported call pathFor(guard.LangUnknown) — i.e. guard.Lang(""), the zero value langOf itself returns on error and that validate()/toCase never let through. Predicted: silently returns "captured.txt", no error. Actual: returned "captured.txt" exactly as predicted.
- Input: pathFor(guard.Lang("rust")) (guard.Lang is a bare string type, so any string is constructible) — same silent "captured.txt" result, confirming the fallback isn't limited to LangUnknown specifically.
- **Blast radius:** pathFor: 1 caller (toCase, bench/captured.go:124). toCase: 1 caller (ScoreCaptured, bench/captured.go:155). ScoreCaptured: 2 call sites, both in bench/captured_test.go, both fed exclusively by LoadCaptured()-validated slices. No external package imports bench's unexported pathFor/toCase. Confined entirely to bench/captured.go plus its own test file — zero cross-package blast radius today; risk is purely latent (a future refactor that calls ScoreCaptured/toCase with unvalidated CapturedCase data).
- **Fix direction:** Make pathFor return (string, error) and propagate the error like langOf/stratumOf, or have toCase reuse the already-known-valid lang exhaustively via a compile-time-checked type switch with a panic (not silent default) on the impossible branch, so a future invariant break surfaces immediately instead of degrading to "captured.txt".

### F95. `cmd/runecho-guard/learnedallow.go:145` — recordApprovals
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** low (matched low-marker: "never fires?")
- **Class:** impossible-state
- **Contract violated:** loadLearnedAllow's own documented postcondition: "Always returns a usable, non-error learnedAllow value... never a nil Repos map" (line 86 seeds the default; the check at line 92 forces that same default whenever parsed.Repos is nil).
- **Hypothesis:** recordApprovals(dir, "r", []string{"Foo"}, now) calls `la := loadLearnedAllow(dir)` at line 144, then checks `if la.Repos == nil { la.Repos = map[string]map[string]learnedEntry{} }` at lines 145-147. Trace every path through loadLearnedAllow: (a) os.ReadFile fails -> returns the line-86 default with Repos already initialized; (b) json.Unmarshal fails -> returns the same line-86 default; (c) unmarshal succeeds but parsed.Repos is nil -> also falls into the line-92 branch and returns the line-86 default; (d) unmarshal succeeds and parsed.Repos is non-nil -> returned as-is, already non-nil. There is no return path in loadLearnedAllow that yields a nil Repos map, and recordApprovals is the only other caller besides learnedAllowedSet (which has no equivalent guard at line 197-198, correctly relying on the same guarantee). So the condition `la.Repos == nil` at line 145 is always false for every possible dir/disk-content/error combination -- the branch is unreachable dead code, never exercised by any test (including TestLearnedAllow_FailOpenOnCorruptStore, which only reaches the fail-open default path where Repos is already non-nil going in).
- **Trace:** Read cmd/runecho-guard/learnedallow.go directly (function names/line numbers match the claim almost exactly: recordApprovals body at 134-166, the guard at 145-147, loadLearnedAllow at 85-97).

loadLearnedAllow's four possible paths, all confirmed by exhaustive trace of the source:
- line 86: `la := learnedAllow{V: 1, Repos: map[string]map[string]learnedEntry{}}` — always seeds a non-nil Repos into the local default.
- line 87-90: os.ReadFile fails -> `return la` (the line-86 default, Repos non-nil).
- line 91-94: `json.Unmarshal(b, &parsed) != nil || parsed.Repos == nil` -> `return la` (same line-86 default, Repos non-nil) -- this branch explicitly catches the nil-Repos-after-successful-unmarshal case too.
- line 95-96: unmarshal succeeded and parsed.Repos != nil -> `parsed.V = 1; return parsed` (Repos non-nil, since the OR-condition on line 92 already excluded nil).

So every return path yields Repos != nil. recordApprovals calls exactly this function at line 144 and nothing else populates `la` beforehand, so the input to the `la.Repos == nil` check at line 145 can never be true.

Executed a throwaway test (cmd/runecho-guard/zzfocus_repro_test.go, now deleted) that calls the REAL loadLearnedAllow with 4 concrete dir/disk-state combinations covering every branch above: missing file, corrupt JSON, valid JSON with `"repos":null`, and valid JSON with a populated repos map. Asserted `la.Repos != nil` in every case.
- **Blast radius:** Not a runtime-behavior bug (the branch being unreachable doesn't corrupt any output — it's defensive code that never fires, not a wrong-computation path), so no caller is affected by incorrect behavior. `recordApprovals` has one call site in the guard's PostToolUse path; `grep -rn "recordApprovals("` shows it's invoked from the guard's main flow only. This is a code-quality/dead-code finding, not a correctness defect with observable impact.
- **Fix direction:** Delete the unreachable `if la.Repos == nil { ... }` guard at recordApprovals (lines 145-147) since loadLearnedAllow already guarantees a non-nil Repos map on every path — or, if defensive redundancy against a future loadLearnedAllow regression is desired, add a one-line comment noting it's a deliberate belt-and-suspenders check rather than reachable logic.

### F96. `cmd/runecho-ir/capture.go:137` — runIndex
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** low (matched low-marker: "zero functional callers")
- **Class:** impossible-state
- **Contract violated:** runIndex's own args[1]-must-not-start-with-'-' check assumes it can still be true when this function runs, but its sole production caller has already eliminated that state before calling in.
- **Hypothesis:** runIndex has exactly one call site: main.go:99 `return runIndex(os.Args)`, reached only through the fallthrough after main.go's run() switch (main.go:57-99). That switch already returns ExitError directly, at main.go:91-95, for any os.Args[1] that starts with '-' -- BEFORE runIndex is ever invoked -- using the identical predicate `strings.HasPrefix(os.Args[1], "-")`. Since runIndex is called with args=os.Args (not a trimmed slice), args[1] inside runIndex is byte-for-byte the same os.Args[1] already proven not to start with '-' whenever len(args)>1. Concrete input os.Args=["runecho-ir","-badflag"]: main.go's default case matches first and returns ExitError=2 with 'unknown flag "-badflag"' printed -- runIndex is never called, so the branch at capture.go:137-141 (the duplicate 'unknown flag %q' check, printUsage(), return ExitError) is dead code in every real invocation. It can only be exercised by a test calling runIndex([]string{...,"-x"}) directly, and no such test exists in the package (grep confirms runIndex has zero direct test call sites), so this validation path has never actually been run against a real flag-like second argument.
- **Trace:** Concrete input: os.Args = ["runecho-ir", "-badflag"].
main.go:57 run() -> len(os.Args)>1 true -> main.go:59 switch os.Args[1] ("-badflag") -> no named case matches -> main.go:90 default: -> main.go:91 strings.HasPrefix("-badflag","-") == true -> main.go:92-94 prints "runecho-ir: unknown flag \"-badflag\"" + usage -> main.go:95 return ExitError (2). Execution never reaches main.go:99 `return runIndex(os.Args)`, so capture.go:134 runIndex is never entered, and its internal duplicate check at capture.go:137 `strings.HasPrefix(args[1], "-")` never runs in this call path.
Predicted wrong/dead state: capture.go:137-141 has 0% execution coverage under the real entrypoint for any flag-like second argument.
Expected if the hypothesis were false: runIndex would show >0% coverage (i.e., some caller reaches it with a "-"-prefixed arg).
- **Blast radius:** Zero functional callers affected — runIndex has exactly one call site (main.go:99), and it is reached only after main.go's own switch has already filtered out every os.Args[1] starting with '-'. The dead branch (capture.go:137-141) can only ever be exercised by a test calling runIndex(...) directly with a synthetic args slice (as confirmed: no such test exists in the repo). No user-facing behavior depends on it; removing it changes nothing observable.
- **Fix direction:** Delete the redundant guard at capture.go:137-141 (or, if defense-in-depth for future direct callers is wanted, keep it but add a comment noting it's currently unreachable via main() and add a direct unit test for runIndex(["prog","-x"]) so the branch has actual coverage instead of being silently dead.

### F97. `cmd/runecho-ir/main.go:137` — runIndex
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** low (matched low-marker: "dead branch")
- **Class:** impossible-state
- **Contract violated:** run()'s postcondition guarantees that by the time control reaches line 99 (`return runIndex(os.Args)`), os.Args[1] (if it exists) does NOT start with "-" — that case was already intercepted at main.go:91-95 (`if strings.HasPrefix(os.Args[1], "-") { ...; return ExitError }`) inside the switch's default branch, which returns before falling through. runIndex is called from exactly one place in the whole binary (main.go:99, `runIndex(os.Args)` — grep confirms no other call site, including tests), and it receives the *unshifted* os.Args (args[1] == os.Args[1], not os.Args[2:]). So capture.go:137's `if strings.HasPrefix(args[1], "-")` is re-checking a condition run() has already proven false on every path that reaches this function.
- **Hypothesis:** Invoking `runecho-ir -x` never reaches capture.go:137-141 at all — run()'s own dash-check at main.go:91 fires first and returns ExitError with 'runecho-ir: unknown flag "-x"' before runIndex is ever called. capture.go:137-141 (the unknown-flag branch inside runIndex) is therefore permanently dead code: no input to the real `runecho-ir` binary can ever make args[1] start with '-' when runIndex executes, since the only caller (main.go:99) is only reached via (a) len(os.Args)<=1, where args[1] doesn't exist, or (b) an os.Args[1] that already passed run()'s own HasPrefix("-") check as false. A maintainer who edits run()'s dispatcher (e.g. removes or narrows the main.go:91 dash-check, or adds a new subcommand alias) can silently change what reaches this 'dead' branch without realizing capture.go:137 was never live — or conversely, believe fixing/extending capture.go:137-141 changes behavior for dash-prefixed input, when it never executes.
- **Trace:** Input: os.Args = ["runecho-ir", "-x"] fed to run() via the existing test helper runWith() (cmd/runecho-ir/entrypoint_test.go:95, calls run() in-process).
Path: main.go:58 len(os.Args)>1 true -> main.go:59 switch os.Args[1]="-x" -> no case matches -> main.go:90 default -> main.go:91 HasPrefix("-x","-")=true -> main.go:92-94 print "runecho-ir: unknown flag \"-x\"" + usage -> main.go:94 return ExitError(2). Execution never reaches main.go:99 (`return runIndex(os.Args)`), so capture.go:134 (runIndex body) and capture.go:137 (its own HasPrefix check) are never entered.
Predicted (per hypothesis): capture.go:137's branch has zero coverage for this input; runIndex itself is never invoked.
Observed: matches prediction exactly (see evidence).
- **Blast radius:** runIndex has exactly one caller in the entire binary (main.go:99, confirmed via `grep -rn "runIndex("` across the whole repo — no other production or test call site). So today the dead branch affects zero behavior. The risk is purely maintenance-time: if a future change to run()'s dispatcher (removing/narrowing the main.go:91 HasPrefix check, adding a subcommand alias, or a new direct call to runIndex with unshifted/different args) is made, a developer could reasonably believe editing capture.go:137-141 changes behavior for dash-prefixed input today — it does not, and won't until/unless run()'s guarantee is altered or a second call site is added.
- **Fix direction:** Delete the dead `if strings.HasPrefix(args[1], "-") { ... }` block in capture.go:137-141 (runIndex should just treat args[1] as rootPath unconditionally, per its documented contract as an internal helper only reachable via run()'s already-validated dispatch), or, if kept intentionally as defense-in-depth for a hypothetical future second caller, add a comment stating explicitly that it is currently unreachable via run() and why, so it isn't mistaken for live behavior.

### F98. `cmd/runecho-ir/repo.go:73` — runRepoAdd
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** low (matched low-marker: "\blatent\b")
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** doReindex's precondition that EffectiveSourceRoot() point at a stable, walkable directory implicitly assumes SourceRoot is CWD-independent (i.e. absolute), but nothing on the write path enforces that.
- **Hypothesis:** Run `runecho-ir repo add . --source-root=../shared-src` from /home/eric/projA (root becomes absolute /home/eric/projA via resolveRoot, but *sourceRoot is passed to db.EnrollRepo verbatim as the literal relative string "../shared-src" — no filepath.Abs is ever applied to it). The DB row stores source_root="../shared-src". Later, run `runecho-ir repo reindex projA-name` (or `repo reindex --all` from a cron job) with CWD=/home/eric instead of /home/eric/projA. doReindex computes srcRoot = repo.EffectiveSourceRoot() = "../shared-src" (still relative) and passes it into buildIR, which does `filepath.Abs(root)` against the CURRENT process CWD. From /home/eric/projA that resolves to /home/eric/shared-src (correct); from /home/eric it resolves to /home/shared-src (wrong directory — either indexes an unrelated tree that happens to exist there, or fails with a misleading 'no such directory' error that never points at the real cause: a relative source-root captured at add-time being re-interpreted against a different CWD at reindex-time).
- **Trace:** Concrete input: `EnrollRepo("projA", "/tmp/.../workspace/projA", "../shared-src", 0)` called with CWD=/tmp/.../workspace/projA (mirrors `runecho-ir repo add . --source-root=../shared-src` from that dir).
Path: repo.go:73 EnrollRepo(n, root, *sourceRoot, *cap) -> registry.go:46 EnrollRepo stores sourceRoot string verbatim ("../shared-src", sourceRoot=="" check doesn't fire since it's non-empty) -> DB row source_root="../shared-src" -> registry.go:35 EffectiveSourceRoot() returns "../shared-src" unchanged -> repo.go:251 doReindex: srcRoot := repo.EffectiveSourceRoot() -> repo.go:252 buildIR(srcRoot,...) -> capture.go:108 filepath.Abs(root) resolves against os.Getwd().
Run #1 (CWD=/tmp/.../workspace/projA, i.e. same CWD as enroll-time): filepath.Abs("../shared-src") = /tmp/.../workspace/shared-src (correct; contains marker.go/CorrectFunc) -> indexed files=[marker.go]. Matches expectation.
Run #2 (CWD=/tmp/.../workspace, simulating `repo reindex` invoked from one directory level up, e.g. a cron job): EffectiveSourceRoot() is STILL the literal string "../shared-src" (nothing in the write path ever made it absolute) -> filepath.Abs("../shared-src") now resolves to /tmp/.../shared-src (one level further up — a completely different, unrelated directory that happened to exist, containing decoy.go/DecoyFunc) -> Generate() silently walks and indexes that wrong tree -> files=[decoy.go].
Predicted wrong output: reindex #2 uses source root /tmp/.../shared-src (decoy) instead of the enroll-time-intended /tmp/.../workspace/shared-src (correct). Actual measured output matched the prediction exactly.
- **Blast radius:** Direct callers of the affected path: runRepoAdd (repo.go:73, the enroll site) and doReindex (repo.go:250-251), which is called by every reindex entry point — `repo reindex <name>`, `repo reindex --all`, and any cron/automation wrapping those (per CLAUDE.md's own `runecho-ir repo reindex <name>` guidance). Any repo enrolled with a relative `--source-root` (the documented use case for "bare-repo worktree layouts") is exposed; impact is latent until reindex is ever invoked from a CWD other than the one active at `repo add` time.
- **Fix direction:** In runRepoAdd, resolve `*sourceRoot` to an absolute path (e.g. `filepath.Abs(*sourceRoot)` when non-empty, resolved relative to the CWD at add-time, mirroring how `root` is already resolved via resolveRoot) before passing it to db.EnrollRepo, so EffectiveSourceRoot() is always CWD-independent thereafter.

### F99. `cmd/runecho-ir/repo.go:312` — resolveRoot
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** low (matched low-marker: "dead branch")
- **Class:** impossible-state
- **Contract violated:** runRepoReindex's own guard `arg == "." || filepath.IsAbs(arg)` already establishes that fs.Args()[0] cannot begin with "-" (an absolute Unix path always starts with "/", and "." starts with "."), so resolveRoot's `strings.HasPrefix(args[0], "-")` flag-misparse check is dead code for this specific call site.
- **Hypothesis:** In runRepoReindex's line 197-201 branch, resolveRoot(fs.Args()) is invoked only after confirming arg=="." or filepath.IsAbs(arg) is true; inside resolveRoot, args[0] equals that same arg, so the condition `strings.HasPrefix(args[0], "-")` at line 312 can never evaluate true for any value that reached this call — the error path at lines 313-314 ('unexpected flag %q where root path was expected') is unreachable from this caller no matter what the user types, silently masking that this guard only does useful work for resolveRoot's other (non-reindex) call sites.
- **Trace:** Input: `runecho-ir repo reindex -- -foo` (RUNECHO_HOME pointed at an isolated temp dir).
Path: main→runRepoReindex(args) [repo.go:171] → parseSub/fs.Parse stops consuming flags at "--", so fs.Args()==["-foo"] → line 193 `arg := fs.Args()[0]` == "-foo" → line 197 `if arg=="." || filepath.IsAbs(arg)` evaluates false ("-foo" doesn't start with "/") → control falls to the ELSE branch (line 208) `repo, err = db.GetRepoByName(arg)` → repo==nil → line 214 prints `No repo named "-foo"` and returns ExitError(2). resolveRoot (and its dash-prefix guard at inspect.go:312-315) is never called on this path, for any input, because the only strings that satisfy line 197's guard (arg=="." or an absolute path starting with "/") can never also start with "-".
Contrast trace confirming the guard is NOT globally dead — only dead at this one call site: same input shape fed to runChurn (cmd/runecho-ir/inspect.go:327), which calls `resolveRoot(fs.Args())` unconditionally with no arg=="."||IsAbs pre-filter: fs.Args()==["-foo"] → resolveRoot line 312 `strings.HasPrefix("-foo","-")` is true → prints `runecho-ir: unexpected flag "-foo" where root path was expected` and returns ExitError(2). So the identical guard is live and doing real work for churn (and the 7 other non-reindex callers: install.go:30, mapcmd.go:79, repo.go:48, inspect.go:28/89/197/254/458), just not for runRepoReindex's line-198 call site.
- **Blast radius:** Only 1 of resolveRoot's 9 call sites is affected: runRepoReindex (repo.go:198). The other 8 callers (install.go:30, mapcmd.go:79, repo.go:48, inspect.go:28, inspect.go:89, inspect.go:197, inspect.go:254, inspect.go:458 — covering commands like map, snapshot, diff, verify, churn, install) still exercise the guard normally and are unaffected. No user-visible incorrect behavior results from the dead branch at the reindex call site — it just means a stray flag-shaped positional arg to `repo reindex` resolves to "No repo named" instead of "unexpected flag", which is arguably still a reasonable message.
- **Fix direction:** Either drop the redundant `if arg == "." || filepath.IsAbs(arg)` pre-check in runRepoReindex and let resolveRoot's own guard handle both flag-misparse and root-resolution uniformly, or add a one-line comment on resolveRoot noting its dash-guard is provably unreachable when called after that specific pre-check, so future maintainers don't assume it protects the reindex path.

### F100. `internal/guard/dropped_import.go:112` — firstUnqualifiedUseLines
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** low (matched low-marker: "zero functional callers")
- **Class:** impossible-state
- **Contract violated:** The invariant note ('open is force-reset... whenever the LineNo sequence is discontinuous') documents this as live behavior for a genuine hunk-boundary input, but the function's only call site never supplies such an input.
- **Hypothesis:** firstUnqualifiedUseLines is only ever invoked as `firstUnqualifiedUseLines(lang, TextToAddedLines(newText))` (dropped_import.go:76). TextToAddedLines splits the full text on '\n' and assigns LineNo = index+1 for every line with no gaps, so for every i>0, prevNo == i and l.LineNo == i+1, making `l.LineNo != prevNo+1` (line 112) always false. The `open = ""` reset on line 113 is dead code in the only production path that reaches this function — the discontinuous-hunk handling the comment describes cannot occur here (it would only fire if this function were ever fed a raw git-diff AddedLine slice with gaps, which it currently never is).
- **Trace:** Real call path: DroppedImportRefs (line 76) -> firstUnqualifiedUseLines(lang, TextToAddedLines(newText)). For any newText, TextToAddedLines produces lines[i].LineNo == i+1 for all i (by construction: strings.Split + i+1 assignment), so for i>0, l.LineNo == i+1 and prevNo == i, giving l.LineNo == prevNo+1 always -> condition at line 112 is always false -> `open=""` never executes on this path.

Isolation test (bypassing TextToAddedLines) to prove the branch is otherwise live:
Input A (discontinuous, LineNo 1 then 3 — simulating a raw diff-hunk gap): lines = [{1,`a = """`},{3,`RealName()`}]. Line 1 opens a Python triple-quoted string unterminated on that line. Because LineNo jumps from 1 to 3, the i=1 iteration hits `l.LineNo(3) != prevNo(1)+1(2)` -> true -> `open` force-reset to "" -> line 2's content is treated as NOT inside the still-open string -> stripLiteralsStateful does not blank it -> `RealName` is scanned and recorded as an unqualified use.
Input B (contiguous, LineNo 1 then 2 — the only shape TextToAddedLines can ever produce): lines = [{1,`a = """`},{2,`RealName()`}]. Discontinuity condition is false, `open` carries forward as the still-open triple-quote, so stripLiteralsStateful blanks line 2's content and `RealName` is never recorded.

Predicted vs actual: predicted uses[RealName] present (LineNo 3) for the synthetic discontinuous input, and absent for the contiguous (real-call-path-shaped) input.
- **Blast radius:** Zero functional callers affected — firstUnqualifiedUseLines has exactly one call site (DroppedImportRefs at dropped_import.go:76), and that call site is itself only reachable through the guard's dropped-import check for Python/JS edits. The dead branch causes no incorrect behavior today (it simply never fires); the risk is latent — if a future caller ever feeds this function a raw git-diff hunk (discontinuous LineNo) expecting the documented reset semantics, or if TextToAddedLines' contiguity guarantee is ever weakened, the invariant comment would silently start mattering, but as of now no caller does this (grep-confirmed single call site).
- **Fix direction:** Either delete the now-dead discontinuity-reset branch and its invariant comment (simplify to match the actual guarantee: input is always contiguous), or if the code is meant to be defensive against future non-TextToAddedLines callers, add a comment stating explicitly that this is defensive/currently-unreachable rather than documenting it as "live" behavior for a case that cannot occur via the only caller.

### F101. `internal/guard/extract.go:686` — stripLiteralsStateful
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** low (matched low-marker: "\blatent\b")
- **Class:** impossible-state
- **Contract violated:** precondition/design invariant: "only Go/JS/Python trigger any stripping; LangUnknown falls through every gated branch and returns text essentially unmodified" and the paired invariant that all four literal-kind branches are "gated mutually-exclusively by lang"
- **Hypothesis:** Every other literal-kind branch (block comment 596, Python triple-quote 618, JS/Go backtick 672) is explicitly gated by a `lang ==` check, but the single/double-quote branch at line 686 (`if c == '"' || c == '\''`) has no lang guard at all. If stripLiteralsStateful (or its stripLiterals wrapper, both unexported-but-package-callable) is ever invoked with lang==LangUnknown on text containing a `"` or `'` — e.g. a `.txt`/no-extension file misrouted through a helper that doesn't pre-filter LangUnknown the way ExtractRefs (423-425), DroppedImportRefs (33-35), and the validate.go loop (74-76) all currently do — the quote content gets blanked exactly as if it were Go/JS/Python, contradicting the documented guarantee that LangUnknown input is returned essentially unmodified. The three production call sites happen to filter LangUnknown before ever reaching this function, so the contract's claim is only true by caller discipline, not by anything internal to stripLiteralsStateful itself — a fourth call site added without that filter (or a direct package-internal call, e.g. from a new helper or test) would silently violate the documented invariant.
- **Trace:** Input: text = `x := "hello world"`, lang = LangUnknown, open = "".
Path: stripLiterals(LangUnknown, text) [extract.go:541-544] -> stripLiteralsStateful(LangUnknown, text, "") [extract.go:557].
- open == "" so the multi-line-continuation block (566-579) is skipped.
- Main loop (581-...): at i pointing to the opening `"`, isInlineCommentAt is false, the /* */ branch (596) requires lang==Go/JS (false, skipped), the Python triple-quote branch (618) requires lang==Python (false, skipped), the backtick branch (672) requires lang==JS/Go (false, skipped).
- Branch at line 686, `if c == '"' || c == '\''`, has NO lang check at all and is entered unconditionally.
- Since lang != LangPython, the f-string sub-branch (694) is skipped, falling into the plain single-line-string blanking path, which overwrites every byte between the quotes with a space.
Predicted wrong output: `x := "           "` (interior of the string blanked despite LangUnknown).
Expected/documented output per the invariant: `x := "hello world"` (text returned essentially unmodified for LangUnknown).
- **Blast radius:** stripLiterals/stripLiteralsStateful are unexported, so only internal/guard package code can call them. `grep -rn "stripLiterals(\|stripLiteralsStateful(" internal/ --include=*.go | grep -v _test.go` shows exactly 3 production invocation sites: extract.go:449 (inside ExtractRefs, gated by the LangUnknown-return at extract.go:423-425), dropped_import.go:116 and dropped_import.go:175 (both inside functions gated by `lang != LangPython && lang != LangJS` return at dropped_import.go:33-35). Current runtime blast radius is 0 — no live caller passes LangUnknown through. Risk is latent: any future call site inside internal/guard (a new helper, a refactor, or a test invoking it directly) that omits the LangUnknown pre-filter would silently corrupt string-literal content in `.txt`/extension-less files.
- **Fix direction:** Add an explicit lang guard to the line-686 condition, e.g. `if (lang == LangGo || lang == LangJS || lang == LangPython) && (c == '"' || c == '\'') {`, so the branch is gated the same way as its three siblings and the function is self-defending regardless of caller discipline.

### F102. `internal/guard/suggest.go:31` — Suggest
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** low (matched low-marker: "\blatent\b")
- **Class:** impossible-state
- **Contract violated:** Same sentinel-collision as above, reachable via the deterministic tie-break rule rather than only via the shortest-distance branch.
- **Hypothesis:** known = map[string]struct{}{"": {}, "zz": {}} and name = "xy" (len 2), where both candidates are within suggestMaxDist. "" has dist=2 (lb==0 fast path returns la=2) and "zz" also has dist=2 (two substitutions). If "zz" is enumerated by map-range iteration before "", the tie-break at line 31 (`dist == bestDist && cand < best`) compares "" < "zz", which is true, so best is overwritten from "zz" back to "". The final `best == ""` check at line 35 then reports no suggestion even though a deterministic tie-break legitimately selected "" as the closest known symbol.
- **Trace:** Input: Suggest("xy", map[string]struct{}{"": {}, "zz": {}})
Line 16-17: best="", bestDist=3 (suggestMaxDist+1)
Iteration order A (""  first):
