  cand="": line 20 d=|0-2|=2, not >2 -> line 27 dist=levenshtein("xy","",2) -> line 46 la=2,lb=0 -> line 49 lb==0 return la=2. dist=2.
  line 31: dist(2) < bestDist(3) -> true -> best="", bestDist=2
  cand="zz": line 20 d=|2-2|=0 -> line 27 dist=levenshtein("xy","zz",2)=2 (two substitutions)
  line 31: dist<bestDist (2<2) false; dist==bestDist && cand<best -> "zz" < "" -> false. best stays ""
Iteration order B ("zz" first) converges to the same best="" (verified by hand: "" < "zz" wins the tie-break when "zz" is provisionally best).
Line 35: best=="" -> return "", false   [ACTUAL, WRONG per contract]
Expected per the doc comment ("ties resolve to the lexicographically smallest candidate"): return "", true — "" is a legitimate, deterministically-selected known symbol, not "no match".
- **Blast radius:** grep -rn for `Suggest(` outside suggest.go itself found exactly one call site: internal/guard/validate.go:89 — `suggestion, _ := Suggest(ref.Name, known)`. That caller already discards the `ok` bool and unconditionally stores the returned string into Violation.Suggestion, so today the bug's *practical* effect is masked for this caller (it would set Suggestion="" whether Suggest returns ("",true) or ("",false) — both look identical downstream). However, this is a latent defect in Suggest's own contract (the `bool` return is supposed to disambiguate "found" from "not found") and would bite any future/other caller that actually checks `ok`, plus it only occurs when an empty string is itself a legitimate entry in the `known` map — worth confirming whether `known` (symbol table) can ever contain "" as a key in practice.
- **Fix direction:** Replace the `best == ""` sentinel check with an explicit `found bool` flag set alongside `best`/`bestDist` inside the loop, and return `found` instead of inferring "not found" from `best == ""`.

### F103. `internal/guard/suggest.go:35` — Suggest
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** low (matched low-marker: "\blatent\b")
- **Class:** impossible-state
- **Contract violated:** Postcondition states: returns (bestName, true) iff some candidate is within suggestMaxDist, and returns ("", false) iff known is empty or no candidate qualifies. The implementation instead treats `best == ""` as its sole signal for 'no candidate found', silently conflating that with 'the winning candidate is the empty string'.
- **Hypothesis:** Suggest("ab", map[string]struct{}{"": {}}) returns ("", false); the correct/intended result per the documented postcondition is ("", true) because the empty-string candidate is at Levenshtein distance 2 from "ab", which is <= suggestMaxDist (2). Verified by direct execution: `go test` output shows `Suggest("ab", map[:{}]) = ("", false)`.
- **Trace:** Input: Suggest("ab", map[string]struct{}{"": {}})
Line 16-17: best="", bestDist=3 (suggestMaxDist+1)
Line 18: loop, cand=""
Line 20-23: d = |len("")-len("ab")| = 2, not > suggestMaxDist(2), continues
Line 27: dist = levenshtein("ab", "", 2) -> in levenshtein, lb=0 so returns la=2
Line 28: dist(2) not > suggestMaxDist(2), continues
Line 31: dist(2) < bestDist(3) -> true -> best="", bestDist=2
Line 35: best == "" -> TRUE (but this is the legitimate winning candidate, not "no candidate")
Line 36: returns ("", false)  <- WRONG per documented postcondition
Expected per postcondition: ("", true), since a candidate ("") is within suggestMaxDist.
Predicted wrong output: ("", false). Actual observed output: ("", false). Match.
- **Blast radius:** Only one call site repo-wide: internal/guard/validate.go:89 — `suggestion, _ := Suggest(ref.Name, known)` — discards the bool return entirely, so this specific caller is not currently affected by the ambiguity (it just uses the string as a best-effort hint regardless of the bool). No other caller branches on the bool today (grep for `.Suggest(` found only the definition and this one call site). Risk is latent: Suggest is exported from the guard package, so any future/external caller relying on the documented `(name, true)` postcondition would silently get a false negative for empty-string-shaped candidate sets (e.g., a symbol table that legitimately contains an anonymous/empty-name entry).
- **Fix direction:** Track "found" with an explicit boolean (e.g., `found := false; ... found = true` alongside updating best/bestDist) instead of inferring it from `best == ""`, and return `(best, found)`.

### F104. `internal/ir/generator.go:160` — walkSourceFiles
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** low (matched low-marker: "\blatent\b")
- **Class:** impossible-state
- **Contract violated:** walkSourceFiles doc comment (lines 144-149): 'It skips ignored directories, symlinked directories, and unsupported extensions' — implies a real SkipDir path for symlinked directories, distinct from the file case.
- **Hypothesis:** filepath.Walk builds every FileInfo it passes to the walk callback — both for root and for every directory entry — via os.Lstat (confirmed in Go 1.26.3 stdlib path/filepath/path.go: `os.Lstat(root)` at line 424 for root, `lstat(filename)` at line 364 inside walk() for every child). Lstat never dereferences a symlink, so for any path where info.Mode()&os.ModeSymlink != 0 is true, info.IsDir() is always false — Walk itself never learns whether a symlink points at a directory. So at line 159-164, `if info.Mode()&os.ModeSymlink != 0 { if info.IsDir() { return filepath.SkipDir } return nil }`, the inner `info.IsDir()` on line 160 can never evaluate true; `return filepath.SkipDir` on line 161 is dead code. Every symlink, whether it targets a file or a directory, falls through to `return nil` on line 163. (This happens to still work by accident — walk() at path.go line 345 only recurses into an entry when `info.IsDir()` is true, so a symlinked directory is skipped anyway via the 'not a directory' path, not via SkipDir — but the explicit SkipDir branch that the doc comment implies exists is unreachable, and any future refactor that changes what 'return nil' vs 'return filepath.SkipDir' does (e.g. adding per-entry logic keyed off the return value) will silently never hit the SkipDir arm for symlinked directories.)
- **Trace:** Input: temp dir root/ containing root/target/ (a real dir with target/inside.go) and root/linkToDir -> root/target (a symlink to that directory).
Path: filepath.Walk(root, cb) at generator.go:151 -> internal path/filepath walk() builds FileInfo for "linkToDir" via lstat(filename) (Lstat, never resolves the link) -> cb invoked with that FileInfo at generator.go:151 -> line 159 `info.Mode()&os.ModeSymlink != 0` is true -> line 160 `info.IsDir()` evaluated on the Lstat-built FileInfo.
Predicted wrong (contract-violating) state: line 160 is always false for a symlink, so line 161 `return filepath.SkipDir` never executes; control always falls to line 163 `return nil`.
Executed and observed exactly this: a direct probe walk logged `info.IsDir() = false` for the "linkToDir" entry, and a walk instrumented to record which branch fired recorded the SkipDir branch never firing (only the fallthrough branch fired). Running the real g.walkSourceFiles against this tree produced `visited = map[]` — no file from inside the symlinked directory was indexed, confirming the *external* behavior is unchanged, but purely via the "not a directory, so Walk doesn't recurse" mechanism rather than the SkipDir arm the doc comment describes.
- **Blast radius:** walkSourceFiles has exactly two callers, both in generator.go: Generate/GenerateCtx (line 210) and Update (line 265) — the two entry points every IR-indexing path (CLI `runecho-ir repo reindex`, MCP structure/locate/guard) funnels through. No caller currently depends on the SkipDir vs. nil distinction for symlinks, so today's indexed output is unaffected; the risk is latent, surfacing only if a future refactor keys new behavior off that return-value distinction (e.g. per-entry stats, symlink-cycle detection, or a callback invoked only on SkipDir).
- **Fix direction:** Resolve intent via os.Stat (not Lstat) on the symlink target before branching, e.g. `if target, statErr := os.Stat(path); statErr == nil && target.IsDir() { return filepath.SkipDir }`, so the SkipDir arm becomes reachable and matches the doc comment (and update the comment/tests to lock in the now-real distinction).

### F105. `internal/snapshot/registry.go:373` — ResolveRepo
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** low (matched low-marker: "\blatent\b")
- **Class:** impossible-state
- **Contract violated:** ResolveRepo's own stated invariant (357-362): 'a transient DB error is otherwise indistinguishable from not-enrolled; warn so the fault is debuggable rather than silent.'
- **Hypothesis:** dir is inside a valid git working tree so gitutil.TopLevel(dir) at line 396 succeeds, but gitutil.CommonDir(dir) fails for a reason unrelated to 'not in a git tree' (older git binary lacking --git-common-dir support, or a linked worktree whose .git file points at an unreadable commondir file) -- cdErr != nil while TopLevel's err is nil. The code assumes CommonDir failure and TopLevel failure are the same underlying condition (both meaning 'non-git dir'), so it never logs anything for this case: `if cdErr == nil { ... }` has no else branch, and warnResolve is only invoked for DB errors inside that block. Every call for this repo silently skips tier 1 and never calls db.backfillCommonDir (line 403/414 both gate on cdErr==nil), so common_dir is never populated and the O(1) fast path is permanently disabled with zero diagnostic trace -- contradicting the function's documented goal of always surfacing tier faults via warnResolve.
- **Trace:** Concrete input: dir="." (relative) while cwd is inside a valid, committed git working tree `root`, with `root` enrolled in the DB without common_dir set (simulating a pre-V4 row needing backfill).
Path: registry.go:373 `gitutil.CommonDir(".")` -> gitutil.go:52-54 hard-rejects non-absolute dir -> returns ("", err) so cdErr != nil, a cause wholly unrelated to "not enrolled"/"non-git dir".
-> registry.go:374 `if cdErr == nil` is false -> tier-1 block skipped entirely, no warnResolve call, falls through.
-> registry.go:396 `gitutil.TopLevel(".")` -> gitutil.go:71-77 has no absoluteness guard, runs `git -C . rev-parse --show-toplevel` against the process cwd -> succeeds, returns the absolute root path (proving dir really is inside a valid git tree, so the "not-enrolled" explanation for cdErr is false).
-> registry.go:400 `db.GetRepoByPath(topLevel)` finds the enrolled repo -> registry.go:403 `db.backfillCommonDir(r.ID, commonDir="", cdErr=non-nil)` -> registry.go:425 `if cdErr == nil` is false -> no-op, common_dir stays "".
-> registry.go:404 returns (repo, topLevel, true).
Predicted wrong output: ResolveRepo returns ok=true (correct repo) but (a) zero bytes written to stderr despite a genuine, non-DB, non-"not-enrolled" error occurring, and (b) repo.CommonDir remains "" forever, permanently disabling the tier-1 O(1) fast path for that repo — with no diagnostic trail per the function's own documented invariant (registry.go:358-362).
Expected/contract-correct output per the stated invariant: some diagnostic surfaced (or at minimum a differentiated code path) when cdErr's cause is unrelated to non-enrollment, and/or an opportunistic backfill attempt (e.g. retrying CommonDir against the now-known-absolute topLevel) so the fast path isn't permanently disabled by an artifact of the caller's dir formatting.
- **Blast radius:** grep -rn "ResolveRepo(" (excluding tests) shows 6 call sites, all affected by the permanently-disabled fast path / missing diagnostic: cmd/runecho-ir/helpers.go:44,77,88; cmd/runecho-ir/repo.go:202; cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:139,293,674; cmd/runecho-guard/dangling.go:126. main.go:139 is the guard's primary per-invocation resolve (passes os.Getwd(), normally absolute, so the relative-path trigger is latent there), but any caller that ever passes a non-absolute `dir` (or hits the old-git/unreadable-commondir-file variants named in the hypothesis) silently loses both the fast path and the diagnostic for the life of that DB row.
- **Fix direction:** Add an else branch that calls warnResolve("common-dir", cdErr) whenever cdErr != nil (mirroring the DB-error warn already done for tier 1), and have backfillCommonDir retry gitutil.CommonDir(topLevel) (topLevel is guaranteed absolute) instead of unconditionally no-op'ing on the original cdErr, so a caller-side relative-path/older-git/unusual-worktree cause doesn't permanently disable the O(1) path nor stay silent.

### F107. `cmd/runecho-guard/declog.go:147` — recentAsk
- **Verdict:** ❓ UNVERIFIED (votes: REFUTED) | **Severity:** unknown (no blastRadius text captured)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** recentAsk's documented postcondition says a match is 'the physically last matching line' in the scanned tail region, and its own doc comment for logDecision claims records are 'single-page JSONL' — but nothing in the codebase enforces a size cap on decisionRecord.Symbols (main.go builds `syms` from an unbounded number of violations/dangling/droppedImps/duplicates with no truncation).
- **Hypothesis:** decisions.jsonl contains, within the last maxOutcomeReadBytes (64KiB) tail window, a precommit-mode 'ask' record whose Symbols slice is large enough that its single JSON line exceeds bufio.Scanner's default MaxScanTokenSize (64KB) — plausible from a large staged diff with hundreds of unresolved-symbol violations (main.go:207-235 has no cap on violations count before building `syms`). Later in the same file (closer to EOF), a legitimate small hook-mode 'ask' record for file `foo.go` is appended within maxOutcomeAge. When logOutcomeForFile("foo.go") runs, recentAsk seeks into the tail window and scans forward with `for sc.Scan()` (line 148); when it reaches the oversized line, Scan() fails with bufio.ErrTooLong and returns false, silently ending the loop — the code never calls sc.Err() to distinguish this from a normal EOF. Because the oversized line sits BEFORE the genuine matching ask record in file order, the scan aborts before ever reaching it, so `found` stays false. logOutcomeForFile then returns early: no 'outcome'/'approved' record is appended and recordApprovals never fires, even though the exact byte range the function claims to search does contain a valid, in-window, unexpired matching ask record. The approval is silently and permanently lost for that call, and nothing in the code path treats 'scan aborted early' differently from 'no match found in this window'.
- **Trace:** Setup: decisions.jsonl = 200,000 bytes filler + 370,160-byte oversized "ask" record (file=other.go) + newline + small "ask" record (file=foo.go, Symbols=[Foo]) + newline. Total size = 570,324 bytes.
recentAsk(path, "foo.go") at declog.go:125:
  line 132-136: stat.Size()=570324, offset = 570324-65536 = 504788
  line 140: Seek(504788) — lands inside the oversized line (which spans roughly bytes 200000-570160), NOT at a line boundary
  line 147-148: bufio.NewScanner(f); for sc.Scan() — first Scan() reads from offset 504788 to the next '\n' at ~570160, a fragment of length ~65372 bytes (LESS than 65536, since window is capped) — Scan() succeeds (not ErrTooLong)
  line 150: json.Unmarshal fails on the truncated/corrupt fragment -> continue
  next Scan(): reads the small foo.go line (~200 bytes) -> succeeds
  line 153-163: rec.Decision=="ask", rec.File=="foo.go" match, ts within cutoff -> match=rec, found=true
  line 166: returns (fooRec, true)
Predicted-by-hypothesis output: found=false (approval silently lost).
Actual output: found=true, rec={File:foo.go, Repo:runecho, Symbols:[Foo], ...} — matches expected/correct behavior.

### F108. `cmd/runecho-guard/learnedallow.go:134` — recordApprovals
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** unknown (no blastRadius text captured)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** recordApprovals increments Count by 1 per entry in the `symbols` slice with no internal deduplication, on the documented assumption (per its own contract) that Count represents 'how many times approved' as an approval-EVENT count, i.e. callers are expected to pass de-duplicated symbol lists per call.
- **Hypothesis:** A single MultiEdit in one PreToolUse hook invocation removes both `import cache` (dropped-import, still used unqualified elsewhere in the new text) and a same-named top-level `def cache():` (dangling, still referenced by another file) from the same file. main.go's `syms` (lines 520-552) is a flat concatenation across the four independently-computed lists (violations, dangling, droppedImps, duplicates) with no cross-list dedup, so syms contains "cache" twice. logOutcomeForFile forwards this list unchanged as ask.Symbols to recordApprovals(dir, repo, ["cache","cache",...], now), which increments cache's Count by 2 for one user approval -- reaching the default learnedThreshold()=2 in a single click instead of requiring two separate approval events as the Count/threshold semantics intend.

Expected/correct output per contract (Count = distinct approval events): Count should be 1 after one event; "cache" should NOT be allowed until a second, separate approval.

Actual: ran the real function once with ["cache","cache"] and checked learnedAllowedSet immediately after — "cache" was allowed after the single call.</trace>

### F109. `internal/guard/diff.go:46` — parseDiffOutput
- **Verdict:** ❓ UNVERIFIED (votes: ) | **Severity:** unknown (no blastRadius text captured)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** Doc comment frames only bufio.ErrTooLong as reachable and treats it as a 'preserve partial results' case; it does not document that any other scanner error takes a materially different, harsher policy (discard everything) despite being reachable if the input source ever changes from strings.NewReader.
- **Hypothesis:** If parseDiffOutput's scanner ever surfaces a non-ErrTooLong error (e.g. io.ErrUnexpectedEOF) after 3 files have already been fully and correctly parsed into result, the function returns (nil, false, err) — discarding those 3 valid FileDiff entries — instead of returning (result, false, err) the way the ErrTooLong branch preserves already-parsed diffs (result, true, nil) for the same 'error mid-stream' scenario. Callers lose already-correct guard data for files that parsed fine before the error, inconsistent with the ErrTooLong branch's partial-result policy.

### F110. `internal/guard/diff.go:58` — parseDiffOutput
- **Verdict:** ❓ UNVERIFIED (votes: ) | **Severity:** unknown (no blastRadius text captured)
- **Class:** impossible-state
- **Contract violated:** parseDiffOutput's postcondition that AddedLines carry correct 1-indexed new-file line numbers, and parseDiffNewPath's premise that a '+++ ' prefix on a scanned line always signals a genuine unified-diff file-boundary header
- **Hypothesis:** Stage a file whose added text is literally `++ i;` (legal prefix-increment syntax in C/C++/Java/JS) or any line starting with two plus signs and a space (e.g. markdown/doc content quoting a diff snippet, or editing this very diff.go's own comments which contain 'b/<path>' examples). git emits this as the raw scanned line '+++ i;' (diff marker '+' followed by content '++ i;'). The unconditional check `strings.HasPrefix(line, "+++ ")` at line 58 fires on this genuine ADDED content line exactly as it would on a real '+++ b/path' header, before the cur==nil guard and regardless of whether a file is already mid-hunk. parseDiffNewPath then either (a) fails the 'b/' check and returns ok=false, setting cur=nil (line 66) — silently truncating ALL remaining added lines of the real current file from AddedLines from that point forward, with no partial/error signal to the caller (unlike the documented bufio.ErrTooLong path) — or (b) if the trailing content happens to start with 'b/' (e.g. an added line whose text is '++ b/foo'), succeeds and appends a bogus new FileDiff{Path:"foo"} (line 60), silently misattributing every subsequent added line in the hunk to that phantom path instead of the real file. Either way runecho-guard (the sole caller, cmd/runecho-guard/main.go:180) receives an incomplete/misattributed diffs slice and can approve a commit containing an actual hallucinated symbol that sat after the '++ ' line, with none of the existing safety signals (partial=true, non-nil err) ever set — this is not caught by FuzzGuardDiff, which only asserts no panic and UTF-8 validity, never LineNo/Path correctness.

### F111. `internal/guard/diff.go:84` — parseHunkStart
- **Verdict:** ❓ UNVERIFIED (votes: ) | **Severity:** unknown (no blastRadius text captured)
- **Class:** impossible-state
- **Contract violated:** extract.go:208, extract.go:437, and dropped_import.go:112 all use `l.LineNo != prevNo+1` as the deliberate signal that a new AddedLine belongs to a different hunk (to reset multi-line parse state such as inPyParen / an 'open' bracket flag / a pending-use tracker), which is only a valid signal if AddedLine.LineNo values are the true, monotonically-correct new-file positions that parseHunkStart is contracted to produce.
- **Hypothesis:** If a file's staged diff contains a hunk whose header parseHunkStart mis-parses to the silent-1 fallback, and that hunk's forced LineNo=1 happens to equal prevNo+1 from the immediately preceding AddedLine (e.g. the previous hunk's last added line has LineNo 0 from another degenerate/zero-count hunk, or is itself the first hunk in the file so the i>0 guard doesn't even apply), the contiguity check in ExtractImports/ExtractRefs fails to detect the hunk boundary and leaves multi-line parser state (e.g. `inPyParen` in ExtractImports) set across the boundary, causing the first line(s) of the new hunk to be misclassified as a continuation of a multi-line Python `from M import (...)` statement from the prior, unrelated hunk — extracting bogus import/def/ref names or dropping real ones, silently corrupting guard.Run's known-symbol set for that file rather than raising any error.

### F112. `internal/guard/diff.go:94` — parseDiffOutput
- **Verdict:** ❓ UNVERIFIED (votes: ) | **Severity:** unknown (no blastRadius text captured)
- **Class:** impossible-state
- **Contract violated:** parseDiffOutput's documented postcondition that every FileDiff.AddedLines[i].LineNo is 'set to the correct 1-indexed new-file line number'
- **Hypothesis:** Feed parseDiffOutput a raw string where a real file boundary is set ('+++ b/x.go', which resets newLineNo to 0 at line 62) but the following line is an added line ('+foo') with no intervening '@@ ...' hunk header ever having been seen for that file (reachable via any caller of the exported-for-testing parseDiffOutput with hand-built/fuzzed input, and via the fuzz corpus's own malformed-header seeds like '@@ malformed +-5 @@' which never call parseHunkStart because HasPrefix(line,"@@ ") still matches but strconv.Atoi fails inside parseHunkStart and falls back to 1 — a related but distinct case; the pure zero-hunk case is '+++ b/x.go\n+foo\n' with no '@@' line at all). The code treats newLineNo==0 as always a valid, header-set counter (invariant claims 'always reset...and overwritten by parseHunkStart's return at each hunk header'), but nothing enforces that a hunk header always precedes an added line for a given file — so the first AddedLine gets LineNo=0, a value that violates the 1-indexed contract and that every downstream consumer (guard.Run / violation reporting at cmd/runecho-guard/main.go's `%s:%d:` format) implicitly assumes can't occur, producing a violation reported at line 0 instead of a real source line.

### F113. `internal/ir/generator.go:221` — GenerateCtx
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** unknown (no blastRadius text captured)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** GenerateCtx postcondition: 'result.Files has one entry per supported file under rootPath that was both encountered before the file cap was reached and parsed without error' — two distinct, successfully-parsed supported files collapse into one entry with zero error/warning trail.
- **Hypothesis:** rootPath contains two distinct, simultaneously-existing files whose names are Unicode-canonically-equivalent but byte-distinct, e.g. 'café.go' (NFD: e + combining acute U+0301) and 'café.go' (NFC: precomposed é) — both valid, separate directory entries on a Linux filesystem (ext4 is byte-oriented and does not canonicalize names). walkSourceFiles visits both as separate supported .go files: stats.SupportedSeen becomes 2, and normalizePath's NFC pass (line 394) canonicalizes both relative paths to the identical string 'café.go'. Line 221's `result.Files[normPath] = fileIR` then executes twice with the same key inside the same walk — the second parseFile result silently overwrites the first, with no key-existence check. GenerateCtx returns success with stats.Indexed=1, stats.ParseErrors=0, stats.SupportedSeen=2: one of the two real, successfully-parsed files has its entire Symbols/Refs permanently discarded from the IR, and Stats gives the caller no signal that a collision (versus a legitimate parse failure) occurred — Coverage() reports 50% with ParseErrors=0, which the 'honest-coverage counters' doc (lines 78-83) has no vocabulary to explain. The identical overwrite exists at UpdateCtx line 295 (and the hash-reuse copy at line 286), so an Update run has the same silent-collapse behavior.
- **Trace:** Read code at internal/ir/generator.go:

- line 210: g.walkSourceFiles(ctx, absRoot, func(absPath, normPath string) error { ... })
- walkSourceFiles (line 150-181), line 174: relPath, _ := filepath.Rel(absRoot, path) — relPath is the raw OS-level byte-distinct name (e.g. "café.go" vs "café.go")
- line 179: return fn(path, normalizePath(relPath)) — normalizePath (line 380-397), line 394: normalized = norm.NFC.String(normalized) — both raw names canonicalize to the identical NFC string "café.go"

- line 228: stats.Indexed = len(result.Files) = 1

  "café.go" (NFD) with `package x\n\nfunc FromNFD() {}\n`
  "café.go"  (NFC) with `package x\n\nfunc FromNFC() {}\n`

### F114. `internal/ir/generator.go:330` — UpdateFile
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** unknown (no blastRadius text captured)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** The outside-repo containment check assumes rootPath and filePath, once each run through filepath.Abs/Clean, share a common lexical prefix whenever filePath genuinely lives inside rootPath. Neither filepath.Abs nor filepath.Clean resolves symlinks (no EvalSymlinks call), so this only holds when both inputs were derived through the same symlink-resolution policy.
- **Hypothesis:** UpdateFile's sole production caller (cmd/runecho-guard/main.go refreshIRForFile, line 337) passes rootPath=srcRoot derived from `git rev-parse --show-toplevel` (git resolves symlinks in its output) and filePath taken verbatim from an edit-tool hook payload. If the project is reached through a symlinked path (e.g. a convenience symlink or a worktree checkout accessed via a linked directory), srcRoot ends up fully resolved while filePath still contains the symlink segment. filepath.Rel(absRoot, absFile) then computes a path starting with '../' for a file that is actually inside the repo, tripping the line 330 guard and returning (existing, false, nil) — the auto-fresh IR hook silently and permanently skips indexing every edit made through that symlinked path, with no error or log to reveal why the IR never updates.
- **Trace:** Input: realrepo=/tmp/.../001/realrepo containing foo.go (bootstrapped into `existing` IR via g.Generate(realrepo)); file edited on disk; caller invokes g.UpdateFile(existing, resolvedRoot, editedPathViaSymlink) where resolvedRoot=/tmp/.../001/realrepo (post EvalSymlinks) and editedPathViaSymlink=/tmp/.../001/link/foo.go (via a symlink 'link' -> 'realrepo', unresolved).

Path: generator.go:320 absRoot=filepath.Abs(rootPath)="/tmp/.../001/realrepo" -> :324 Clean (no-op) -> :325 absFile=filepath.Abs(filePath)="/tmp/.../001/link/foo.go" (Abs does NOT resolve symlinks) -> :329 rel=filepath.Rel(absRoot, absFile) lexically computes "../link/foo.go" (siblings 'realrepo' and 'link' under the same parent, no shared prefix beyond the parent) -> :330 strings.HasPrefix(rel, "../") is true -> guard fires -> :331 return existing, false, nil.

Predicted wrong output: changed=false, err=nil, returned IR pointer == existing (i.e., a total no-op, indistinguishable from "file legitimately outside repo" or "nothing changed"), even though foo.go is genuinely inside the repo and was just edited.
Expected correct output: changed=true (or at least a re-parsed entry), since the file's content actually changed and it lives inside the repo.

Observed actual output (executed): "UpdateFile: changed=false err=<nil> updated==existing(ptr):true" — exactly the predicted wrong output.</trace>

### F115. `internal/parser/python.go:157` — pyImportsAndExports
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** unknown (no blastRadius text captured)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** pyImportsAndExports's postcondition assumes hasAll==true only occurs for a genuine __all__ *assignment* (so exports staying empty under hasAll==true is limited to the documented 'explicit empty __all__=[]' or 'multi-line content pyAllRegex can't bridge' cases). pyAllPresentRegex (line 48: `(?m)^\s*__all__\s*(?::[^=\n]*)?\+?=`) has no `[^=]` guard after its final `=`, unlike pyConstRegex (line 56) which explicitly adds `[^=]` to reject `==` comparisons. So a line like `__all__ == ['a', 'b']` (a no-op comparison statement, not an assignment — e.g. a `=`/`==` typo) satisfies pyAllPresentRegex (matches the first `=` of `==`) and sets hasAll=true, while pyAllRegex (line 35, which requires `\+?=\s*[\[\(]` — an `=` immediately followed by whitespace then a bracket) fails to match at all because the second `=` sits between them, so exports stays completely empty.
- **Hypothesis:** For a file containing `__all__ == ['a', 'b']` followed by `def public_fn():\n    pass`, pyImportsAndExports returns (hasAll=true, exports=[]) — verified directly by executing pyImportsAndExports on this exact source. In Parse (line 105), `!hasAll` is false, so pyFallbackExports is never called, leaving FileStructure.Exports == [] even though public_fn is a legitimate no-underscore top-level function that the no-__all__ convention would otherwise surface. The code assumes 'pyAllPresentRegex matched' implies 'a real __all__ declaration exists that intentionally curates the export surface,' but a stray comparison (typo'd `==` instead of `=`) reaches the same hasAll==true state while contributing zero real exports, silently dropping the entire module's export surface instead of falling back.
- **Trace:** Input source:
```
__all__ == ['a', 'b']

def public_fn():
    pass
```
Path: pyImportsAndExports (python.go:131) is called from PythonParser.Parse (python.go:97).
- Line 152-156: `pyAllRegex.FindAllStringSubmatch(source, -1)` — pyAllRegex = `__all__\s*\+?=\s*[\[\(]([^\]\)]+)[\]\)]` (python.go:35). After matching literal `__all__` and the following space, the pattern requires `\+?=` then `\s*[\[\(`. The very next character is the *first* `=` of `==`; matching it consumes that `=`, leaving the *second* `=` where `\s*[\[\(]` expects whitespace-then-bracket — the second `=` satisfies neither, so the whole match attempt fails at this position and there is no other `__all__` occurrence to retry. Result: zero matches → exports stays nil.
- Line 157: `pyAllPresentRegex.MatchString(source)` — pyAllPresentRegex = `(?m)^\s*__all__\s*(?::[^=\n]*)?\+?=` (python.go:48) has no `[^=]` guard after its trailing `=` (unlike pyConstRegex at line 56). It matches `__all__ =` by consuming only the *first* `=` of `==` and stops there (the regex is satisfied as soon as it sees one `=`, it doesn't care what follows) → returns hasAll=true.
- Back in Parse (python.go:105): `if !hasAll { exports = pyFallbackExports(...) }` — hasAll is true, so this branch is skipped; the no-underscore fallback (which would have surfaced `public_fn`) never runs.
- Result: FileStructure.Exports == [] even though `public_fn` is a legitimate no-underscore top-level function.

Predicted wrong output: hasAll=true, exports=[], FileStructure.Exports=[] (public_fn missing).
Expected/correct output (if the typo were treated as "no real __all__"): fallback should run and FileStructure.Exports should contain ["public_fn"].
Observed: matches the predicted wrong output exactly.</trace>
<evidence>Command:

package parser

func TestFocusReproAllTypoEquals(t *testing.T) {

	imports, exports, hasAll := pyImportsAndExports(src)
	t.Logf("imports=%v exports=%v hasAll=%v", imports, exports, hasAll)

	p := NewPythonParser()

	if err != nil {
		t.Fatalf("Parse error: %v", err)
	}

		t.Logf("CONFIRMED: hasAll=true, exports empty, FileStructure.Exports empty despite public_fn present")

		t.Logf("NOT REPRODUCED: hasAll=%v exports=%v fsExports=%v", hasAll, exports, fs.Exports)

Any real-world .py file containing a `__all__ ==` typo (or other accidental double-equals on that line) would have its entire export surface silently reported as empty instead of falling back to the no-underscore convention — a false "no exports" signal repo-wide for that file, not just a missed name.</blastRadius>

### F116. `internal/snapshot/diff.go:39` — Churn (internal/snapshot/churn.go), consuming computeDiff via db.Diff
- **Verdict:** ❓ UNVERIFIED (votes: ) | **Severity:** unknown (no blastRadius text captured)
- **Class:** unhandled-postcondition
- **Contract violated:** Same computeDiff postcondition as above: a both-sides-present symbol with exactly one empty Hash is dropped from Added/Removed/Modified.
- **Hypothesis:** Given two consecutive snapshots metas[i] and metas[i+1] where metas[i]'s stored sig_hash for a symbol is "" (parser didn't populate it, e.g. a kind/language where hashing isn't implemented) and metas[i+1]'s sig_hash for the same symbol is non-empty because the symbol's body changed, Churn()'s loop at churn.go:34-55 only increments symbolChanges via fd.Added/fd.Removed/fd.Modified. The symbol is silently dropped by computeDiff (present both sides, hash-empty guard fails), so Churn() never increments its churn counter for that diff step, and FormatChurn/ChurnPayload under-report that symbol's actual change frequency — a symbol that changed every diff in the window could show 0 churn if its baseline hash is consistently empty on one side of each pairwise diff.

### F117. `internal/snapshot/diff.go:51` — Churn (internal/snapshot/churn.go:11), consuming computeDiff output via db.Diff
- **Verdict:** ❓ UNVERIFIED (votes: ) | **Severity:** unknown (no blastRadius text captured)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** Same computeDiff postcondition as above: fd.Modified excludes any symbol whose Hash is empty on either side (diff.go:135-138), which includes every export/import/import_name/export_wildcard-kind symbol by construction (ir/storage.go Symbol.Hash doc).
- **Hypothesis:** Across a sequence of snapshots where only a file's top-level export/import list changes repeatedly (function bodies untouched), fd.Modified is empty for every one of those diffs (the changed symbols are hash-less import/export kinds), so the loop at churn.go:51-54 never increments symbolChanges for them. The resulting ChurnReport.Symbols list (and 'hot symbols' section of FormatChurn/ChurnPayload) reports zero churn for a symbol that in fact changed in every single diff in the window, understating `runecho-ir churn`'s hot-symbol output for any codebase whose churn is concentrated in import/export edits rather than function bodies.

### F118. `internal/snapshot/diff.go:149` — computeDiff
- **Verdict:** ❓ UNVERIFIED (votes: ) | **Severity:** unknown (no blastRadius text captured)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** computeDiff's docstring/comment context (echoed in DiffPayload's comment: 'a machine consumer... sees identical output regardless of entry point — they cannot drift') implies the diff is reproducible/deterministic for identical inputs (Files ordering is explicitly made deterministic via sort.Strings over paths at line 93).
- **Hypothesis:** Given two snapshots where the same file has two symbols both newly added in B with identical Name but different Kind (e.g. Kind="type",Name="Server" and Kind="func",Name="Server"), fd.Added is built by ranging over the Go map bSymSet (line 129, iteration order randomized per run) and then sorted only by sym.Name via the non-stable sort.Slice (line 149) — since both share Name="Server", sort.Slice may leave them in either relative order. Two separate invocations of computeDiff on the exact same two snapshots can therefore emit fd.Added as [{type,Server},{func,Server}] in one run and [{func,Server},{type,Server}] in another, so FormatCompact/FormatFull/DiffPayload output differs byte-for-byte across runs for identical input, when the correct behavior (implied by the reproducible/comparable-diff intent) is identical output every time — e.g. a Modified/Added tie-break should also key on Kind (or use a stable sort), not Name alone.

### F119. `internal/snapshot/diff.go:151` — changedSymbols (cmd/runecho-ir/mapcmd.go), consuming computeDiff via db.DiffLive
- **Verdict:** ❓ UNVERIFIED (votes: ) | **Severity:** unknown (no blastRadius text captured)
- **Class:** unhandled-postcondition
- **Contract violated:** computeDiff's documented postcondition: a symbol present in both aSymSet and bSymSet where exactly one side's Hash=="" is placed in none of Added/Removed/Modified and is silently dropped from the diff.
- **Hypothesis:** Given a baseline snapshot where some SymbolDelta.Hash=="" (storage.go:36 documents Hash is empty unless the parser populates it — a real, current-code state, not just legacy data) and a live IR where the same symbol now has a non-empty Hash after its body actually changed, changedSymbols() at mapcmd.go:151 calls db.DiffLive, then only walks res.Files[].Added and res.Files[].Modified (lines ~160-163) to build the 'changed' set consumed by `runecho-ir map --since=<label>`. Because the symbol exists in both aSymSet and bSymSet (so it's not Added or Removed) and the hash-empty guard at diff.go:135 prevents it from being classified Modified, it never appears in fd.Added or fd.Modified. changedSymbols() therefore omits this genuinely-changed symbol from the returned map, so `runecho-ir map --since=X` prints it as unchanged (or omits it under --since filtering) even though its body hash changed between baseline and live.

### F120. `internal/snapshot/diff.go:166` — changedSymbols (cmd/runecho-ir/mapcmd.go:130), calling computeDiff via db.DiffLive
- **Verdict:** ❓ UNVERIFIED (votes: ) | **Severity:** unknown (no blastRadius text captured)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** computeDiff postcondition (diff.go:135-138): Modified is populated ONLY when both aSym.Hash and sym.Hash are non-empty; a symbol with an empty hash on either side can never appear in Modified. Per ir/storage.go Symbol.Hash doc, Hash is 'empty unless the parser isolated a body' -- export/import/import_name/export_wildcard-kind symbols never carry a hash.
- **Hypothesis:** For a file where an existing import statement's target changes (e.g. `from pkg import Foo` -> a different re-export path) but the bound name 'Foo' and its Kind 'import_name' are unchanged between the --since baseline snapshot and the live IR, both aSym.Hash and sym.Hash are '' (imports are never hashed), so computeDiff's switch at diff.go:129-141 falls through both the !exists and hash-mismatch branches and reports neither Added nor Modified for that symbol. `changedSymbols` at mapcmd.go:165-168 only calls mark(fd.Path, fd.Added) and mark(fd.Path, fd.Modified), so this genuinely-changed import is never inserted into the returned `changed` map, even though the function's own doc comment (mapcmd.go:128-129) promises 'every symbol the live IR added or modified' -- `runecho-ir map --since <label>` then renders that file's changed-import symbol as unchanged (silently omitted from the highlighted set) despite the source line differing between snapshots.

### F121. `internal/snapshot/diff.go:170` — symbolSet
- **Verdict:** ❓ UNVERIFIED (votes: ) | **Severity:** unknown (no blastRadius text captured)
- **Class:** impossible-state
- **Contract violated:** computeDiff precondition: "Within a single file+snapshot, Kind+':'+Name...is assumed to uniquely identify a symbol" and postcondition: "Added/Removed are exact key-set differences of aSymSet/bSymSet"
- **Hypothesis:** A Python file with a try/except ImportError fallback (e.g. `try:\n    from ujson import loads\nexcept ImportError:\n    from json import loads`) produces TWO Symbol{Kind:"import_name",Name:"loads"} entries in the IR for that file: internal/ir/generator.go's symbolsFromStructure (line 496) calls add(importedNames(path, src), "import_name") directly on guard.ExtractImports' raw, unsorted, undeduplicated output -- unlike Functions/Classes/Exports/Imports, which each parser sorts+dedupes before generator.go ever sees them (internal/parser/go.go:115-118,130-133; internal/parser/js.go:202-213). Both duplicate entries carry Hash="" (import_name is never hashed) and different Line values, and both survive unchanged into storage (loadSymbolsBySnapshot/irToMaps just mirror FileIR.Symbols). When computeDiff's symbolSet(aSymbols[path]) runs (diff.go:170), `m[s.Kind+":"+s.Name] = s` collapses both "import_name:loads" entries into ONE map entry (last one wins). If snapshot B deletes the whole fallback block (both import lines gone), the removed-loop at diff.go:143-148 sees exactly one aSymSet key ("import_name:loads") missing from bSymSet, so fd.Removed gets exactly 1 entry and TotalRemoved is incremented by 1 -- even though two independent import bindings actually existed and were both removed. FormatCompact/FormatFull then print "-1 symbol" (and list only one Removed name) when the true removed count is 2, silently under-reporting the diff for any file where the same import name is bound by more than one import statement.

### F122. `internal/snapshot/diff.go:211` — DiffPayload
- **Verdict:** ❓ UNVERIFIED (votes: ) | **Severity:** unknown (no blastRadius text captured)
- **Class:** impossible-state
- **Contract violated:** DiffPayload's own doc comment (203-206, 208-210) asserts a load-bearing machine-consumer contract: 'a zero-drift diff marshals "files": [] rather than "files": null... an array consumer must never have to null-guard.' The nil-guard at 211-214 only normalizes the top-level d.Files slice.
- **Hypothesis:** Any FileDiff whose Status is 'modified' but which has zero symbol-level changes reaches this state with fd.Added, fd.Removed, and fd.Modified all left at their zero value (nil slice) — e.g. a tracked file with no parseable symbols (a .go file with only package/import decls, or any non-code file runecho still hashes) whose content hash changed between snapshot A and B. computeDiff builds such a FileDiff via the composite literal at lines 118-123 (no Added/Removed/Modified field set) and neither of the two symbol-diff loops (129-141, 143-148) appends anything because aSymSet and bSymSet are both empty maps. That FileDiff is appended to d.Files (153) and reaches DiffPayload unmodified. json.Marshal(DiffPayload(d)) then produces `"files": [{"Path":"pkg/const.go","Status":"modified",...,"Added":null,"Removed":null,"Modified":null}]` — the exact null-array shape the function's own comment says a machine consumer (the CLI --json flag / MCP diff oracle / harness gate) should never have to null-guard against, because only the outer Files slice got the nil->[]FileDiff{} treatment, not the three nested slices inside each element.

### F123. `internal/snapshot/registry.go:156` — RemoveRepo
- **Verdict:** ✅ CONFIRMED (votes: CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED/CONFIRMED) | **Severity:** unknown (no blastRadius text captured)
- **Class:** impossible-state
- **Contract violated:** RemoveRepo's postcondition is documented and tested as the 'refuse to delete if snapshots exist' safety check, positioned in the contract as the intentional protective counterpart to PurgeRepo's unconditional delete — implying it is the function CLI callers should reach for when a safe/reversible remove is wanted.
- **Hypothesis:** cmd/runecho-ir/repo.go's `runecho-ir repo rm <name>` command (runRepoRemove, repo.go:144-167) never calls db.RemoveRepo at all — it calls db.PurgeRepo(repo.ID) unconditionally (repo.go:162). Grepping the whole repo for RemoveRepo shows zero non-test call sites. A user who has snapshots and runs `runecho-ir repo rm <name>` expecting the documented safety behavior (refuse-if-has-snapshots) instead gets an unconditional, irreversible purge of all refs/symbols/files/snapshots/repo rows — the protective function exists and is unit-tested but is unreachable from any CLI surface, so no user input ever benefits from its guard.
- **Trace:** Input: enroll a git repo via `runecho-ir repo add --name=focusrepo --no-hooks <path>` (auto-reindexes, creating snapshot id=1 with 1 file) → then run `runecho-ir repo rm focusrepo`.
Path: main.go run() -> runRepo(["rm","focusrepo"]) [repo.go:16] -> case "rm": runRepoRemove(["focusrepo"]) [repo.go:27] -> db.GetRepoByName("focusrepo") finds repo id=1 [repo.go:154] -> db.PurgeRepo(1) [repo.go:162] -> registry.go:177 unconditionally executes 5 DELETE statements (refs, symbols, files, snapshots, repos) in one transaction, no snapshot-count check anywhere in this path -> repo.go:165 prints "Removed focusrepo (id=1) and its history." and returns 0.
Predicted wrong output (per documented contract, which frames RemoveRepo as the safety counterpart CLI users would expect for `repo rm`): refusal, e.g. an error like "repo 1 has 1 snapshot(s); use PurgeRepo to delete them along with the repo", exit code ExitError, repo/snapshot data preserved.
Actual output observed: exit code 0, stdout "Removed focusrepo (id=1) and its history.", and a follow-up `db.GetRepoByName("focusrepo")` after the command returned nil (repo gone) — i.e. full irreversible purge occurred silently despite a pre-existing snapshot, with no refusal ever raised.
Sanity control run in the same test: calling `db.RemoveRepo(1)` directly (simulating what the doc implies the CLI should use) on the same DB state (repo id=1, 1 snapshot) correctly returned the error "repo 1 has 1 snapshot(s); use PurgeRepo to delete them along with the repo" — proving RemoveRepo's guard logic itself works fine; it is simply never invoked by any CLI/non-test code path.</trace>
<evidence>Command: `go test ./cmd/runecho-ir/... -run TestFocusRepro_RepoRm_BypassesRemoveRepoSafety -v` (scratch file cmd/runecho-ir/zzfocus_repro_test.go, deleted after run; git status clean afterward).

### F124. `internal/snapshot/snapshot.go:78` — writeSnapshotTx
- **Verdict:** ❓ UNVERIFIED (votes: ) | **Severity:** unknown (no blastRadius text captured)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** Postcondition states: 'On any Exec/Prepare/Scan failure at any stage, returns (0, wrapped error) immediately' — implying every failure mode surfaces as an error return, matching the pattern of all other branches in this function (each of which does `if err != nil { return 0, fmt.Errorf(...) }`).
- **Hypothesis:** Call writeSnapshotTx(tx, repoID, sessionID, label, root, nil) (reachable if SaveSnapshot or RollAutoSnapshot is ever invoked with a nil *ir.IR, e.g. an upstream indexing failure that produces no ir.IR but the caller doesn't explicitly nil-check before calling). Expected per the function's own stated error-return convention: (0, error) such as 'insert snapshot: irData is nil' or similar. Actual: line 78's `irData.RootHash` dereferences a nil pointer unconditionally, so the function panics instead of returning an error — crashing the whole process (or, if recovered by a caller-level defer, skipping the deferred tx.Rollback() semantics tests may assume) rather than cleanly failing the transaction the way every other malformed-input path here does.

### F125. `internal/snapshot/snapshot.go:78` — writeSnapshotTx
- **Verdict:** ❓ UNVERIFIED (votes: ) | **Severity:** unknown (no blastRadius text captured)
- **Class:** impossible-state
- **Contract violated:** precondition: irData must be non-nil
- **Hypothesis:** writeSnapshotTx(tx, repoID, sessionID, label, root, nil) — reachable if any caller of SaveSnapshot/RollAutoSnapshot forwards a nil *ir.IR (e.g. a future call site that races past a build-error check, or misreads a (nil, nil-error) return from an IR builder) — dereferences irData.RootHash unconditionally on line 78 and then ranges irData.Files on line 89, panicking with a nil-pointer dereference instead of returning (0, err) like every other failure branch in this function (Prepare/Exec/Scan errors all return a clean error). The panic unwinds through SaveSnapshot/RollAutoSnapshot's deferred tx.Rollback() (so the DB itself stays consistent) but is never recovered, so it crashes the calling goroutine/process rather than surfacing as an error — a much worse failure mode than the one every sibling branch in this file is designed to produce.

### F126. `internal/snapshot/snapshot.go:101` — checkDuplicateDefs
- **Verdict:** ❓ UNVERIFIED (votes: ) | **Severity:** unknown (no blastRadius text captured)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** DefsOfName's documented postcondition scopes matches to kind IN ('function','class') only, deliberately excluding kind='export' rows; checkDuplicateDefs's caller-side extraction (defSet/ExtractDefs via rePyConstDef in internal/guard/extract.go) treats Python module-level UPPER_CASE constants as legitimate 'added defs' worth duplicate-checking, but those constants are stored in the snapshot symbols table under kind='export' (internal/parser/python.go pyFallbackExports -> FileStructure.Exports), not 'function'/'class'.
- **Hypothesis:** Editing a Python file to add a module-level constant `MAX_RETRIES = 3` when another already-indexed file in the same repo already defines `MAX_RETRIES = 5` at module level, with RUNECHO_GUARD_DUPLICATE=1 set: addedDefs (duplicate.go) extracts "MAX_RETRIES" via rePyConstDef and calls db.DefsOfName(snapID, "MAX_RETRIES") at duplicate.go:101; DefsOfName's kind filter excludes the pre-existing constant's export-kind row, returns an empty path list, so checkDuplicateDefs emits zero warnings — the genuine duplicate constant is silently never flagged, even though the function's own doc comment claims it warns whenever 'an edit introduces a NEW symbol definition ... whose name is already defined in a DIFFERENT file'.

### F127. `internal/snapshot/snapshot.go:156` — GetLatestByLabel
- **Verdict:** ❓ UNVERIFIED (votes: ) | **Severity:** unknown (no blastRadius text captured)
- **Class:** assumption-mismatch
- **Contract violated:** GetLatestByLabel (and the identical ORDER BY in GetLatestByLabelSession line 174 and List line 279) assumes wall-clock timestamp order and autoincrement insertion order (id) are always concordant, using timestamp as the PRIMARY sort key and id only as a tiebreaker for equal timestamps.
- **Hypothesis:** Two writeSnapshotTx inserts straddle a backward system clock correction (WSL2 clock drift after host suspend/resume, or an NTP step) — the second insert gets a higher autoincrement id but a lexicographically SMALLER RFC3339 timestamp string than the first. `ORDER BY s.timestamp DESC, s.id DESC LIMIT 1` then ranks the earlier, lower-id row first because timestamp is compared before id, so GetLatestByLabel/GetLatestByLabelSession/List return the stale (older-by-insertion) snapshot as 'latest' while the true latest snapshot exists in the table but is never selected — the E6 guard's freshness baseline and `diff --since=<label>` silently compare against outdated history.

### F128. `internal/snapshot/snapshot.go:280` — List
- **Verdict:** ❓ UNVERIFIED (votes: ) | **Severity:** unknown (no blastRadius text captured)
- **Class:** unhandled-postcondition
- **Contract violated:** List's doc says it 'returns the n most recent snapshots for repoID' — it implicitly assumes n is a positive count, but nothing validates that before the value reaches `LIMIT ?`.
- **Hypothesis:** Caller passes n=0 (e.g. cmd/runecho-ir/inspect.go's `runLog` with `-n=0`, or Churn(repoID, 0)): SQLite executes `LIMIT 0` and returns zero rows even though the repo has snapshots, so runLog prints an empty/'no snapshots' result for a repo with real history. Separately, n=-1 (a decremented/miscalculated counter, or a user passing a negative flag value) makes SQLite treat the negative LIMIT as unbounded per SQLite's documented LIMIT semantics, so List silently returns the ENTIRE snapshot history instead of a bounded window — Churn(repoID, n) then builds an O(all-history) diff chain instead of the intended fixed-size window, contradicting its own 'churn across the last n snapshots' contract.

### F129. `internal/snapshot/snapshot.go:281` — List
- **Verdict:** ❓ UNVERIFIED (votes: ) | **Severity:** unknown (no blastRadius text captured)
- **Class:** impossible-state
- **Contract violated:** implicit assumption that n only bounds the result set from above (0..n rows)
- **Hypothesis:** List(repoID, -1) — reachable via `runecho-ir log -n -1` (cmd/runecho-ir/inspect.go's `n := fs.Int("n", 10, ...)` flag has no lower-bound validation before being passed straight into db.List(repoID, *n)) — binds -1 into `LIMIT ?` in the query at line 281. SQLite's LIMIT clause treats a negative bound as 'no limit' rather than 'zero rows' or an error, so runLog silently dumps the repo's ENTIRE snapshot history for any negative -n input instead of erroring or returning nothing, a state the code never anticipates because n is implicitly assumed to always be a non-negative cap.
